b'ON TENNIS'
b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'Not much head scratching is required when it comes to deciding how to start a wish list for tennis in 2019.'
b'A sport that has long been concerned about punching below its weight spent too much of last year elbowing itself in the ribs as its too-numerous leaders traded blows and crossed purposes.'
b'This is no way to run a niche sport concerned about market and mind share in a ruthlessly competitive global entertainment landscape. Improvement is all the more urgent with tennis\xe2\x80\x99s biggest stars, Roger Federer and Serena Williams, both 37.'
b'And so with a new season about to get serious with the start of the Australian Open on Monday, my No. 1 wish for tennis is unity. In an ideal world, that would mean unified governance.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt will never happen, but what we need more than anything is a commissioner,\xe2\x80\x9d said Brad Gilbert, the longtime player, coach and analyst.'
b'That would require each of tennis\xe2\x80\x99s seven governing bodies to cede some of its authority, a situation that would probably require an existential threat to the game\xe2\x80\x99s viability or profitability.'
b'In an imperfect but still better world, unity could also mean a genuine players\xe2\x80\x99 union \xe2\x80\x94 why not men and women together while we\xe2\x80\x99re wishing? \xe2\x80\x94 that could make for more meaningful progress on tennis\xe2\x80\x99s now-intractable issues through tough negotiations with those who own and operate the tournaments.'
b'In the current system, the players and regular tour events are in partnership, an unusual arrangement in professional sports that can make consensus and change difficult.'
b'Novak Djokovic, back at No. 1 and president of the ATP Player Council, has explored the concept. But for now, a union appears to be wishful thinking: too many legal and logistical hurdles.'
b'But the sport can still do better at finding common ground in 2019.'
b'Start with agreeing on a more coherent schedule that does not include three men\xe2\x80\x99s team events within less than four months: the Laver Cup in September 2019, the revamped Davis Cup in November 2019 and the revived ATP Cup in January 2020.'
b'Continue by creating a meaningful mixed men\xe2\x80\x99s and women\xe2\x80\x99s team event that will carry on the legacy of the Hopman Cup. Further embrace tennis\xe2\x80\x99s ability to showcase men\xe2\x80\x99s and women\xe2\x80\x99s stars in the same events \xe2\x80\x94 a longtime strength that other sports are interested in replicating.'
b'Reach an agreement on coaching that will apply to all sectors of the pro game. The women\xe2\x80\x99s tour currently allows on-court coaching visits once a set while the men\xe2\x80\x99s tour and main-draw Grand Slam events do not allow any coaching during play.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf we have it, we should have it nonstop,\xe2\x80\x9d said Simona Halep, the women\xe2\x80\x99s No. 1. \xe2\x80\x9cIf we don\xe2\x80\x99t, we should stop completely.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Halep prefers letting players solve their own tactical and psychological issues under pressure, as do I and plenty of others. But the existing coaching situation is confusing to fans and disorienting to women\xe2\x80\x99s players, who have to change routines in the tournaments that matter most. In light of the difficulty for umpires to fully police player-coach communication, perhaps allowing signals from the box and only the box is the right compromise.'
b'More tennis wishes for 2019:'
b'ELIMINATE LETS ON SERVES A point or a tournament can already end with a net-cord winner during a rally when a groundstroke, volley or overhead hits the tape and trickles over. Why should a serve be treated any differently? This will also speed play, slightly reduce costs (sensors are used to detect lets) and bring pro tennis in line with college tennis.'
b'ELIMINATE PLAYERS\xe2\x80\x99 RIGHT to catch a service toss without penalty. If a player chooses not to hit the ball once tossed, it should count as a missed serve. This will also speed play and, in making the ideal toss more elusive, take away a smidgen of a server\xe2\x80\x99s advantage.'
b'MAKE A MORE CONCERTED EFFORT to push tournaments to use balls from the same brands or at least with the same characteristics during the different surface swings: hard court, clay court, grass and indoor. Few things irritate players more than significant disparity between balls week to week, and there is concern that abrupt changes can lead to injury. The ATP is working on this issue. Time to hurry up.'
b'PROVIDE PLAYERS AND COACHES with detailed information about court speed and ball characteristics well in advance of a tournament to allow competitors to better prepare. This might also help reduce injuries.'
b'PERMIT FANS TO ENTER A STADIUM as the players change ends after the first game of a set. The current policy, which typically does not allow fans to enter until the changeover after the third game, leaves too many paying customers waiting for too long.'
b'COOPERATE TO DEVELOP JUST ONE MAJOR RATING SYSTEM for tennis players, be they professional or amateur. The Universal Tennis Rating, with the backing of strong private investors, is making inroads. But the International Tennis Federation is also creating its own rating system and algorithm. Such a system is an important concept that could simplify and improve the transition to the professional game. Why create more tennis confusion with competing systems instead of joining forces to produce one that will be universally accepted?'
b'FAIRER USE OF WILD CARDS The Grand Slam tournaments should no longer allow reciprocal wild card entry to players from other Grand Slam nations. It is elitism. And the new-look Davis Cup should definitely not be granting two wild cards to its 18-team final phase. It is anti-competitive.'
b'MORE CONSISTENCY IN APPLYING THE RULES on coaching violations, the timing of line-call challenges and the eligibility of convicted administrators to serve on the ITF board of directors.'
b'A MEN\xe2\x80\x99S GRAND SLAM SINGLES CHAMPION UNDER AGE 30 (there are none active at the moment) and a new French Open men\xe2\x80\x99s champion. And a first major title for South Africa\xe2\x80\x99s Kevin Anderson, which would be the first for an African in singles in 38 years.'
b'ONE MORE MAJOR for Petra Kvitova, who has come back so inspirationally from adversity. Another chance in a major final for Madison Keys to conquer her nerves and play to her potential.'
b'MORE VARIETY IN COURT SPEEDS on tour, fewer injury timeouts. More open roofs, less pain for Andy Murray. More drop-shot returns, fewer tweeners. More integrity, fewer conflicts of interest. More conversations, fewer social-media posts. More players, fewer hitters.'

b'Supported by'
b'By The Associated Press'
b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 Brazilian tennis player Joao Souza has been provisionally suspended again amid a corruption investigation by the Tennis Integrity Unit.'
b'Souza had already been provisionally suspended on March 29 but was reinstated on April 8 following a successful appeal.'
b'The TIU says that the provisional suspension has been put back in place "following consideration of additional evidence submitted by the TIU," adding that no more appeals will be accepted.'
b'No further details were given for the reason of the suspension.'
b'The 30-year old Souza is currently ranked No. 422, having reached a career-high of No. 69 in 2015.'
b'Also in 2015, Souza played in the longest Davis Cup singles match ever, losing to Leonardo Mayer of Argentina 15-13 in the fifth set after 6 hours, 42 minutes.'
b'The TIU is a joint initiative of the Grand Slam Board, the International Tennis Federation and the ATP and the WTA tours.'

b'Supported by'
b'By David Waldstein'
b'TORONTO \xe2\x80\x94 In a subterranean food court in downtown Toronto, shoppers bustled past Maria Patrascu without a glance, unaware that the young woman sipping green tea was the leader of a growing rebellion in professional tennis.'
b'A year ago at this time, Patrascu was a little-known left-hander playing obscure tournaments in Egypt as she tried to get her world ranking under 600. But now she is unable to enter tournaments because of controversial new International Tennis Federation rules designed to slash the ranks of pro players.'
b'So instead of playing, Patrascu, 22, remains at home, seeking to upset the I.T.F.\xe2\x80\x99s new World Tennis Tour one signature at a time. But what began as a petition has turned into a surging player revolt that Patrascu, more than any other player, has helped bring to light.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt started out rebellious, but it has definitely evolved,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s just a movement to pursue justice.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'About 10 months ago, Patrascu began reading how the I.T.F., one of four governing bodies in tennis, planned to introduce a complicated string of rules to restructure the lower levels of the sport. Patrascu grew alarmed that she and hundreds of young players like her would find it far more difficult to get into tournaments and pursue a tennis career.'
b'Last March, Patrascu started an online petition to halt the changes. For many months, it gathered only a modest response \xe2\x80\x94 about 2,400 signatures through December. But once the changes took effect in January and thousands of aspiring players felt the full force of the new rules, support for her petition soared.'
b'It added more than 12,000 new signatures in just the last six weeks and now has more than 14,500. With Patrascu leading the way, supporters have already extracted one concession from the I.T.F., with more possibly on the way.'
b'The movement continues to grow, and some players have met with lawyers to discuss a lawsuit against the I.T.F. Dave Miley, a former federation official and coach who has also opposed the new rules, praised Patrascu and the players and coaches who have joined the fight.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhat she and other players are doing is admirable, and they have cause,\xe2\x80\x9d Miley said. \xe2\x80\x9cTo me, 14,000 voices out there are not uninformed.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Professional tennis has several tiers, much like baseball with its major leagues and several levels of minor leagues below them. The best and most famous tennis players play in ATP or WTA tournaments. The rest, as many as 14,000 of them, toil anonymously around the globe in small events that are supposed to serve as tennis\xe2\x80\x99s talent incubator.'
b'Patrascu is one of those. Born in Bucharest, Romania, in 1997, she moved to Toronto with her parents when she was 5. She showed promise as a junior, winning the Canadian under-14 championship, and turned professional at 18. But her career-high ranking is No. 615 in the I.T.F. and No. 819 in the WTA.'
b'Most players\xe2\x80\x99 chances of making it to stardom are slim, and for many, it is challenging to just break even financially after paying for travel, training and other expenses. That is why the I.T.F., after commissioning an extensive study, declared the old structure unsustainable. Too many marginal players were basically masquerading as professionals.'
b'The I.T.F.\xe2\x80\x99s mission is to promote tennis around the world, and the organization works to ensure that there are tournaments on all continents. But those events have been open to all comers, and they have included players with little hope of breaking into the top tier \xe2\x80\x94 some of them over 50 years old. The I.T.F. study determined that in one year, as many as 6,000 so-called professional players did not earn even $1. A recent independent investigation also found that there was a \xe2\x80\x9ctsunami\xe2\x80\x9d of fixed matches at the lower levels, where players earning little prize money are vulnerable to betting syndicates.'
b'The I.T.F. determined that the best model for professional tennis should include no more than 750 men and 750 women. It recommended new rules to restructure the tour, effectively eliminating almost 13,000 aspirants.'
b'The new system is intended to provide an easier path for the top 100 juniors to matriculate via easier access to bigger tournaments, perhaps at the expense, opponents say, of other players who develop at later ages. (A certain number of spots are reserved at some events for the players in the top 100 junior rankings.) With a smaller pool of truly professional players, the I.T.F. hopes, the meager prize money and ranking points offered at the lower levels could be distributed more efficiently.'
b'But Patrascu, and many others who are taking to various platforms to vent their anger, say that hard-working players with real potential are being caught up in the cull as tournament sizes are reduced and ranking points become more difficult to attain.'
b'Patrascu said she received so many messages every day from frustrated players detailing their own problems with the new tour that she was unable to reply to them all.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99re killing the players\xe2\x80\x99 dreams, just to end up with a handful of really, really good players,\xe2\x80\x9d she said of the I.T.F. \xe2\x80\x9cAll the rest are forgotten.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In December, the I.T.F. granted Patrascu a one-hour conference call with the federation officials Jackie Nesbitt and Andrew Moss. Patrascu later said she felt she had let her fellow players down on that call, because she could not stop the new plan.'
b'Then, in January, the new tour was introduced and Patrascu\xe2\x80\x99s WTA ranking disappeared, she said. The most jarring change for most players is the limit on entrants for the qualifying rounds, the mini tournaments that allow fringe players to play their way into the main draws, where modest prize money and ranking points were up for grabs. These entries were cut to 24.'
b'In the past, many tournaments had large qualifying draws of 48, 64 or even occasionally 128 players.'
b'Patrascu explained how the changes in the size of qualifying draws have affected her boyfriend, Kevin Portmann of Italy, who went to a tournament in Tunisia last month and was required to play two pre-qualifying matches on the day he arrived. That was just to get into the qualifying rounds. She said she could not afford to travel to Africa or Europe for tournaments with little hope of reaching the main draw.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou have to win five matches just to be in position to play someone who is totally fresh,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not fair.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Players are fuming because they now require more points to move up in the rankings, but it is harder to get into the tournaments to get those points. Also, doubles specialists are at a greater disadvantage because singles rankings are now used to determine entry into the doubles draws.'
b'As the new reality sinks in, many players and their coaches, families and friends are turning to Patrascu\xe2\x80\x99s petition. Some have followed her initiative with Facebook pages, like the one with a banner headline that reads, \xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t Kill Tennis.\xe2\x80\x9d Rafael Nadal\xe2\x80\x99s uncle and coach, Toni Nadal, who runs the player\xe2\x80\x99s academy, spoke out against the new rules in an Instagram video this month.'
b'The I.T.F. insisted that Patrascu\xe2\x80\x99s petition contained \xe2\x80\x9cinaccuracies\xe2\x80\x9d and said that much of the other criticism had been \xe2\x80\x9cuninformed.\xe2\x80\x9d But, under siege, it made its first amendment to the new rules last month by expanding qualifying draws to 32 players. The federation also promised to continue monitoring the rules and to act accordingly.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOf course we are listening to the players,\xe2\x80\x9d said Kris Dent, the I.T.F.\xe2\x80\x99s senior executive director for pro circuits. \xe2\x80\x9cIt would be foolish not to listen to our constituents. Change is never easy, but in this case it is vital.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Patrascu said she was encouraged by the revision but said it should only be the start. Meanwhile, her days are spent training indoors in Toronto and stoking the budding rebellion.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t feel like I\xe2\x80\x99m doing this for myself, especially because I\xe2\x80\x99m not sure where my career is headed,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe time that I\xe2\x80\x99ve dedicated to it is really from the bottom of my heart. I wish players could have more opportunities.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Supported by'
b'By Adam Zagoria'
b'The United States Clay Court Championships, a men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis tournament that ended Sunday in Houston, signaled something beyond the transition from the hardcourt season to clay.'
b'It marked the end of the tennis tours\xe2\x80\x99 two-month American swing, which featured six tournaments, including two of the biggest tournaments outside of the four Grand Slam events \xe2\x80\x94 the BNP Paribas Open in Indian Wells, Calif., and the Miami Open.'
b'As the ATP and WTA Tours shift to the red clay and grass courts of Europe, the next major events in the United States won\xe2\x80\x99t come until the hardcourt season in July in the lead-up to the United States Open.'
b'And after the U.S. Open wraps up in early September, the tennis tours depart again, spending much of end of the season in Asia.'
b'American tennis fans used to have more options. In 1990, 24 of 55 WTA events were in the United States. But with the sale of the Connecticut Open in New Haven this year, only seven of 55 WTA events currently on the 2019 calendar are on American soil. Five of those seven are joint events with men, including the U.S. Open, Indian Wells and Miami.'
b'On the men\xe2\x80\x99s side, 16 of 77 worldwide ATP events in 1990 took place in the United States. This year, 11 of 63 will be.'
b'At one time, both the men\xe2\x80\x99s and women\xe2\x80\x99s year-end tour finals were played at Madison Square Garden, but now the men\xe2\x80\x99s event takes place in London and the women\xe2\x80\x99s is in Shenzhen, China. Smaller tournaments in the United States have had trouble selling enough tickets and sponsorships to stay financially viable. And there was even some concern that the Miami Open, which was looking for a new stadium site last year, might be lured out of the country.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think that we will ever become a U.S.-centric tour again,\xe2\x80\x9d said Steve Simon, the chief executive of the WTA. \xe2\x80\x9cI think there\xe2\x80\x99s certainly room for growth for a couple more events, but I think the growth will be in that the events that are here in the States will continue to get bigger. But I do think that we have moved to having a global footprint versus being focused primarily in one country.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Simon said that the WTA planned to introduce two new events in the United States, one beginning this year and another in 2020, both of which will take place the week before the U.S. Open. The location of the 2019 tournament, which would bring the total of WTA events in the country to eight, is expected to be announced in May.'
b'The decline in the number of American tournaments over the last three decades corresponds with the decline in the number of Americans atop the world rankings \xe2\x80\x94 especially on the men\xe2\x80\x99s side \xe2\x80\x94 and the growth of tennis in Europe and Asia.'
b'In December 1990, seven of the top 20 men\xe2\x80\x99s players in the world were Americans, including household names like Andre Agassi, Pete Sampras, Michael Chang and John McEnroe.'
b'The current rankings feature only John Isner at No. 10 among the top 20, followed by Frances Tiafoe at No. 29. They are the only American men in the top 50, and no American man has won a Grand Slam event since Andy Roddick at the U.S. Open in 2003. Since then, Europeans, led by Switzerland\xe2\x80\x99s Roger Federer, Spain\xe2\x80\x99s Rafael Nadal and Serbia\xe2\x80\x99s Novak Djokovic, have won 59 of the 61 major titles.'
b'Women\xe2\x80\x99s tournaments fled the United States even though Serena and Venus Williams were dominant players over the past 20 years and are the reason many current American players took up tennis.'
b'With more than half of the world\xe2\x80\x99s population in Asia, the WTA looked to that continent as a pillar of growth, said Stacey Allaster, the chief executive of professional tennis for the United States Tennis Association and a former leader of the WTA.'
b'In 1990, there were only four WTA tournaments in Asia. This season there are 11 in China alone, part of a tennis boom fueled by the success of Li Na.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think it\xe2\x80\x99s about the quantity of events\xe2\x80\x9d in the United States, Allaster said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe need successful events.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'And for smaller tournaments, being successful can be tough.'
b'When Anne Worcester, the tournament director of the Connecticut Open, realized the tournament was no longer economically viable, she attempted to find a new title sponsor for the event in New Haven.'
b'She considered offers from various American cities, but ultimately sold the tournament to the highest bidder, APG, a sports and entertainment company with a strong footprint in Asia. This year, the tournament, which used to be held the week before the U.S. Open, will be in Zhengzhou, China, the week after the Open.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt has been very emotional to let go of something that I\xe2\x80\x99ve birthed and nurtured for 21 years,\xe2\x80\x9d said Worcester, who was the chief executive of the WTA from 1994 to \xe2\x80\x9998. \xe2\x80\x9cMy kids are 21 and 23, so it was really like having a third child. But the economics were so clear and because I was leading the charge to secure a title sponsor as well as cultivate bidders around the world, I just saw the writing on the wall. As much as our board didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to sell, there was just no choice.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Worcester said it was hard to sell tickets and sponsorships in part because there were fewer American stars to promote. The Connecticut Open in recent years has featured European stars like Simona Halep, Petra Kvitova and Caroline Wozniacki.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn this global sport of tennis, it\xe2\x80\x99s not easy to promote non-Americans,\xe2\x80\x9d Worcester said. \xe2\x80\x9cAmericans want to see Americans.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She remembered her time as the director of worldwide operations for the Virginia Slims Tour, which began in 1970, organized by Billie Jean King and backed by the Philip Morris company.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cJust in the United States of America, Virginia Slims had 17 named tournaments in the major markets of the United States,\xe2\x80\x9d Worcester said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis was filling arenas, indoor and outdoors. It was a very different era, a very different economy, a different product. There were more American players that were on a first-name basis with the world.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The bleeding may have stopped on WTA events leaving the United States. Interest was high in the New Haven event, Worcester said, because global bidders knew that a tournament of its caliber would not be sold again for a long time.'
b'When the men\xe2\x80\x99s Memphis Open faced declining profit and failed to secure a title sponsor several years ago, Josh Ripple feared the event might be purchased by a company that would move the tournament outside the United States.'
b'Ripple, a former president of the WTA Tour, is the executive vice president of GF Sports, a New York-based events company that owns and operates several pro sports events.'
b'In 2015, an affiliate of GF Sports purchased the tournaments in Memphis and Atlanta from the U.S.T.A. and committed to not letting them leave the United States, Ripple said.'
b'After speaking with representatives from Nashville; Columbus, Ohio; Seattle; Dallas; and Phoenix, Ripple and his company moved the Memphis event in 2018 to the renovated Nassau Coliseum on Long Island, where it was held in February. (The Racquet Club in Memphis, which hosted the tournament for 40 years, is closing this spring and will be turned into a hotel and apartment complexes.)'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHopefully, it can have a nice long stay in New York,\xe2\x80\x9d Isner said, adding that he liked \xe2\x80\x9cplaying in the United States as much as possible.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Patrick McEnroe, an ESPN analyst, said that the major American events like the U.S. Open, Indian Wells, Miami and Cincinnati are stronger and more popular than ever but that the lower-level events like the New York Open might continue to face difficulties.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo me, the only way that those can get back to being consistently viable year after year is if at the top we have more American tennis players close to the top that have personality that can sell some tickets,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'

b'Supported by'
b'By The Associated Press'
b'ORDINO, Andorra \xe2\x80\x94 As a brave whistleblower, Marco Trungelliti should be feeling good about himself. The Argentine player exposed match-fixing crooks in tennis, helped the fight against the criminal gambling syndicates that are corroding his sport from within and testified about dishonest fellow professionals who, in part thanks to his evidence, are now banned.'
b"But instead, the 29-year-old says doing the right thing cost him dearly. Ranked No. 139, he's one of the few players so established in the sport willing to speak frankly about the fixers who pay athletes to lose so they can profit from bets on the crooked results. The price of Trungelliti's honesty has been rejection by other players and stress that hurt his health and his game."
b"Compounding his unhappiness, Trungelliti also feels he's been left out to dry by tennis administrators and their anti-corruption investigators. Having pumped him for evidence, he says they failed to publicly defend him against those in tennis who muddied his name, questioned his motives for giving evidence and labeled him a rat."
b'"They just used me," he says. "They just dropped me in the middle of the sea."'
b'"It was a disaster, disaster. In my opinion, it was one of the worst procedures that I have ever seen," he adds. "I\'m still paying the price."'
b'Trungelliti caused a sensation at the French Open last year when he, his younger brother, mother and 88-year-old grandmother squeezed into a rental car and dashed 1,000 kilometers (600 miles) from Spain to Roland Garros so he could fill a "lucky loser" spot at the Grand Slam tournament that opened at the last minute when injured players withdrew.'
b"What few knew at the time was that behind his easy smile, thick curls and feel-good 6-4, 5-7, 6-4, 6-4 first-round victory against Australian Bernard Tomic, Trungelliti was shouldering a weighty secret: He'd been a key witness in a match-fixing probe that snared three fellow Argentines, testifying even though he knew that, back in Argentina, he'd likely face a backlash for doing so."
b"Best-known of the three was Nicolas Kicker, at No. 84, the highest-ranked player convicted so far of fixing matches. The Tennis Integrity Unit, the sport's anti-corruption body with 17 full-time staffers, an annual budget of nearly $5 million and veteran ex-police investigators, announced Kicker's guilt just three days before the French Open, where he had been preparing to play. Neither the TIU nor Trungelliti gave even the slightest hint at the time of the role he'd played."
b"In the aftermath, however, Trungelliti noticed player attitudes changing toward him. Even some he regarded as friends asked why he didn't keep his mouth shut."
b'"No one was saying \'Hi\' any more. No one was looking at me," he says. "It\'s sad."'
b'Contacted by The Associated Press, the TIU said it couldn\'t comment because of its "long-standing confidentiality policy with regard to disciplinary hearings and witness evidence."'
b'Behind the scenes, Trungelliti has repeatedly contacted the unit, asking without success for it to defend him.'
b'"Due to my participation in the trial, I receive all kinds of insults from players to managers," he emailed the TIU last August. "They are trying soil my honor."'
b"Trungelliti's wife, Nadir, says there were times when the stress reduced him to tears. When he was playing, he just wanted to be home. He smashed rackets. A back injury flared again."
b"But he's not shutting up."
b'Trungelliti says match-fixing is an open secret in the game and getting worse.'
b'"It\'s not just the players\' problem," he says. "There are a lot of coaches involved. A lot. A lot. More than we think."'
b'"If you are weak mentally, then you go in, you are all in, for sure, because it\'s easy money," he says. "If you think about it, this is like one hour working for one hundred thousand dollars."'
b'The evidence bears him out.'
b'An investigation commissioned by tennis administrators concluded last December that betting-related corruption is "particularly acute and pervasive" at lower- and mid-level Futures and Challenger tournaments, below the top-tier ATP tour.'
b"Gambling syndicates often target players who, unlike the sport's multi-millionaire stars, struggle to make a good living. In Belgium, prosecutors say they identified 137 mostly lower-level players , from more than a half-dozen countries, suspected of having worked with an Armenian-led gang rolled up last June that allegedly paid 500 to 3,000 euros ($570 to $3,400) for fixed matches and sets. Police say the syndicate employed mules, people hired for a few dollars to place bets small enough to slip under the radar of gambling watchdogs. Two other match-fixing operations were broken up in Spain , in June and October."
b'Trungelliti says he felt compelled to come forward when he was approached in July 2015 by a fixer who posed as a potential sponsor and was introduced via his coach. He wrote to the TIU, saying the fixer "asked me to keep quiet."'
b'"But I can\'t because I hate this," he wrote. "Can you please tell me what I can do? I have his name, his telephone number and a few things he told me."'
b'Those "things" proved explosive.'
b'In a subsequent hour-long interview with a TIU investigator and in a four-page witness statement, Trungelliti meticulously detailed what he knew. He said the fixer laid out a sliding scale of bribes: $2,000 to $3,000 for fixed Futures matches; $5,000 to $10,000 in mid-level Challenger tournaments; $50,000 to $100,000 on the ATP tour where the biggest stars play.'
b"The fixer said he paid cash and communicated using encrypted, easily deleted text messages. He reeled off players he said he'd fixed matches with. Three leapt out at Trungelliti, all Argentines: Kicker, Patricio Heras and Federico Coria."
b'The fixer was particularly "proud" of a Challenger match fixed in Italy with Kicker, Trungelliti told the TIU. Kicker lost 6-1, 6-2 in 63 minutes to South Korea\'s Duckhee Lee, then ranked 74 spots below Kicker, at No. 278.'
b'Kicker is now serving a three-year ban, with the possibility of an additional three-year suspension hanging over him if he breaches anti-corruption rules again.'
b'Heras, whose career-best ranking was No. 269 in 2013, also is banned for three years, with an additional two years suspended .'
b"Coria was banned for two months, with another six months suspended, for failing to report that he was offered money in July 2015 to lose a set at a Futures tournament in Italy and for not telling the TIU of another approach a month later to lose several matches. The TIU specified that Coria hadn't actually taken money or fixed games. But the TIU investigator who questioned Coria testified there was evidence in his iPhone of contacts with the fixer who also sought to groom Trungelliti."
b"Whether the fixer is still operating is unclear. The TIU hasn't announced any sanctions against the fixer or said whether it shared Trungelliti's testimony about him with police."
b"As painful as the whistleblowing process has been for Trungelliti, he says he'd go through it again if he had to. He says he reported a separate approach by another fixer in 2016."
b'His TIU witness statement neatly summed up his thinking.'
b'"I love tennis," he testified. "I feel very saddened by the state of tennis and the fact that match-fixing is happening so often."'

b'(Reuters) - Brazilian Joao Souza has been provisionally suspended for the second time this year amid a corruption investigation, the Tennis Integrity Unit (TIU) said on Friday.'
b'Souza, ranked 422nd in the world, was initially suspended on March 29 due to alleged breaches of the Tennis Anti-Corruption Program but was reinstated this month following a successful appeal.'
b'However, the TIU said the suspension has been reimposed "following consideration of additional evidence", adding that no more appeals will be accepted.'
b'"The effect of the provisional suspension is that Mr Souza is ineligible to compete in or attend any sanctioned event organized or recognized by the governing bodies of the sport," the TIU said in a statement http://www.tennisintegrityunit.com/media-releases/brazilian-tennis-player-joao-souza-provisionally-suspended-independent-anti-corruption-hearing-officer.'
b'Souza, who turned professional in 2006, has never won an ATP Tour title as he has spent the majority of his career on the Challenger circuit. '
b'The 30-year-old reached his career-high singles ranking of number 69 in 2015.'
b'More tennis players were disciplined for violations of anti-corruption rules in 2018 than in any other year since the creation of the TIU 10 years ago.'

b'By Cindy Shmerler'
b'DELRAY BEACH, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 Dan Evans finished a practice session last month, grabbed a racket by the strings and marched from the court toward the player locker room.'
b'It was the same path walked by Juan Mart\xc3\xadn del Potro the night before. For del Potro, a flash mob gathered as fans chanted \xe2\x80\x9cOl\xc3\xa9, Ol\xc3\xa9, Ol\xc3\xa9, Delpo, Delpo,\xe2\x80\x9d and implored the popular Argentine to autograph photos, tennis balls, hats, T-shirts and even one man\xe2\x80\x99s bald head.'
b'When Evans walked the route, just hours before he was to take the court against Radu Albot in the final of the Delray Beach Open on Feb. 24, no one stopped him to chat or ask for his autograph. Not a single spectator recognized Evans, a 28-year-old Briton.'
b'He was alone with his thoughts. But he was used to that.'
b'For more than a year, Evans spent most of his time alone after being barred from the ATP Tour for a positive drug test for cocaine. Evans said that while he used cocaine recreationally and out of competition, which is not prohibited in tennis, he tested positive during the Barcelona Open in April 2017 when he left some of the drug in a bag that contaminated other medication.'
b'Evans, who was ranked a career-high No. 41 at the time of his ban, had recently reached his first career ATP final in Sydney. He did not appeal the charge.'
b'The Delray Beach Open was only his fourth ATP Tour tournament since his return in April 2018. He lost the final to Albot in a third-set tiebreaker despite holding three match points, but his ranking is up to No. 100 as he begins the qualifying tournament for the BNP Paribas Open in Indian Wells, Calif., on Tuesday.'
b'With no ability to play tournaments or train during the ban, Evans retreated to his home in Cheltenham on the outskirts of the picturesque Cotswolds, some 90 miles northwest of London. He was forbidden to even practice at any facilities affiliated with Britain\xe2\x80\x99s Lawn Tennis Association for 10 months.'
b'He filled his days quietly playing golf and watching television, though he refused to tune in to any tennis matches. He said he would not even follow tournament results in the newspaper. Some days, he said, it was too painful to leave the house.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was a really tough time in my life,\xe2\x80\x9d Evans said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut there were a lot of other people around me who had a difficult year as well. I would be selfish to think that it didn\xe2\x80\x99t affect everyone else in my life.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThose feelings of anger and hurt at what you did to people don\xe2\x80\x99t go away easily,\xe2\x80\x9d Evans added, referring to the pain and embarrassment he caused his family, his girlfriend and a bevy of coaches and supporters.'
b'This was not the first time he had been penalized. In 2006, Evans was pulled from the Wimbledon junior tournament by the L.T.A., the national governing body the sport, for unacceptable on-court behavior. Two years later, he was suspended by the L.T.A. for four months after he was photographed during Wimbledon at a nightclub in the early morning hours. And in 2010, the L.T.A. stopped financially supporting him for underperformance and a poor attitude.'
b'Evans was unranked when he returned from this latest suspension in April 2018 and was forced to start at the lower levels of professional tennis. With no points to defend, and little compassion from his fellow competitors, Evans began entering Challengers, tennis\xe2\x80\x99s version of the minor leagues. He often had to play three matches just to get into the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s main draw. But in August he won a Challenger in Vancouver, British Columbia, and reached the final of another in France in February.'
b'At the ATP Tour level, he was given a wild card to play the event at Queen\xe2\x80\x99s Club in London in June and lost his first match. He tried to qualify for Wimbledon last year, reaching the second round. He qualified for the main draw of this year\xe2\x80\x99s Australian Open and lost to Roger Federer in the second round. His breakthrough at Delray Beach included wins over No. 9 John Isner and No. 35 Frances Tiafoe.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn retrospect, his journey has been incredibly quick for someone with no ranking,\xe2\x80\x9d said David Felgate, Tim Henman\xe2\x80\x99s longtime coach, who began working with Evans just after his return. \xe2\x80\x9cDan doesn\xe2\x80\x99t expect anything from anyone; he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t expect sympathy. He knows what he did to himself. But it does give him a different perspective and may prolong his career. When you realized you missed a year, you want to make up for it. You want this career to go on for a long time because you know what not playing felt like.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'At 5-foot-9, Evans lacks the serving power of tennis\xe2\x80\x99s taller players like del Potro, who is 6-6. But Evans is scrappy off the ground, particularly with his running forehand pass down the line. He also possesses an effective one-handed slice backhand. And he loves to volley, just as his countryman Henman did.'
b'As far as he has come over the last year, he knows he has still got a long way to go.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cListen, that episode in my life of being banned, it\xe2\x80\x99s over,\xe2\x80\x9d Evans said. \xe2\x80\x9cEveryone forgave me as soon as I held my hands up and accepted the blame. But it\xe2\x80\x99s not easy to be happy with yourself day in and day out when the fact is, I was No. 41 in the world and I threw it all away.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He added: \xe2\x80\x9cBut to say that I\xe2\x80\x99ve grown, that would be justifying it. There\xe2\x80\x99s no sort of philosophical looking back on it. It was the worst thing ever. Now, I\xe2\x80\x99m just back trying to win tennis matches.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'On Tennis'
b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'INDIAN WELLS, Calif. \xe2\x80\x94 Novak Djokovic played his first official tennis match in more than a month on Saturday night, defeating the American Bjorn Fratangelo in straight sets at the BNP Paribas Open.'
b'But Djokovic has hardly been taking an extended break from official tennis business.'
b'Back at No. 1 in the world by a hefty margin, he is also wielding his renewed clout off court as president of the ATP player council. As a result of his maneuvering, the men\xe2\x80\x99s tour is in need of a new chief executive along with some collective purpose and peace of mind, which are likely to remain more elusive than Djokovic and his allies might like.'
b'As ever, the tension is between the players, who understandably want to maximize their earnings in a brutally competitive sport, and their paymasters, who own and operate the tournaments and understandably would rather keep prize money under tight rein. But the unusual and inconvenient thing in men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis is that the players and paymasters are part of the same internally conflicted organization: the ATP.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are really blocked,\xe2\x80\x9d said Gilles Simon, the French player and a former council member. \xe2\x80\x9cThe structure works against us and the imbalance being already there between the tournaments and the players, the imbalance endures.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Acrimony is inevitable. Progress is not. Last week, Djokovic and the players appeared to send a strong message when the player representatives on the ATP Tour\xe2\x80\x99s board of directors voted against extending the contract of Chris Kermode, the ATP\xe2\x80\x99s executive chairman and president, who will now be obliged to step down at the end of 2019.'
b'But such a political power play is only intimidating if the players are truly united, which seems far from the case.'
b'The player council, in a nonbinding vote before the board meeting, could not reach agreement on whether to recommend or reject Kermode\xe2\x80\x99s extension.'
b'In an age of constant communication, the biggest stars are somehow struggling to connect. Roger Federer, a former president of the player council, said Sunday that he had reached out to Djokovic before the vote only to be told that Djokovic could not squeeze him in.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s hard to understand for me,\xe2\x80\x9d Federer said.'
b'Rafael Nadal, a supporter of Kermode and continuity, said his cellphone was primed and ready, but no calls or texts came his way.'
b'This sounds more like high school than a global professional sport.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey are representing us, so normally they have to ask, what\xe2\x80\x99s our opinion? Not in every small decision, but in big decisions,\xe2\x80\x9d Nadal said. \xe2\x80\x9cIn my opinion, this one was a big decision.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The players and the tournaments each have three representatives on the ATP board of directors. The chairman \xe2\x80\x94 Kermode since 2014 \xe2\x80\x94 has the ability to cast a tiebreaking vote but would prefer to avoid it when possible for fear of endangering support from one side of the divide.'
b'It is a difficult dance even in the best of circumstances, and Kermode seems to have stepped on the wrong feet.'
b'Djokovic did not vote him out. That was up to the player representatives that he and the player council have supported or voted into place: David Egdes, a Tennis Channel executive; Alex Inglot, the director of communications at Sportradar; and Justin Gimelstob, the Tennis Channel commentator and former American player, who remains the most polarizing back-room figure in the sport and has remained in place despite facing felony battery charges.'
b'Under the ATP\xe2\x80\x99s voting system, Kermode needed majority support (at least two votes) from each camp to continue. He received all three of the tournament representatives\xe2\x80\x99 votes but apparently failed to get any of the player representatives\xe2\x80\x99 votes.'
b'In a letter to ATP staff last week after his ouster, Kermode said it was \xe2\x80\x9cironic\xe2\x80\x9d that he was leaving after \xe2\x80\x9cthe players have achieved some of the greatest gains in the history of the ATP Tour in the past five years.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Kermode, a former low-level pro player and high-level tournament director, is a polished and genial Briton who knows how to work a room but apparently not every boardroom.'
b'Running the ATP Tour is a compromised position to begin with; the real power in tennis lies with the four Grand Slam tournaments, which function independently. Still, he navigated his position of weakness for more than five years, securing sponsorships and a hard-won prize money increase from the top tier of ATP tournaments.'
b'He also led the creation of new events like the Next Gen ATP Finals, designed to promote young players like 19-year-old Canadian Denis Shapovalov, who will eventually have to step out of the ink-black shadow cast by Federer, Nadal and Djokovic.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFrom what I know of Chris, he was unbelievable,\xe2\x80\x9d Shapovalov said.'
b'But clearly not everyone is in the Kermode fan club.'
b'He is seen by some of the players as a \xe2\x80\x9ctournament guy,\xe2\x80\x9d a characterization he rejects. Others grumble about his handling of the ATP Cup, which will be relaunched in the opening week of the 2020 season in Australia.'
b'With the new-look Davis Cup using a similar format, Kermode tried to avoid a team-event glut by working toward a combined event. But he was overruled last year by the players.'
b'There is also criticism that he did not secure more prize money gains, above all from the four Grand Slam events. As council president, Federer once spearheaded a successful push for major increases, but with Grand Slam revenues growing, the concern is that prize money has not kept pace.'
b'Federer and Nadal could re-enter the fray. They talked tennis governance over coffee at Federer\xe2\x80\x99s rented house here last week. But for now, it is the 31-year-old Djokovic\xe2\x80\x99s turn to lead on court and off. He is multitasking at a point in his career when family time is ever more important to him and when he is again on the verge of holding all four of the Grand Slam singles titles.'
b'Why bother with tennis politics at this stage?, I asked him.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI tend to ask that myself, as well,\xe2\x80\x9d he said with a grin. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I feel that it is my responsibility, in a way, as a top player to contribute to the sport in that way, as well.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Even if he charts a steadier course in the months to come, putting a more \xe2\x80\x9cplayer friendly\xe2\x80\x9d ATP chief in place looks all but impossible with the tournament representatives effectively possessing veto power on the board.'
b'Changing the governance structure, as Djokovic has suggested, sounds nearly as tricky.'
b'Craig Tiley, the chief executive of Tennis Australia and a driving force in the Australian Open\xe2\x80\x99s growth, would be a strong ATP leader and has been interested in the chief executive post in the past.'
b'But with mutual trust at low ebb and no player union in sight, it is likely a compromise candidate will take over.'
b'Sure, tennis needs change and fresh ideas. But when you tear down a building, it seems best to have a clear idea what will stand in its place.'

b'Burned out, struggling with depression and fed up with cyberbullying, Rebecca Marino, one of Canada\xe2\x80\x99s brightest prospects, quit tennis in 2013. A year into her comeback, she\xe2\x80\x99s climbing the rankings.'
b'By Ben Rothenberg'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 For the first point she played at a Grand Slam event in six years, Rebecca Marino hit an ace.'
b'She celebrated with a subtle fist pump, determined to have the best next act she could after a lengthy intermission during which she became the face of depression among athletes.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s easy to get caught up in the moment, just going from tournament to tournament now,\xe2\x80\x9d Marino said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut if I stop and think about it, then that\xe2\x80\x99s when I see that it\xe2\x80\x99s pretty cool that I was able to do this, and to get this far, from no ranking to suddenly in the qualies of a Slam.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Marino lost, 6-2, 6-2, to Caroline Dolehide on Tuesday in the first round of Australian Open qualifying, limited by a back injury, which curtailed her off-season training. Despite her stiffness, Marino, 28, showed flashes of the power and clean ball-striking that sent her into the upper echelons of tennis seven years ago.'
b'With a percussive forehand and a booming serve that topped out at 120 miles per hour, Marino surged to a high of 38th in the rankings in the summer of 2011, when she was 20. Not a highly touted junior prospect, she had planned to enroll in college before her tennis successes mounted, catapulting her faster and further than she was prepared to handle.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNot expecting it, I felt like I was thrown into this machine, and I didn\xe2\x80\x99t understand how it worked,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Marino stepped back from the sport for the first time in 2012, taking seven months off. After returning for several months, she retired in February 2013 at age 22.'
b'In a conference call announcing her decision, Marino revealed her struggles with depression; days earlier, she had discussed her social media abuse in an interview with The New York Times. Her leaving the sport was often attributed to one of those factors, or both of them, which Marino said was inaccurate in retrospect.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen I look back, I wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t necessarily say it was depression,\xe2\x80\x9d she said of her decision to stop playing. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was burnout, and it was expectations put on my shoulders by myself and others, and I just wasn\xe2\x80\x99t able to cope. It kind of all came to a head in a big, giant burnout, I guess.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Though her absence was longer than most, Marino is not the only player to have stepped away from the sport because of burnout. Most notably, the top Australian Ash Barty took off nearly two years early in her career. Barty has become a top player in her return, and she defeated No. 1 Simona Halep in Sydney this week.'
b'For Marino, stepping away from tennis made her \xe2\x80\x9cable to become superhappy and enjoy my life,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. '
b'Marino\xe2\x80\x99s retirement at 22 generated considerable attention, particularly in her native Canada, where she was one of the brightest tennis prospects in generations. '
b'Her story resonated with others, but she felt uneasy being a touchstone for athletes struggling with depression. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt wasn\xe2\x80\x99t something I was prepared for, and it\xe2\x80\x99s still something I\xe2\x80\x99m kind of grappling with,\xe2\x80\x9d Marino said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m still a really private person, and so for people to come up to me and tell me all of the things they\xe2\x80\x99ve dealt with, or how I\xe2\x80\x99ve affected them, it\xe2\x80\x99s difficult sometimes, because I don\xe2\x80\x99t really know what to say. Even though I\xe2\x80\x99m happy that I\xe2\x80\x99ve helped people, it can be overwhelming because I\xe2\x80\x99m not professionally trained to help people.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After retiring from tennis, Marino worked one summer for her family\xe2\x80\x99s construction business, pouring cement and digging through clay. She later began teaching tennis lessons and enrolled at the University of British Columbia, where she studied English literature. The works she enjoyed most, she said, were ones from the Victorian era that grappled with the effects of industrialization on society.'
b'In her second year, the university\xe2\x80\x99s rowing coach recruited her to join the team, knowing her athletic background and her family\xe2\x80\x99s extensive history in the sport. b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo have a competitive outlet through a team like that was superfun,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt made me feel like I was a part of the university community. People didn\xe2\x80\x99t look at me for my tennis anymore; they just looked at me as a student-athlete.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Marino was shaken in February 2017 when her father, Joe, received a prostate cancer diagnosis.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAfter he finished chemo, I kind of took a step back and wanted to look at what was important in my life,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cI didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to live with any regrets, and I thought that tennis was the one thing in my life that I kind of wish I had a do-over for.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She also wanted her father to see her play again. Marino weighed the idea of a return for months and gained confidence after serving as a hitting partner at a tournament in Vancouver, her hometown, in August 2017. '

b'After a false start because she did not re-enter tennis\xe2\x80\x99s antidoping program in time, Marino returned to the sport at its lowest rung last January, at a series of small tournaments in Turkey. b'Marino plans a long stay in the sport this time, and is working to ensure it is more pleasant and sustainable. She stays in better contact with friends, including more trips home to Vancouver, to help her keep one foot outside the sometimes suffocating tennis bubble.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMy friends don\xe2\x80\x99t play tennis, so they don\xe2\x80\x99t care if I win or lose,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99re just concerned about how I\xe2\x80\x99m doing as a person, if I\xe2\x80\x99m enjoying myself, and when I\xe2\x80\x99ll be back so we can hang out. Though she has shown signs of resurgence, she is also a cautionary tale after struggling to manage new expectations, albeit with a more limited tennis skill set than Andreescu\xe2\x80\x99s.'
b'Keeping Andreescu grounded as her prospects soar is her team\xe2\x80\x99s goal, and her own goal, too.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s easy to get distracted,\xe2\x80\x9d said her coach, Sylvain Bruneau, the head of women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis at Tennis Canada. \xe2\x80\x9cBut it\xe2\x80\x99s going to be part of my work to make sure she stays in the moment.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Andreescu does her part by spending 15 minutes each morning doing what she calls \xe2\x80\x9ccreative visualization\xe2\x80\x9d: imagining herself experiencing the situations she will face on court and off so she will be better equipped to manage them if and when they come. Many elite athletes rely on visualization, including the world\xe2\x80\x99s best women\xe2\x80\x99s Alpine skier, Mikaela Shiffrin.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI used to do hours and hours of it, but I found that 15 minutes has really helped me, and it\xe2\x80\x99s not time-consuming at all,\xe2\x80\x9d Andreescu said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s something I got online from a course. My mom introduced it to me when I was 13, and I have been doing it ever since.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Andreescu\xe2\x80\x99s parents moved to Canada in 1994. Her mother, Maria, has a master\xe2\x80\x99s degree in economics; her father, Nicu, is a mechanical engineer.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe arrived in Canada with two suitcases, and that\xe2\x80\x99s all,\xe2\x80\x9d Nicu Andreescu told The Globe and Mail. \xe2\x80\x9cWe had a great first impression when we arrived, having come from a former communist country. We wanted to go to Canada and start a new life and have a better future for any kids we might have.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Bianca is their only child, and though she developed her game under the umbrella of Tennis Canada, the sport\xe2\x80\x99s governing body there, she said she took her first tennis lesson at age 7 in Romania, where her mother had moved back temporarily for a business opportunity.'
b'That lesson was on clay (bring on Roland Garros), and though her family was soon reunited in Canada, Andreescu has retained strong ties to Romania. Simona Halep, the Romanian star, was one of her two main tennis role models along with Kim Clijsters.'
b'Andreescu speaks Romanian with her parents and attributes her combativeness on court to her \xe2\x80\x9cRomanian roots.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think we are very passionate, and we leave it all out there,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s all heart.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She has shown plenty of grit in Indian Wells, rallying in the first round to beat the Romanian player Irina-Camelia Begu, 6-7 (3), 6-3, 6-3, on the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s second biggest show court.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI actually thought I was going to lose,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cI was really nervous.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She experienced back pain in that match, which has been a recurring problem and was still troubling her late Friday night as she repeatedly shifted position in her chair during an interview after the duel with Svitolina.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI have a lot of weakness in my core, so that\xe2\x80\x99s definitely something I\xe2\x80\x99m improving on,\xe2\x80\x9d said Andreescu, who has also missed significant court time with a stress fracture in her foot.'
b'On Friday against Svitolina, she had to fight through leg cramps in the final set, in which she managed to convert her fourth match point \xe2\x80\x94 mixing drop shots with big, bold groundstrokes as she constructed points down the stretch.'
b'Though tennis stars are trending taller, Andreescu is 5-foot-7. But she has powerful legs that help her generate tremendous pace when she needs it with both her midcourt forehand and her two-handed backhand and to leap high off the ground when serving. Her second serve, unlike for many players of her size, is not a weakness.'
b'Though she has abundant power and world-class mobility, what separates her from the pack is her ability to change pace. She can lob and generate acute angles with off-speed groundstrokes. b'Andreescu fearlessly uses the whole canvas.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI love that,\xe2\x80\x9d she said of the description. \xe2\x80\x9cNo one has ever said that about my game before, but that definitely describes it, I think. I like to hit every shot in the book.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She is now 2-0 against top-10 players after upsetting Caroline Wozniacki in January in Auckland, where she also defeated Venus Williams.'

b'But though the emotions were powerful again on Friday night, beating her tour elders is fast becoming a habit. Instead of merely making it into the French Open draw, she now has a fine chance of being seeded.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI do believe that I deserve to be here,\xe2\x80\x9d she said sotto voce as the interview ended. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I didn\xe2\x80\x99t expect for it to come so quickly. b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'Another season of Grand Slam tennis begins at the Australian Open on Monday, but Agnieszka Radwanska, who retired in November, won\xe2\x80\x99t be part of it.'
b'Aptly called \xe2\x80\x9cThe Ninja\xe2\x80\x9d for her ability to inflict out-of-nowhere pain on the opposition from all manner of contortionist positions, Radwanska\xe2\x80\x99s spectacular, poker-faced shotmaking will be missed.'
b'But even without its Ninja, the women\xe2\x80\x99s game is in a memorable phase when it comes to entertainment value and players with an uncommon touch.'
b'At the moment and probably not for long, the tour is a clash of generations with Serena Williams, 37, and Venus Williams, 38, still in the mix along with midcareer champions like Angelique Kerber, 30, and Caroline Wozniacki, 28, and the new wave led by Naomi Osaka, 21, the Japanese sensation who upset Serena Williams to win the United States Open last year. It is rare to see such a range of players clashing with the outcomes so uncertain.'
b'The tour has geographical breadth with players from the United States, Europe, Asia and Australia all in the top 20 and with Ons Jabeur, 24, of Tunisia in the top 60 after last year, becoming the first Arab woman to reach a WTA final.'
b'But there is another strong and too often undervalued selling point: stylistic variety. Though serious baseline power remains the most popular and fail-safe route to stardom, players with subtler, more creative games are also finding a way to win consistently, just as Radwanska, a former world No. 2 and Wimbledon finalist, did before her injuries.'
b'Several of these tennis \xe2\x80\x9cartists\xe2\x80\x9d will be seeded at the Australian Open: No. 10 Daria Kasatkina of Russia, No. 13 Anastasija Sevastova of Latvia, No. 15 Ashleigh Barty of Australia, and No. 28 Hsieh Su-wei of Taiwan, a 33-year-old whose double-handed, frequently off-speed strokes are as crafty as they come. There is also Jabeur, still an outsider but whose game is a crowd-pleasing mix of baseline punch, feathery touch and Federer-esque flourishes.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere will always be exceptions to the power players,\xe2\x80\x9d said Paul McNamee, the former Australian men\xe2\x80\x99s star who advises Hsieh. \xe2\x80\x9cThe players you refer to, however, all have one thing in common: exceptional hands. They have amazing touch, and this is why they can survive even if they have less raw power.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That hardly means they have none. Barty, despite being 5-foot-5 and shorter than most of her rivals, generates the leg drive and racket-head speed to hit big serves and forehands. Her crisply sliced backhand has unusual bite, and she has perhaps the best net game in the sport.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe plan to get to the net more often is a focus for 2019,\xe2\x80\x9d said Craig Tyzzer, her coach. \xe2\x80\x9cAsh certainly benefits from playing more doubles than most of the other singles girls, but her volley skills were certainly developed from an early age, which is a massive advantage.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Kasatkina has a heavy topspin forehand that she can flatten out to create more pace when she requires it.'
b'But what distinguishes the members of the WTA\xe2\x80\x99s creative class from their peers is the size of their tool set and the range of their tactical options. Their success has meant more matchups that feature contrasting styles: important to the appeal of a game where patterns have a tendency to repeat.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTennis is a game of chess, of tactics,\xe2\x80\x9d said Philippe Dehaes, Kasatkina\xe2\x80\x99s coach, who has emerged as one of the tour\xe2\x80\x99s leading mentors and motivators. \xe2\x80\x9cYou have to vary zones and trajectories and find the answer suited to what your opponent is doing. To have women who play well tactically and who can keep the ball in play, while varying and creating, makes the show much more interesting for people, in my opinion.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It is not the contrast that tennis once regularly offered. When Martina Navratilova was attacking the net in the 1970s and 1980s against her baseline-hugging archrival Chris Evert and others, the gulf between styles and tennis philosophies was much wider.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen you had serve-and-volleyers going against baseliners, that was more of a complete and obvious contrast,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tracy Austin, the precocious champion who faced Navratilova frequently. \xe2\x80\x9cBut in this day and age where the game has become homogenized, we\xe2\x80\x99re looking for any contrast. It\xe2\x80\x99s not as extreme as it used to be, but that\xe2\x80\x99s why Hsieh Su-wei is fun to watch, because you feel like you can see the wheels turning in her mind as to where to place the ball, the geometry of the court. So many players use left and right, and she uses north and south as well.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Hsieh is constantly changing depth: shifting her target from the backcourt to the forecourt as she mixes in drop shots, angled volleys and sliced and flat groundstrokes.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHer hands can redirect a shot in either direction on both wings with pinpoint accuracy,\xe2\x80\x9d McNamee said. \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s not normal.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But outlier fast-twitch defensive skills are required to thrive in an era of abundant power and athleticism, of taller, stronger opposition with superior leverage like Petra Kvitova, Garbine Muguruza, Karolina Pliskova, Madison Keys and the ascendant Aryna Sabalenka.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI try to do something else than the normal,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sevastova, a U.S. Open semifinalist last year whose trademark is the drop shot. \xe2\x80\x9cI think it\xe2\x80\x99s important, and it\xe2\x80\x99s my style. It\xe2\x80\x99s not like I don\xe2\x80\x99t have power. I just don\xe2\x80\x99t have that much. But I can handle their pace and hit the ball quickly, and I like variety.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Dehaes sees more women being able to survive the onslaught.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think that has always been the case, but in the last few years we saw it a bit less,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think the equipment played a big role, and there was the evolution of women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis with players becoming stronger physically and better technically. Because everyone trains a lot and everyone trains well, which was not always the case in former times. So with more athletic players and more high-performance equipment, the pace of the game accelerated. But I think now the girls are getting used to it and are more able to counter the games of these super-powerful players.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Tennis\xe2\x80\x99s recent honor roll confirms that. b'\xe2\x80\x9cHonestly, it could be just 15 percent more aggression that can make the difference,\xe2\x80\x9d Austin said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou are just robbing your opponent of a little bit of time on certain shots.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Martin Blackman, general manager of player development at the United States Tennis Association, says he believes that \xe2\x80\x9cwe will see more and more complete players on the women\xe2\x80\x99s side.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Purer power players are also trying to broaden their range. In her late teens, Osaka clearly had potent groundstrokes and a penetrating serve. b'\xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s pulled back some; Sascha\xe2\x80\x99s got her thinking more on the court rather than just see ball, hit ball,\xe2\x80\x9d Austin said. \xe2\x80\x9cNow, she\xe2\x80\x99s fit enough and aware enough and realizes, \xe2\x80\x98O.K., this is a red-light ball. b'The artists are also at work on finding the time to use their brushes.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMy challenge with Dasha,\xe2\x80\x9d said Dehaes, using Kasatkina\xe2\x80\x99s nickname, \xe2\x80\x9cis to help her find a way to stay in the rally even under great pressure, and at a certain moment, the right moment, make the difference with a variation. b'DELRAY BEACH, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 Before the start of every tennis match now, Stevie Johnson walks to the back of the court and squats down for a moment or two. Sometimes he says a little prayer. Often he gives himself an abbreviated pep talk.'
b'Almost always he thinks of doing things the way his father wanted him to.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI really just say a couple of words to myself to help me put everything in perspective,\xe2\x80\x9d said Johnson, 29, whose father, Steve, died of a heart attack at 58 nearly two years ago. \xe2\x80\x9cI tell myself to do things the right way and to treat people with respect. And I remind myself that tennis doesn\xe2\x80\x99t define me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Johnson has had a hard time keeping tennis, and life, in perspective since May 2017, when his mother reached him by phone just as he was about to board a plane to Rome for the Italian Open and told him that his father had failed to wake up that morning.'
b'Not only had his father taught Stevie how to play the game, he also sat in the stands for college matches at Southern California and for pro matches at Wimbledon and the United States Open. He witnessed his son\xe2\x80\x99s first ATP pro titles in Nottingham, England, in 2016 and in Houston just weeks before his death.'
b'Entering the Delray Beach Open, which began on Feb. 16, Johnson had not won a match since squandering a two-sets-to-one lead against ninth-seeded Dominic Thiem in the second round of last year\xe2\x80\x99s U.S. Open.'
b'Johnson had lost nine straight matches, including one against Borna Coric in the Americans\xe2\x80\x99 Davis Cup semifinal loss to Croatia in September. He fell in the first round at last week\xe2\x80\x99s New York Open to 154th-ranked Brayden Schnur, even though he served for the match and held two match points (Schnur was the eventual tournament runner-up). After that loss, Johnson was despondent in the locker room.'
b'When Johnson, seeded fourth in Delray, won his first match on Tuesday over a longtime friend and Southern California neighbor, 131st-ranked Jason Jung, he said, \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m just glad to get the monkey off my back and not lose 10 straight.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He followed that with a win over Paolo Lorenzi of Italy on Thursday but then lost in the quarterfinals to 82nd-ranked Radu Albot of Moldova, 1-6, 6-3, 7-6 (5). In that match, Johnson raced to a 5-0 lead in only 18 minutes, and then to a 6-1, 3-1 lead before Albot reeled off 12 of the next 15 points and five consecutive games. Johnson was two points from winning the match late in the third set, but Albot sneaked to the net for a backhand stab volley, and Johnson then hit a forehand wide on match point.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s embarrassing,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s frustrating. I was up a set and a break, and I got tight. Thought I was on a good path, and then this. That\xe2\x80\x99s the way life\xe2\x80\x99s been going for me these days.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Despite his five-month losing streak, Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s ranking should stay near his current No. 34. He is the third-best American, behind No. 9 John Isner and No. 29 Frances Tiafoe, the defending Delray Beach champion, who lost in the first round here this year.'
b'Losing has been a bitter pill, especially because he came so close to upsetting Thiem. But a rolled ankle midway through the second set contributed to the 3-hour-34-minute loss.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI probably shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have even played after the U.S. Open,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson said. \xe2\x80\x9cI just didn\xe2\x80\x99t have any tennis left in me. Just all the traveling, from New York to L.A. to Croatia, back to L.A., then Asia and Europe. The way the schedule is, you feel like you need to play all the time, and I got into that trap. But that\xe2\x80\x99s what you have to do when you play tennis; you have to earn it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not an N.F.L. player who signs a lucrative four-year deal and then can take five months off, have a bad slump and then turn it around. Every week you have to prove yourself. If you have a bad six months, you can go from No. 8 in the world to No. 78, or worse.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Johnson has been transparent about how difficult life has been since his father\xe2\x80\x99s death. He often looks to his players\xe2\x80\x99 box, only to see a glaring vacuum where his father used to sit. There are days when he still can\xe2\x80\x99t bring himself to leave the house.'
b'After a third-round loss to the eventual runner-up Marin Cilic at Wimbledon in 2017, he was so physically and emotionally spent that he developed a fever that lingered and landed him in the hospital. And after a three-set loss in the first round of the 2018 New York Open, he felt as if the ground was spinning, and he experienced shortness of breath that was attributed to anxiety.'
b'That experience led Johnson to seek advice from Mardy Fish, a former top-10 player whose career was marked by bouts of anxiety. At the urging of his mother, Michelle, Johnson also sought help from a psychologist, someone he continues to see whenever he is home in Redondo Beach, Calif.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cStevie\xe2\x80\x99s mom has been instrumental to him,\xe2\x80\x9d said Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s wife, Kendall, a former U.S.C. volleyball player who has been with him for almost seven years. \xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s paved the way with her own recovery and helps him put things into perspective. Even through his grieving, Stevie knows his father wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t want him to struggle and that he would want him to keep playing.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Craig Boynton, who has coached Johnson through much of his professional career, said he understood the danger of being sucked down a losing-run rabbit hole.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe funny thing about streaks is that when they snowball the right way, you stop thinking and have great clarity in your execution of your shots,\xe2\x80\x9d Boynton said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut when the streak is going the wrong way, there\xe2\x80\x99s a tendency to overthink and doubt yourself. That takes away your focus from your execution. There\xe2\x80\x99s no flow, and it creates drought or a rut, and that\xe2\x80\x99s what Stevie\xe2\x80\x99s been going through. One match can change things in either direction.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After two wins in Delray Beach, there was finally a greater hop in Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s step. But it does not mean he no longer has dark thoughts, no longer wonders whether he should even continue to play tennis.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSome days it\xe2\x80\x99s easy to fight through and enjoy it,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut those hard days have been outweighing the good days at the moment.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s hard to fake the passion,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, choking on his words and using a towel to wipe away tears. \xe2\x80\x9cI mean, my father was such a big part of my tennis life. Tennis is just a weird dynamic for me right now. Every day is different. I mean, he should still be here watching me.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'\xe2\x80\x9cMentally, it\xe2\x80\x99s the same stuff. Technically, she knows tennis. She knows what I need to do on the court to be better. For me, that\xe2\x80\x99s what is important.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Pouille\xe2\x80\x99s choice of Mauresmo was the second high-profile hiring of a female coach in men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis this decade. The first was in 2014, when Andy Murray also hired Mauresmo.'
b'Pouille\xe2\x80\x99s decision generated far less second-guessing than Murray\xe2\x80\x99s, which was met with skepticism from both the news media and fellow players.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe pressure with Andy was tremendous, and the criticism that went with it was huge,\xe2\x80\x9d Mauresmo said. \xe2\x80\x9cI knew I had a lot to prove, and I knew that every match he would play would be about the job I\xe2\x80\x99d done, or not done, or could do better. That was making it pretty difficult, but pretty challenging as well, and I worked really, really hard.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Pouille said many of the queries that came with his choice were more inane than negative.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cA lot of people have asked me: \xe2\x80\x98Is it different that she\xe2\x80\x99s a woman? What do you do \xe2\x80\x94 can she come in the locker room?\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut what is important is what\xe2\x80\x99s happening on court, what\xe2\x80\x99s happening to get ready for the match, and what happens after the match. I don\xe2\x80\x99t care who is in the locker room.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Pouille said that, for now, he appreciated the lack of wasted time in his practice sessions with Mauresmo, and also her drive and willingness to join him in his various fitness and running drills.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou can see on the court that she\xe2\x80\x99s a champion,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe way she is on the court, the way she\xe2\x80\x99s committed to it, it\xe2\x80\x99s just remarkable.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Pouille is hoping that Mauresmo\xe2\x80\x99s coaching can help him return to the top 10. Over the past three decades, French men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis has packed the sport\xe2\x80\x99s peloton, but it has struggled to catapult anyone into regular championship contention.'
b'Pouille is one of five active Frenchmen who can claim to have made the top 10, joining Richard Gasquet, Gilles Simon, Ga\xc3\xabl Monfils and Jo-Wilfried Tsonga. Together, they have reached only one Grand Slam final in the past decade: when Tsonga finished as the runner-up at the 2008 Australian Open.'
b'Mauresmo says she probably has particular credibility in French tennis as a two-time Grand Slam singles champion and a former No. 1 player, accomplishments that outshine those of all the country\xe2\x80\x99s other players \xe2\x80\x94 male or female \xe2\x80\x94 in her lifetime. But she is uncertain whether most men would be ready to hire a woman with less than hall-of-fame credentials.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cProbably not yet,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cMaybe not, but it will come. Maybe not in the next two, three, five years, but it will come.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Patience also was required as Pouille started his 2019 season. He opened the year by losing all three matches he played at the Hopman Cup, as well as another at the ATP tournament in Sydney. b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 When Andy Murray announced that he planned to retire from tennis this year because of chronic hip pain, the news generated the expected plaudits and empathy from the rivals who had shared a locker room with him for years.'
b'The most distinct voices in the chorus of praise, however, were female.
