b'By Ben Rothenberg'
b'PERTH, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 When Serena Williams and Roger Federer played against each other for the first time, on Tuesday night at the Hopman Cup, it was the ultimate expression of an event that has brought the best men and best women in tennis together for more than three decades.'
b'But despite the power of seeing Williams and Federer on opposite sides of the net, the future of the Hopman Cup is uncertain, with a new men\xe2\x80\x99s team event set to eclipse it, part of a trend of realignment and reinvention in tennis. Tennis Australia, which manages the Hopman Cup, will next year help organize the ATP Cup, a 10-day tournament that will have men\xe2\x80\x99s teams from 24 countries competing across three Australian cities for ranking points and $15 million in prize money.'
b'With mixed doubles increasingly outstripped in prize money and prestige at Grand Slam events, the Hopman Cup \xe2\x80\x94 with two-person teams from eight countries competing in singles and mixed doubles \xe2\x80\x94 is the lone place to see top men and top women team up besides the Olympics.'
b'Though Federer did not participate in the Hopman Cup through the middle years of his career, he has a long attachment to the event, first coming to Perth as a hitting partner in 1999. He won the tournament with Martina Hingis in 2001 about a month before taking his first title on the ATP Tour. At the next Hopman Cup, he partnered with his future wife, Mirka Vavrinec.'
b'[Read: Roger Federer struggles with Serena Williams\xe2\x80\x99s serve. And vice versa.]'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMen and women, we share a lot of tournaments together, but it\xe2\x80\x99s not the same as when you play each other or share the same court,\xe2\x80\x9d Federer said. \xe2\x80\x9cSo I think the players have always enjoyed this event.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Hopman Cup\xe2\x80\x99s distinction as a mixed event stands in contrast to the trend of new team tennis concepts for men only. Tennis Australia has taken an aggressive role in event creation, cofounding the men-only Laver Cup and the ATP Cup in recent years.'
b'That focus on men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis could doom the coed Hopman Cup. The host cities for the ATP Cup have not yet been announced, but the state-of-the-art Perth Arena, where the Hopman Cup has been held since 2013, is a likely choice. Even if Perth is not chosen, it would be difficult to imagine Tennis Australia hosting two competing team events in the same week.'
b'The Hopman Cup remains an oddity in its 31st year, at once a playful exhibition that serves as a relaxing lead-up to the Australian Open and, since 1997, an officially sanctioned International Tennis Federation event.'
b'The tournament has been bankrolled by the Western Australian government\xe2\x80\x99s tourism body, Tourism W.A. Player appearance contracts have included clauses forbidding them from criticizing Perth, and at times the programming can feel like an infomercial for the region. After his first match at this year\xe2\x80\x99s tournament, Federer gave an on-court interview that centered on his appreciation for the region and a photo shoot at a scenic rock formation nearby.'
b'Among locals, the main concern is less about preserving the Hopman Cup and more about making sure that isolated Perth, which is 1,300 miles from another city of more than 100,000 people, keeps a foothold in tennis and is not left out of the pre-Australian Open swing.'
b'In the wider tennis community, the Hopman Cup\xe2\x80\x99s uniqueness is appreciated. It has rarely sparked the tribal passions on which Davis Cup prides itself, but the Hopman Cup has been a crowd-pleasing event, cherished by tennis fans who have savored the opportunity to see the sport\xe2\x80\x99s top women and top men compete and commingle.'
b'The New Year\xe2\x80\x99s Day battle of Williams and Frances Tiafoe against Federer and Belinda Bencic represented an apex of many captivating Hopman Cup combinations. Marat Safin and Dinara Safina, the only brother-sister pair to both reach the No. 1 ranking, played together for Russia in 2009. Boris Becker and Steffi Graf played together in 1992 for the only time in their careers, a pairing of stars so sought after that a German television station helped the tournament organizers pay the players\xe2\x80\x99 appearance fees.'
b'The tournament has also featured some irresistible matchups of men\xe2\x80\x99s and women\xe2\x80\x99s stars who would never otherwise intersect. In the 2011 final, the 5-foot-5 Justine Henin tried to return the booming serve of the 6-foot-10 John Isner.'
b'Not everyone is ready to write an obituary for the event, though. David Haggerty, president of the I.T.F., which sanctions the Hopman Cup as its official mixed team competition, said the event was \xe2\x80\x9cvery, very important and should continue.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Haggerty said he expected Tennis Australia to honor its remaining contractual obligations for managing the Hopman Cup in the first week of the season, which run through 2022.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re just excited to continue to see Hopman Cup through because it is a great way to have the men and women playing,\xe2\x80\x9d said Haggerty, who spearheaded a massive overhaul of the Davis Cup format last year despite strong resistance from governing bodies, including Tennis Australia.'
b'If Saturday\xe2\x80\x99s final was the event\xe2\x80\x99s last gasp, it had a breathtaking finish, with Federer and Bencic prevailing in an 18-shot rally on a winner-take-all final point against Alexander Zverev and Angelique Kerber, clinching a second straight title for the Swiss pair.'
b'Tennis Australia\xe2\x80\x99s Paul Kilderry, who serves as the Hopman Cup\xe2\x80\x99s tournament director, declined to comment for this article, citing uncertainty about the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s future.'
b'As Haggerty expressed reason for the Hopman Cup to endure, Ross Hutchins, the ATP vice president for player relations, was scouting Perth Arena as a potential venue for the ATP Cup, for which he will be managing director. Hutchins is also visiting Adelaide, Brisbane and Sydney, which all have existing tennis facilities.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cUltimately we thought this time of year, leading into a Grand Slam, is important to do something major in, and that\xe2\x80\x99s what we will target,\xe2\x80\x9d Hutchins said. \xe2\x80\x9cThis event will be a major event on the ATP Tour.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The ATP Cup is landing in a jam-packed first week of the tennis season, which this year has seven tournaments: the Hopman Cup; WTA tournaments in Auckland, New Zealand, and Shenzhen, China; ATP tournaments in Doha, Qatar, and Pune, India; and a combined ATP-WTA tournament in Brisbane. Hutchins said only one of the ATP events would remain on the schedule as a complement to the ATP Cup, with no survivor yet designated.'
b'The ATP is eager to add more events that it will own outright. The ATP Cup will be the third new annual men\xe2\x80\x99s team event introduced since 2017. The Federer-backed Laver Cup, which pits a European team against one from the rest of the world, is held in September. The reworked 18-country Davis Cup will culminate in November. Hutchins said he thought there was room for all three to flourish.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think there is a fatigue of team events because it\xe2\x80\x99s not something that we think is diluted, and they\xe2\x80\x99re all slightly different,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'But there is nothing quite like the Hopman Cup on the horizon. Without any fixed plans for the event\xe2\x80\x99s end or its continuation, players and organizers at this year\xe2\x80\x99s tournament participated with a mixture of wistfulness and confusion.'
b'In the afterglow of her match with Federer, Williams was caught off-guard by a question about the Hopman Cup\xe2\x80\x99s probable demise. \xe2\x80\x9cOh, really? I never heard that,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt would be heartbreaking.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 As the tennis world was transfixed on Andy Murray  as he played what may have been the final match of his career last Monday night, another drama was beginning in Interview Room 2 at the Australian Open.'
b'After a first-round loss, Australia\xe2\x80\x99s Bernard Tomic launched the opening volley in an off-court rift between Lleyton Hewitt and some of the top male players in Australian tennis, a conflict that kept heads turning and eyes rolling throughout the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s first week.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m going to say it honestly: No one likes him anymore,\xe2\x80\x9d Tomic said of Hewitt, the country\xe2\x80\x99s most successful men\xe2\x80\x99s player in the past 20 years and the current Davis Cup captain.'
b'Australian men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis was a dominant force in the sport in the 1950s and 1960s, producing players who won 52 of the 80 Grand Slam singles titles in that span. Hewitt arrived on the scene many years later and in the early 2000s, finished two seasons at No. 1 and captured two Grand Slam titles.'
b'But ever since Hewitt fell out of the top tier in 2006, Australia has not had a male Grand Slam singles champion or a top-10 men\xe2\x80\x99s player. Instead, men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis in the country has now become a soap opera, more memorable for its spats than its results on the court.'
b'At this Open, every Australian man fell out of the tournament after just six days. It meant that the host country had failed to have a representative in the second week of men\xe2\x80\x99s singles for the eighth time in the past 13 years. Meanwhile, an Australian woman, 15th-seeded Ashleigh Barty, plays on into the quarterfinals, her mellow and modest manner perhaps making up for the men\xe2\x80\x99s maddening mayhem.'
b'And a lot of that mayhem has to do with Hewitt, who retired with considerable fanfare at the 2016 Australian Open and segued into a new role as the Davis Cup captain. But his debut in that role was dominated by infighting, with Tomic, in a midmatch rant to Hewitt, accusing his teammate Nick Kyrgios of faking an illness. Hewitt, in turn, failed to quell Tomic\xe2\x80\x99s ire.'
b'Last Monday, Tomic accused Hewitt of a litany of misdeeds as Davis Cup captain, including giving preferential treatment to players with whom he had management deals and continuing to play doubles tournaments and in the Davis Cup as well.'
b'Tomic said he and others did not want to play Davis Cup anymore because Hewitt \xe2\x80\x9chas ruined the system.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cGo away,\xe2\x80\x9d he added. \xe2\x80\x9cLiterally, if he is retired, why is he still in tennis? Why do you play these doubles tournaments?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Hewitt entered the men\xe2\x80\x99s doubles events in Brisbane, Sydney and the Australian Open this month.'
b'Rather than defuse the flames, Hewitt fanned them in his own extraordinary news conference after his loss in Melbourne on Thursday night. He accused Tomic of unspecified threats and \xe2\x80\x9cblackmail\xe2\x80\x9d against him and his family, essentially giving up any hope of working with Tomic again.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re trying to set cultural standards for the Davis Cup and representing Australia; he hasn\xe2\x80\x99t really been close to those in the last couple of years,\xe2\x80\x9d Hewitt said.'
b'Hewitt said that Tomic \xe2\x80\x9cwon\xe2\x80\x99t play Davis Cup while I have anything to do with it,\xe2\x80\x9d but that his relationship with Kyrgios, another controversy-prone Australian, was \xe2\x80\x9csalvageable.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAll I want guys to do is to commit to the sport and work hard, to want to play for Australia,\xe2\x80\x9d Hewitt said. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think that\xe2\x80\x99s too much to ask.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Tomic, 26, and Kyrgios, 23, were junior Grand Slam champions and undeniable talents whose professional careers have been a mix of bright spots and bad moments, with both players seeming to relish the chance to challenge the idealistic Australian notion as to how a sportsman should conduct himself.'
b'Kyrgios, who also lost in the first round of this tournament, mostly mocked the questions he received about Tomic and Hewitt in his post-match news conference last Tuesday. He did not pick a side.'
b'But it was clear Kyrgios also had soured on Hewitt after he posted a picture on Instagram on Wednesday of Hewitt watching Alex de Minaur, the recent Sydney champion who has become his prot\xc3\xa9g\xc3\xa9, and implying that Hewitt would not be watching any other Australian player.'
b'Hewitt, 37, responded by saying Kyrgios\xe2\x80\x99s post was \xe2\x80\x9cone of the standards we can\xe2\x80\x99t put up with.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cJust for the culture of Australian tennis moving forward, can\xe2\x80\x99t do it,\xe2\x80\x9d Hewitt added. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think it\xe2\x80\x99s a good look. I\xe2\x80\x99ve spoken to Nick about it. He understands that. Whether he learns from it, that\xe2\x80\x99s another thing.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'On Sunday, Kyrgios posted a photo of himself with de Minaur on Twitter, seeming to clarify that any bad blood is strictly intergenerational.'
b'De Minaur, 19, is currently the highest-ranked Australian man, at No. 29. He has a game built on dazzling defense, with some of the flashiest footwork on tour. Increasingly, he is presented as a golden boy of the sport in contrast to the ne\xe2\x80\x99er-do-wells Tomic and Kyrgios. De Minaur is so committed to playing for Australia that he has \xe2\x80\x9c109\xe2\x80\x9d tattooed on his chest because he was the 109th player to represent the country in Davis Cup.'
b'As all of this was playing out, Matt Dwyer, the chief tennis officer of Tennis Australia, got involved, too, issuing a statement on Friday that highlighted de Minaur, Alex Bolt and 19-year-old Alexei Popyrin, all of whom made the third round here, and praising \xe2\x80\x9ceach player\xe2\x80\x99s unwavering passion to compete and their genuine love of the game, all underpinned by the Tennis Australia values of excellence, loyalty, teamwork and humility.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSupport and opportunities will be offered to players who live these values and demonstrate the commitment to maximize their potential, with our ultimate ambition being to develop and foster athletes we can all be proud of,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 the statement added.'
b'The statement did not mention Tomic and Kyrgios.'
b'Other talented Australian boys have fallen short in recent years. Omar Jasika, who won the 2014 United States Open in boys\xe2\x80\x99 singles and doubles, received a two-year ban last year after testing positive for cocaine.'
b'Oliver Anderson, the 2016 Australian Open boys\xe2\x80\x99 singles champion, served a 19-month provisional suspension for match-fixing for deliberately losing a set in a 2017 match.'
b'There has also been recent tragedy: Todd Reid, the 2002 Wimbledon boys\xe2\x80\x99 singles champion, died in October at 34.'
b'Asked if he was uncomfortable with the good-kids-versus-bad-kids narrative that predominates Australian men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis, de Minaur demurred.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a lot of stuff that happens off court, but I think at the end of the day what I really want is to be that boring guy that lets his tennis do the talking, you know?\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI want everyone to know that I\xe2\x80\x99m that kid that\xe2\x80\x99s going to leave it all out there, fight till the end, and just continuously want to improve. If I\xe2\x80\x99m that boring guy in the media, then I\xe2\x80\x99m doing something right.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'De Minaur has been able to stay away from the fray by making his base in Alicante, Spain. After soundly beating de Minaur in the third round, Rafael Nadal said he wished Tomic and Hewitt could learn from de Minaur\xe2\x80\x99s aversion to advertising adversity.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWill be more normal if they sit and they talk,\xe2\x80\x9d Nadal said, \xe2\x80\x9cmore than do this thing here in the media.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As Hewitt lurched toward the end of a news conference that John McEnroe described as \xe2\x80\x9cpouring gasoline on the fire,\xe2\x80\x9d he did not deny that there was toxicity in the men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis culture in Australia. But he insisted that there were good stories, too, including John Millman\xe2\x80\x99s upset of Roger Federer at the 2018 United States Open'

b'Supported by'
b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'Difficult as it might be to remember at this time-is-money stage in tennis, the sport once had no tiebreakers.'
b'Long ago, every set had to be won by a two-game margin and theoretically had no finish line. Which meant that at Wimbledon in the first round of the men\xe2\x80\x99s singles in 1969, the great but aging Pancho Gonzales defeated Charlie Pasarell by the score of 22-24, 1-6, 16-14, 6-3, 11-9 in a two-day match that lasted five hours and 12 minutes.'
b'The tiebreaker was introduced to Grand Slam tennis the following year at the 1970 United States Open, with red flags being flown courtside whenever a set reached 6-6.'
b'It has taken 49 more years for the major tournaments to reach the awkward phase where all four use different methods to resolve deciding sets in singles.'
b'The red flags are long gone, but the novelty effect is back. The Australian Open, which begins on Monday, will use a best-of-18-point tiebreaker at 6-6 in deciding sets, which are third sets for the women and fifth sets for the men.'
b'Later this year, Wimbledon will introduce a conventional best-of-12-point tiebreaker at 12-12. That will leave the French Open as the only Grand Slam tournament that uses no deciding-set tiebreaker in singles.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think the International Tennis Federation, the ATP and the Grand Slams should find, more or less, some consistency of the rules for the understanding of the public,\xe2\x80\x9d Guy Forget, the French Open tournament director, said in an interview. Consistency and mutual understanding seem particularly elusive at this fractious stage of the game.'
b'The Grand Slam leaders meet regularly and have usually made a big effort to project unity in the last 30 years as their tournaments have grown and prospered. But they have squabbled much more often lately.'
b'There have been disputes about the possible introduction of in-match coaching, which Wimbledon\xe2\x80\x99s leadership continues to oppose. There have been disagreements about the new Laver Cup team event, which the Australian Open and U.S. Open are formally backing.'
b'It seems symbolic that, with the Australian Open\xe2\x80\x99s switch from Wilson to Dunlop, each of the four Grand Slam tournaments is using balls manufactured by a different company this year.'
b'Breaking ranks over tiebreakers is the latest sign of the times, even if it hardly seems a major offense.'
b'Other sports also lack consensus. Consider men\xe2\x80\x99s golf, which has four majors of its own and four ways of resolving ties at the top of the leaderboard after 72 holes.'
b'Despite any confusion, fans still seem quite capable of enjoying golf. Tennis fans surely will end up feeling the same even if tiebreakers in their sport are a great deal more common than golf playoffs.'
b'Top tennis players had best remain alert, however.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m O.K. with any format, really,\xe2\x80\x9d said Roger Federer, the Swiss superstar who remains a traditionalist on some fronts, including in-match coaching. \xe2\x80\x9cThe funny thing is we have different formats now in four different Slams, so it\xe2\x80\x99s just important to remind yourself when you do get to 6-all in the fifth, what\xe2\x80\x99s going on here now? Do you remember which one it is?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'For women, that internal dialogue will come at 6-all in the third set even if there has been little concern about the length of Grand Slam women\xe2\x80\x99s matches, which are all best-of-three sets.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was enjoying it, because you have to go far, and you don\xe2\x80\x99t know how the score will be at the end,\xe2\x80\x9d said Angelique Kerber, who lost a taut Australian Open semifinal to Simona Halep last year 6-3, 4-6, 9-7. \xe2\x80\x9cI will miss it, for sure, but I don\xe2\x80\x99t know if it\xe2\x80\x99s a good or a bad rule change. We will see.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'One wonders what Jimmy Van Alen would think of it all. It was Van Alen, a wealthy American, who pushed for brisker, innovative formats \xe2\x80\x94 including the tiebreaker \xe2\x80\x94 in the 1960s. Van Alen, a former play who died in 1991, was also one of the driving forces in creating the International Tennis Hall of Fame in Newport, R.I.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cJimmy Van Alen would not have liked the confusion of different ways of concluding matches at the four Grand Slam events,\xe2\x80\x9d said Steve Flink, an American tennis historian who met Van Alen several times.'
b'Van Alen\xe2\x80\x99s idea of a sudden-death tiebreaker managed to change the game in earnest \xe2\x80\x94 a best-of-nine-point duel with a winner-take-all point at 4-4, which in a decisive set could give both players a match point simultaneously.'
b'This was the tiebreaker the U.S. Open adopted for all sets in 1970 at 6-6 but abandoned in 1975 in favor of the best-of-12-point tiebreaker that had to be won by two and seemed, to the players, less of a lottery. Wimbledon embraced the best-of-12-point tiebreaker in 1971, but chose to use it at 8-8 instead of 6-6.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI guess tennis has always had some inexplicable inconsistencies with formats and scoring systems,\xe2\x80\x9d Flink said.'
b'Wimbledon maintained its scoring system until 1979, when it opted for tiebreakers at 6-6, waiting 40 years before adopting a decisive-set tiebreaker at 12-12 after last year\xe2\x80\x99s semifinal between Kevin Anderson and John Isner (Anderson finally won, 26-24, in the fifth set on Centre Court, disrupting the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s schedule).'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI know Jimmy Van Alen was dismayed when his original sudden death nine-point tiebreaker was discarded,\xe2\x80\x9d Flink said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I have no doubt he would have preferred the Australian Open fifth-set tiebreaker to what Wimbledon is doing. Waiting until 12-12 in the fifth would not have suited him at all.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But for this year at least, the French Open remains the last Grand Slam holdout, a decision Forget said came about because, unlike Wimbledon, the French Open had not had an ultramarathon final set in recent seasons.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe will not go with the tiebreak for now,\xe2\x80\x9d Forget said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I hope personally that our sport will adopt new rules in the future as we need to modernize our game a bit.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ben Rothenberg contributed reporting.'

b"Garin remained dominant on serve in the second set, winning 16 of 19 service points as Querrey's forehand failed him."

b'The Chilean made his first ATP Tour final last month at the Brasil Open and is projected to move inside the top 50 if he wins on Sunday.'

b"(Reuters) - Former champion Marcel Granollers used the drop shot to good effect as he surprised fifth-seeded American Taylor Fritz in three sets at the U.S. Men's Clay Court Championship in Houston on Monday."
b'The 32-year-old Spaniard claimed a 6-2 4-6 6-2 victory over Fritz, the only seeded player in first round action at the River Oaks Country Club.'
b'"Taylor is a player who can hit very hard. He hits very hard from the baseline and I needed to change rhythm," said Granollers, who won the tournament in 2008.'
b'"If I hit good drop shots, I think it\xe2\x80\x99s a good option against him and I think today it worked."'
b'Granollers reeled off three consecutive games, including a break at 5-2, to claim the opening set.'
b'World number 58 Fritz bounced back in the second, surging ahead after Granollers had tied the set at 4-4.'
b'The deciding set was all Granollers after Fritz, the 2018 semi-finalist, took the opening game.'
b'Granollers won five consecutive games before Fritz held at 5-2.'

b'By Ben Rothenberg'
b'PERTH, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 After nearly two decades of appearing alongside each other on billboards and in record books, Serena Williams and Roger Federer faced off across a tennis court for the first time on Tuesday.'
b'The incandescent stars, now both 37, finally aligned for the first time by taking part in a mixed doubles match between the United States and Switzerland at the Hopman Cup team event.'
b'On the opening point, Williams pulled Federer wide to his forehand side with a sharply angled volley, then sent a smash toward the opposite corner that he could not reach in time to send back. Long exchanges between the two proved few, however, with each using their serve to effectively neutralize the other.'
b'It did not seem to matter to the crowd of 14,064 in Perth Arena, the highest single-session attendance in the event\xe2\x80\x99s 31-year history, and Williams and Federer clearly delighted in the chance to hit the ball around with each other a couple of weeks before more serious play occurs at the Australian Open.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was a great experience,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams said as she joined Federer on court after the match. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m kind of sad it\xe2\x80\x99s over. It was just warming up.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Federer and his partner, Belinda Bencic, beat Williams and Frances Tiafoe in an abbreviated format match by the score of 4-2, 4-3 (5-3) in 46 minutes.'
b'Despite the initial, promising exchange in the first set, Williams and Federer seemed to settle into more conservative play; in the entire first set, neither Federer nor Williams succeeded in making a single return off the other\xe2\x80\x99s serve.'
b'(There were, technically, two other people on the court as well. Bencic hit a pivotal return winner off Tiafoe\xe2\x80\x99s serve that helped Switzerland take the lead in the first set.)'
b'Federer and Williams both gained more of a foothold on the other\xe2\x80\x99s serve in the second set, which was highlighted by a six-shot exchange of powerful cross-court groundstrokes between the two before Federer won the point by ripping a forehand toward Tiafoe.'
b'Williams and Federer afterward sized each other up.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was nervous returning, because you just don\xe2\x80\x99t know,\xe2\x80\x9d Federer said. \xe2\x80\x9cPeople talk about her serve so much, and I see why it is such a wonderful serve, because you just can\xe2\x80\x99t read it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t read yours either,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams interjected, laughing.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have the same qualities, you know?\xe2\x80\x9d Federer said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYours is a bit better,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, provoking a good-natured eye roll from Williams.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was great, great fun,\xe2\x80\x9d Federer added. \xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s a great champion \xe2\x80\x94 you see how focused and determined she is \xe2\x80\x94 and I love that about her.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Williams eagerly reciprocated.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI mean, the guy is great, he\xe2\x80\x99s the greatest of all time, to be honest,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams said, drawing applause from the crowd (Williams has said she doubted she could beat Federer in a singles match).'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe has a killer serve,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cLiterally, you can\xe2\x80\x99t read it, and there\xe2\x80\x99s a reason why he\xe2\x80\x99s the greatest, because you can\xe2\x80\x99t be that great and not have an awesome weapon like that serve.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That Williams\xe2\x80\x99s serve would prove daunting to one of the best men\xe2\x80\x99s players is no surprise, especially one day after she had sent a clean ace past the reach of 6-foot 4-inch Stefanos Tsitsipas in a mixed doubles match.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLike I had any chance of returning that one,\xe2\x80\x9d Tsitsipas wrote on Twitter, replying to an image of the serve spinning well beyond his reach.'
b'After Williams insisted that they hold rackets during an on-court selfie, she and Federer walked back to their seats with their arms wrapped around each other, and Federer said his racket was hers to keep.'
b'As she carried it into the players\xe2\x80\x99 area of Perth Arena alongside Tiafoe, Williams stared at the racket with visible wonderment, showing it to her partner and letting him hold it briefly.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was so excited,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams told reporters. \xe2\x80\x9cLiterally, it was the match of my career. I don\xe2\x80\x99t know, just playing someone so great, and someone that you admire so much \xe2\x80\x94 and a match that actually means something. It\xe2\x80\x99s not often that that happens.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The mixed doubles win gave the tie to Switzerland, who are the defending champions after Federer and Bencic won the competition last year. Switzerland will qualify for Saturday\xe2\x80\x99s final if it beats Greece on Thursday in Group B. The United States, which lost to Greece on Monday, can not advance.'
b'Williams, meanwhile, expressed mild disappointment at her play, especially considering her superior doubles pedigree of 16 Grand Slam titles to Federer\xe2\x80\x99s none.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m the one that won those doubles Grand Slams, but it didn\xe2\x80\x99t look like it,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Williams said she had been tempted to bring her 16-month old daughter, Olympia, to the match. She ultimately decided against that, settling for having an unforgettable story to tell her.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMen and women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis just don\xe2\x80\x99t compete against each other,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cSo it\xe2\x80\x99s just really great and special to go against the greatest of all time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After this summit of superstars, Federer could tell his children the same thing.'

b'On Tennis'
b'By Kurt Streeter'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 The last time Serena Williams came here for the Australian Open, in 2017, the talk swirling around her focused on tennis. Could she capture her 23rd major title and break past Steffi Graf on the list of Grand Slam title winners since the sport went professional?'
b'She did indeed emerge victorious, beating her sister Venus in the final and doing so, she would later reveal to the world, while in the early stages of pregnancy.'
b'On Tuesday, Williams returns to the sunbaked Melbourne courts, with her 16-month-old daughter in tow, bidding for another place in the record books. This time, though, her tennis is nearly an afterthought.'
b'Four months ago, in the final of the United States Open, Williams\xe2\x80\x99s most compelling moments came during angry outbursts against the umpire that won both praise and criticism, propelling an already epochal athlete to the very forefront of debates about sports and gender, race and power.'
b'That flare-up is still being frequently discussed as the Australian Open begins this week, though Williams herself is not expected to speak to reporters before she plays.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSerena has actually expanded her presence in people\xe2\x80\x99s lives,\xe2\x80\x9d Delia Douglas, a Canadian sociologist who studies women in athletics, said in an interview. \xe2\x80\x9cThe way people talk about her, the way people debate her and what she stands for, is now heightened.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Her tennis is certainly still part of the discussion.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe all know Serena is very dangerous when she\xe2\x80\x99s fit and when she\xe2\x80\x99s healthy,\xe2\x80\x9d said Chris Evert, the former world No. 1 who is now an analyst for ESPN.'
b'But just as many, if not more, focus on what Williams means.'
b'As Soraya Chemaly, a prominent feminist activist and social critic, explained: She fits perfectly in these times, \xe2\x80\x9cwhen so much of what is happening in our world is related to gender and race and power. And right now, you can see it. Serena is sitting at that nexus, at the very intersection of all these important social conversations.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The powerful combination of her celebrity, the internet and social media amplifies the discussion each year she continues to play, threatening to overshadow the tournaments she plays in.'
b'The last time she played the Australian Open, she was pregnant. Eight months later, she nearly died during childbirth. She named her baby girl Alexis Olympia. Months afterward, she married her daughter\xe2\x80\x99s father, Alexis Ohanian, a co-founder of the popular website Reddit.'
b'Williams, same as ever, did not shy from attention \xe2\x80\x94 or from making a point. She shared her story publicly and said she was experiencing the same troubles faced by many other mothers. In her first Grand Slam tournament after childbirth, the 2018 French Open, she was not in shape, and she withdrew with an injury in the fourth round. She wore a sleek, black, full-body tennis suit. It was part fashion statement, part medical necessity \xe2\x80\x94 it reduced the chances of a recurrence of blood clots she experienced during childbirth.'
b'But the \xe2\x80\x9ccat suit,\xe2\x80\x9d as it came to be called, was so controversial that French tennis officials discussed banning outfits like it from Roland Garros in the future. (As a countermove, the WTA, which governs the women\xe2\x80\x99s tour apart from the Grand Slams, clarified its rules to allow compression garments to be worn without skirts or dresses over them.)'
b'Undeterred, Williams spoke pointedly at Wimbledon about protecting rights of new mothers \xe2\x80\x94 on the tour and in the workplace. She marched through the draw. But, still out of shape, she lost in the final. A few weeks later, she withdrew from the Rogers Cup in Montreal, eventually citing postpartum depression, a condition that afflicts about 15 percent of all mothers but is often dogged by stigma.'
b'Then came the United States Open.'
b'Nobody here in Melbourne has forgotten what happened during the women\xe2\x80\x99s singles final. Carlos Ramos, the umpire, spotted Williams\xe2\x80\x99s coach motioning at her to be more aggressive. Ramos warned about a coaching infraction. Williams shouted with an angry, unyielding insistence that she had done nothing wrong, that she would never cheat.'
b'Nobody has forgotten the smashed racket, the point deducted as a penalty, her continued shouting: \xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99re a thief,\xe2\x80\x9d she defiantly yelled at Ramos.'
b'Nor has anybody forgotten the game taken away as another penalty, Williams\xe2\x80\x99s assertion that male players often behave badly and get away with it, the booing and the tumult, and finally her surprising loss to Naomi Osaka, a rising star who may threaten her again in this tournament.'
b'Admirers praised Williams for showing courage, for being willing to stand up to a man, for being a black woman ready to argue her point in front of everyone, for enduring long years of racial slights, for engaging boldly nonetheless \xe2\x80\x94 and for never losing any of her fire. (A cartoon with racist imagery lampooning Williams in an Australian newspaper shortly after the U.S. Open was yet another reminder of those slights.)'
b'Critics saw her as unhinged. This had nothing to do with womanhood or being African-American, they said. To them, she had behaved like a spoiled and raving maniac. More than that, they claimed, she had obscured the performance of a lifetime by Osaka, who had played remarkably from the start.'
b'But who could be surprised that Osaka got short shrift? Win or lose, the talk is almost always about Serena.'
b'Chemaly, the social critic, noted how, during a tour for her new book, \xe2\x80\x9cRage Becomes Her,\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cpeople kept bringing up Serena.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The book urges women to be unafraid of showing rightful anger.'
b'Chemaly said she had been asked: \xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98What do you think of Serena Williams?\xe2\x80\x99 \xe2\x80\x98What does she mean for this moment?\xe2\x80\x99 \xe2\x80\x98How would you compare what happened at the U.S. Open to Brett Kavanaugh\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d and the anger he displayed before a Congressional panel?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPeople really want to think about what it means,\xe2\x80\x9d Chemaly said.'
b'During 2018, Williams, 37, went without a major title for the first time since 2011 (she skipped the Australian Open in 2018, still recovering from giving birth in September 2017), and she did not play another tournament after the U.S. Open.'
b'But this is a new year. Based on her play during a string of exhibition matches in Perth \xe2\x80\x94 where fans greeted her warmly \xe2\x80\x94 and during practices this week in Melbourne, she looks primed to win again.'
b'If she does, she\xe2\x80\x99ll have achieved yet another milestone: a 24th major singles title, tying the former Australian great Margaret Court, whose Grand Slam championships came in both the amateur and professional eras.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cShe seems fitter than last year,\xe2\x80\x9d Evert said of Williams. \xe2\x80\x9cThe scary thought, looking at the women \xe2\x80\x94 they have to be thinking at this point, \xe2\x80\x98Gosh, she was 60-70 percent last year, reaching two Grand Slam finals. And now she seems fitter, leaner. She\xe2\x80\x99s moving better. She\xe2\x80\x99s fresher.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'People are talking. \xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s so controversial now, everyone here will be paying close attention to that first match,\xe2\x80\x9d one local fan, Jess Stow, 34, said, echoing a commonly heard sentiment as she walked with her 2-year-old son near the Australian Open grounds a day before play was set to begin. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat will she end up saying?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But so far Williams hasn\xe2\x80\x99t said much. In Perth, she avoided discussion of the U.S. Open partly by keeping her news briefing to just a few minutes.'
b'She did tell GQ Magazine in November that Ramos, the umpire at the U.S. Open, should have defused the contretemps by telling her about the signals from her coach before punishing her. It would have let her set things straight without the penalty, she said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTell me that something\xe2\x80\x99s happening,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, and she would tell her coaching box, \xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98Whatever you\xe2\x80\x99re doing, don\xe2\x80\x99t.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Otherwise, she has held her peace in Melbourne. Her racket may offer her most meaningful reply.'

b'By Cindy Shmerler'
b'DELRAY BEACH, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 As Radu Albot became the first player from Moldova to win an ATP title on Sunday, his small home country in Eastern Europe was holding parliamentary elections.'
b'Unlike four years ago, when he was in France for a tennis tournament and spent about $200 on a taxi to the Moldovan Embassy so he could cast a ballot, Albot said he could not make his way to a voting booth on Sunday.'
b'This time, he was busy in the Delray Beach Open final, where he held off Dan Evans to capture the title, 3-6, 6-3, 7-6 (7), and earn $97,490, the biggest payday of his career.'
b'Albot, 29, has been on tour for more than a decade but is only now hitting his stride. Entering the Delray Beach Open he was ranked No. 82 in the world, just off his career high of No. 81, set nearly two years ago. With the win over Evans, in which he saved three match points, Albot moved to a new career high of No. 52.'
b'Albot is the first player, man or woman, from Moldova to be ranked within the world\xe2\x80\x99s top 100. Most have never broken the top 300.'
b'Moldova, a former Soviet republic with a population of 3.55 million, is better known for producing wine than tennis players. It has, however, had its share of Olympic wrestlers, Nordic skiers and soccer players. Natalia Levchenkova placed eighth in biathlon at the 2006 Winter Olympics.'
b'At the 2016 Summer Games in Rio de Janeiro, 23 Moldovan athletes competed, including Albot, the country\xe2\x80\x99s first Olympic tennis player. He beat Teymuraz Gabashvili of Russia in the first round before losing to Marin Cilic of Croatia. In those Games, one Moldovan, a flat-water canoeist named Oleg Tarnovschi, won the country\xe2\x80\x99s only medal, a bronze that was later stripped because he violated antidoping rules.'
b'The next-highest-ranked male player from Moldova, the 36-year-old Roman Borvanov, reached No. 200 back in 2011. Now a teaching pro near Miami, he was in Albot\xe2\x80\x99s players\xe2\x80\x99 box cheering for his countryman on Sunday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn a way, coming from this country, the results I\xe2\x80\x99ve had, it\xe2\x80\x99s a miracle,\xe2\x80\x9d Albot said. Unlike players in countries that host a Grand Slam and have a history of producing star players, he said, he had no Pete Sampras or Andre Agassi in front of him as role models and challenges.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThen you have a goal, you want to be as them,\xe2\x80\x9d Albot said. \xe2\x80\x9cMe, growing up, I had nobody ahead of me except the guy ranked 200. I wanted to be as him, better than him. But as soon as I got to 190, then what? I didn\xe2\x80\x99t know how to go higher. I didn\xe2\x80\x99t have someone to ask how to get there, to go to for advice. I had to build my game by myself.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'When Albot was 6, his father, Vladimir, saw a tennis match on television and decided he wanted his only child to play the sport. Vladimir Albot was able to arrange for his son to train at a school that specialized in tennis \xe2\x80\x94 a government-funded academy near the family\xe2\x80\x99s home in Chisinau, the Moldovan capital. The club has eight outdoor red-clay courts and two indoor courts. Until recently, those courts were made of wooden planks, but they have been converted to a hardcourt surface.'
b'Though his parents were of modest means \xe2\x80\x94 Radu still lives with them in the two-room apartment they own \xe2\x80\x94 Vladimir traveled with Radu to junior tournaments while his mother, Svetlana, stayed home to work in her dental therapy practice. Vladimir sold some property he owned to fund his son\xe2\x80\x99s travel.'
b'Rather than spend money on hotel rooms, the pair would often sleep on mattresses inside gyms connected to the clubs where Radu competed, Albot said. Whenever Radu was offered a chance to share a room with another competitor, his father would pitch a tent for himself in the tournament parking lot.'

b'At 13, Albot was playing in Germany, and he met Jimmy Oganezov, a local businessman from the former Soviet Republic of Georgia who had become a tennis coach. That summer turned into more than a dozen summers, and the training convinced Albot that he could have a career as a professional tennis player.'

He will next play the Masters 1000 events in Indian Wells, Calif., and in Miami.'

b'By Cindy Shmerler'
b'MIAMI GARDENS, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 Stephen M. Ross swears he is not embroiled in a third-set tiebreaker with Larry Ellison, the billionaire co-founder of Oracle who bought the BNP Paribas Open in Indian Wells, Calif., a decade ago and transformed it into a tony desert party for tennis players and fans.'
b'Still, when the moved and improved Miami Open begins this week at Hard Rock Stadium, home of Ross\xe2\x80\x99s Miami Dolphins, it will not be hard to imagine Ross, a billionaire real estate developer, keeping a tiny scorecard in his back pocket.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLarry\xe2\x80\x99s done a great job,\xe2\x80\x9d Ross said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe set the bar high, and it\xe2\x80\x99s all great for tennis. But for us, it\xe2\x80\x99s more natural not to compete, or at least to do so in our own way.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ross, who bought the Dolphins in 2008 and spent $550 million renovating the stadium, stepped in when IMG, which owns the Miami Open, found itself at an impasse with a Key Biscayne resident who controlled the land where the tournament had been played since 1987.'
b'That man, Bruce Matheson, refused to allow $50 million worth of renovations to the Crandon Park site, and his prolonged lawsuits convinced the tournament that it was time to go.'
b'Rather than see the tournament \xe2\x80\x94 and its hundreds of millions in local revenue \xe2\x80\x94 uprooted from South Florida to Orlando or China, Ross decided to partner with IMG and move the tournament about 20 miles northwest to his football stadium. He spent an additional $72 million to transform it into a state-of-the-art tennis venue.'
b'The move wasn\xe2\x80\x99t well received by everyone.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cKey Biscayne had a very intimate setting, and you can\xe2\x80\x99t beat the drive over the Rickenbacker Causeway, with blue water on both sides of you,\xe2\x80\x9d said John Isner, the defending Miami Open champion. \xe2\x80\x9cWe had a lot of history in that place, and that stadium court will always be very special to me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'At the new site, a temporary main court was erected on the football field, with half of the seats were blocked off by screens. A 5,191-seat grandstand court, two other show courts and eight additional match courts \xe2\x80\x94 all permanent \xe2\x80\x94 were built on top of parking lots.'
b'On a recent tour, those lots were indiscernible behind purple flowers, artificial grass, 35-foot mature palm trees costing $35,000 a pop, and a giant fountain that guards one of the many entrances to the stadium. There is also a 40-by-90-foot video screen, the largest in tennis, just outside the stadium in a spot modeled after Wimbledon\xe2\x80\x99s Henman Hill, minus the grass.'
b'The change recalls the United States Open\xe2\x80\x99s move from the charming but outgrown West Side Tennis Club in Forest Hills in 1978 to the more functional, if less romantic, U.S.T.A. Billie Jean King National Tennis Center in nearby Flushing Meadows. It took a while to get used to the new digs, but no one would ever want to go back to the old ones.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis place has a much larger footprint, so we can do more things,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tom Garfinkel, the Dolphins\xe2\x80\x99 chief executive. \xe2\x80\x9cWe are giving people an unprecedented luxury experience in tennis, just like the N.F.L.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Tournament organizers did not take the word \xe2\x80\x9cluxury\xe2\x80\x9d lightly. The stadium court \xe2\x80\x94 painted in colors called Oasis Blue and Biscayne Blue \xe2\x80\x94 seats 13,800, the same as the main court in Key Biscayne. But this court features 4,738 premium seats, many that resemble Barcaloungers, with individual television screens. These seats range in price from $50,000 to $70,000 for the two-week tournament. Some are right on the court.'
b'Premium-seat packages, most of which were sold out two months before the start of the tournament, include private dining rooms. Some suites have seats made out of Ferrari leather. For a privileged 1,000 visitors, there is a dedicated entrance from a private parking lot, in which spectators pass through a tent lined with art, including works by Pablo Picasso and Andy Warhol that can be purchased for upward of $1 million.'
b'Ticket prices at every level have increased by up to 40 percent over last year, though several thousand grounds passes are available for as little as $15 each day. Sales by the end of last month were up 25 percent, thanks, in part, to Dolphins season-ticket holders who have been cajoled into watching tennis.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a bit of a challenge in giving people the confidence that this really is for the best,\xe2\x80\x9d said James Blake, the tournament director.'
b'Ross helped choose everything on the site: the flowers, the gigantic paintings that line the stadium corridors, the tiles on the bathroom walls.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI had a picture in my head of what I wanted this to look like, the same way I do my real estate deals,\xe2\x80\x9d said Ross, who is also behind Manhattan\xe2\x80\x99s Hudson Yards project. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s all in the details. Little things matter. People notice, and they\xe2\x80\x99re watching for those details.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The number of practice courts, many with spectator seating, have doubled from those at Key Biscayne, to 18. But unlike in Key Biscayne, those courts will not be turned over for the public to play on after the tournament ends.'
b'The players, at least, should be happy. Their amenities have been enhanced, with dining areas and gym spaces tripling in size. The top eight seeds in the men\xe2\x80\x99s and women\xe2\x80\x99s singles draws, as well as all former champions, will be given private suites to be used by their entourages.'
b'But organizers see the event as more than a tennis tournament. The grounds will open at least two hours before play begins each day to encourage people to come early to eat, shop and listen to concerts by local musicians.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhat we wanted was a venue that would allow us the freedom and flexibility to grow and innovate the event,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mark Shapiro, president of Endeavor, IMG\xe2\x80\x99s parent company. \xe2\x80\x9cKey Biscayne was lovely, but we simply outgrew it. What we\xe2\x80\x99ve got now is going to be supernatural, like walking through a Lollapalooza, and a tennis tournament grew out of it. b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'MIAMI GARDENS, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 By reaching the semifinals of the Miami Open, the Canadian youngsters Felix Auger-Aliassime and Denis Shapovalov achieved something that Roger Federer and John Isner never managed.'
b'Federer, for all his obvious and precocious tennis talents, never made it to this late a stage of a Masters 1000 event in singles as a teenager. Isner was still a student-athlete at the University of Georgia in his late teens.'
b'But neither Auger-Aliassime, 18, nor Shapovalov, 19, was able to make the next leap on Friday as Isner and Federer took turns holding back youth on the temporary center court at Hard Rock Stadium.'
b'Federer, 37, and Isner, 33, will now play an old-guard final on Sunday.'
b'On Friday afternoon, Isner was opportunistic in his 7-6 (3), 7-6 (4) victory against the silken Auger-Aliassime. In the evening, Federer was brilliant in his 6-2, 6-4 demolition of Shapovalov, a flashy left-hander with a one-handed backhand who grew up idolizing Federer and now has a much clearer understanding of what it is like to face him.'

b'By Motoko Rich'
b'TOKYO \xe2\x80\x94 If anyone can stir Japanese national pride at the moment, it is Naomi Osaka.'
b'The world\xe2\x80\x99s No. 1-ranked player in women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis, Ms. Osaka is among the biggest stars in Japan, splashed across television programs and advertisements for Nissan cars and Citizen watches. As a mixed-race person, she has also helped prompt a discussion about how Japanese see their country.'
b'But a looming deadline \xe2\x80\x94 Ms. Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s 22nd birthday in October \xe2\x80\x94 has raised the question of whether she can continue to represent Japan on the international tennis circuit, where she has given the country bragging rights on the world sports stage.'
b'Ms. Osaka, whose mother is Japanese and father is Haitian-American, has citizenship in both Japan and the United States. Under Japanese law, dual citizens must choose between the two nationalities by the time they turn 22.'
b'That legal clause has left fans and commentators trying to guess whether Ms. Osaka will pick citizenship in Japan, the country of her birth, or the United States, where she has lived since she was a young child.'
b'The choice facing Ms. Osaka comes as Japan is under pressure to loosen its entrenched insularity. Japan has long prized racial purity, seeing a largely homogeneous population as crucial to social cohesion. But with the country\xe2\x80\x99s population declining and employers increasingly desperate for workers, its legislature passed a law in December to admit more guest workers, starting this month.'
b'Ms. Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s case, along with the new influx of foreigners, could exert new pressure on the government to begin to bring Japanese citizenship laws in line with those in the roughly three-quarters of countries, including the United States, that allow dual citizenship.'
b'For now, though, Ms. Osaka has a decision to make. When asked by reporters which nationality she intended to choose, she responded with trademark feistiness.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m pretty sure it\xe2\x80\x99s obvious,\xe2\x80\x9d she said at a news conference following the China Open in October. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m playing for Japan. Not to be disrespectful or anything, but I don\xe2\x80\x99t really get where the conclusion that it\xe2\x80\x99s a hard choice for me or anything comes from.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Still, it might be hard to imagine Ms. Osaka giving up her American citizenship to keep playing under the Japanese flag. And in reality, she may not have to. Legal experts say the Japanese government rarely enforces the law requiring citizens to choose between nationalities.'
b'The Justice Ministry estimates that about 890,000 Japanese citizens may also hold foreign passports, and the government has never revoked Japanese citizenship from anyone who, like Ms. Osaka, was granted citizenship at birth. (Japanese citizens who voluntarily naturalize in another country automatically lose their Japanese citizenship.)'
b'But some analysts warn that because of Ms. Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s celebrity, it would be difficult for the government to quietly give her a pass on dual citizenship.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think for the government it is a problem if she openly carries on having two passports,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sachiko Horiguchi, associate professor of anthropology at Temple University\xe2\x80\x99s Tokyo campus. \xe2\x80\x9cBecause that means the public would know that the law isn\xe2\x80\x99t really enforced. I don\xe2\x80\x99t think the government wants to admit that or the public to know that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Three years ago, when Renho Murata, whose father is from Taiwan, ran as the first woman to lead the opposition Democratic Party, right-wing critics attacked her because she had not formally relinquished her Taiwanese citizenship.'
b'Partly in response to the frenzy over Ms. Murata, Kimi Onoda, a member of Parliament from the governing Liberal Democratic Party who was born in the United States to an American father and a Japanese mother, formally renounced her American citizenship.'
b'Ms. Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s multicultural background has challenged Japan\xe2\x80\x99s notions of national identity, and she has become the most prominent mixed-race and mixed-nationality figure in a country where only one in 50 children born each year has a foreign parent. Though she is not fluent in Japanese, she has captivated the country with her whimsical remarks to the news media, as well as her humility in victory.'
b'Her parents decided when she was young that she and her sister, who also played, would represent Japan, partly because the American tennis federation showed them little attention.'
b'Anticipating Ms. Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s citizenship choice, Michio Ushioda, a former columnist for The Mainichi Shimbun, a daily newspaper, and a professor at Teikyo University in Tokyo, said on Twitter that Japan would fall into a national funk if she elected American citizenship over Japanese.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe disappointment of the Japanese at that time would be great,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Ushioda wrote in a tweet that only select followers could view, even suggesting that Japan\xe2\x80\x99s current administration would collapse if Ms. Osaka competed for the United States in the Olympics.'
b'Under International Olympic Committee rules, competitors must be nationals of the countries they represent. Similarly, under International Tennis Federation rules, Ms. Osaka could not play for Japan if she gave up her Japanese citizenship.'
b'Legal experts say Japanese law provides a loophole through which dual citizens can effectively retain both nationalities. The law requires only that a Japanese citizen \xe2\x80\x9cendeavor to renounce\xe2\x80\x9d foreign nationality, a phrase that can provide just enough wiggle room for citizens to hold on to an extra passport.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMany people misunderstand the law and feel threatened that they have to choose a nationality,\xe2\x80\x9d said Yasuhiro Okuda, a law professor at Chuo University.'
b'Until 1985, Japan granted citizenship only to children whose fathers were Japanese. When it changed the law \xe2\x80\x94 a move it made under pressure from international critics who said the rules discriminated against women \xe2\x80\x94 the government added the clause stipulating that children with dual citizenship would have to choose between their passports by the time they turned 22.'
b'Analysts say Japan\xe2\x80\x99s law makes little sense in a modern world filled with multicultural citizens like Ms. Osaka.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt goes against Japan\xe2\x80\x99s efforts to recruit and retain global talent,\xe2\x80\x9d said Erin Chung, a professor of East Asian politics at Johns Hopkins University in Baltimore. \xe2\x80\x9cIf you basically maintain the spirit of the current nationality act, that will be a huge deterrent for athletes and other members of what\xe2\x80\x99s called the global talent pool to stay in Japan.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'For older generations, opening Japan to a pool of newly naturalized citizens could generate a considerable political backlash.'
b'But younger Japanese are growing more accustomed to living and working with international neighbors and colleagues.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYoung people in their 20s now are much more familiar with foreigners or so-called \xe2\x80\x98hafu,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d said Satoko Takeda, a visiting researcher at Osaka University of Economics and Law, using the Japanese term, from the English word \xe2\x80\x9chalf,\xe2\x80\x9d to describe those of mixed-race descent like Ms. Osaka. \xe2\x80\x9cThey are different from previous generations. b'Andreescu can bang groundstrokes at a world-class clip or change pace abruptly with slice. She also can hit rolling, off-speed, angled winners from either wing that might well become her trademark. b'Andreescu can attack the net or defend in the corners with her foot speed and excellent footwork. She has a strong first serve and, perhaps more important in the return-focused women\xe2\x80\x99s game, a solid second serve that is difficult to attack.'
b'Andreescu also likes the drop shot, which can be a joy and a curse \xe2\x80\x94 as was evident against Kerber. b'In his early teens, Tiafoe promised his family that he would one day become a star tennis player, and take care of everyone.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI obviously wasn\xe2\x80\x99t a normal tennis story,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'In the beginning of his career, he said, he had been playing for his family. Not long ago, he bought his mother a house and he is indeed providing his family with a comfortable life. \xe2\x80\x9cNow,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m trying to do it for me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Dimitrov, 27, is a tour stalwart known for his immense talent, long among the world\xe2\x80\x99s top-20 men\xe2\x80\x99s players, and the winner of eight tour titles. But from the start of this match, Tiafoe, who has won just a single title, gave as good as he got.'
b'The match turned in the second set tiebreaker. Facing a trio of set points, Tiafoe responded as he has all week \xe2\x80\x94 first in his win against Kevin Anderson, one of the tournament favorites, and then over the 35th-ranked Italian veteran Andreas Seppi. He buckled down, kept his chin up and a spring in his step, and scorched a series of winners and error-inducing groundstrokes. Not long afterward, aided by a Dimitrov double fault, the set was his, and soon the match.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn that tiebreak, as much as I was playing better and better, he just kept coming back with good answers,\xe2\x80\x9d said Dimitrov, whose own Grand Slam coming out came in 2014, when he lost in the Wimbledon semifinals to the eventual champion, Novak Djokovic.'
b'On Sunday, after a match point in which a Dimitrov groundstroke fell into the net, Tiafoe bent over in the moment, hands on his knees, stunned. Who could blame him? He had struggled at the end of last year, losing matches a player of his talent is expected to win.'
b'His traveling coach, Zack Evenden, explained that a turn came following the painful defeat two weeks ago to Millman, ranked No. 37, at the Sydney International.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMillman wanted it more,\xe2\x80\x9d Evenden said. He recalled Tiafoe realizing that he could learn from the Australian journeyman, who is deeply admired on tour for his doggedness. \xe2\x80\x9cTalent is not enough to get you where you want to be. You\xe2\x80\x99ve got to turn up for every single point. You have got to want it, and want it bad.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Tiafoe now goes up against a player who has 17 Gand Slam titles and is perhaps the greatest competitor in tennis history.'

b'Siblings of top players have often drafted off that familial fame to get started in their career, but the main draw wild card for Mari Osaka raised many eyebrows around the tournament, considering she was ranked more than 200 spots below the cut for the qualifying draw for this elite event. b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 At the start of this year\xe2\x80\x99s Australian Open, the French tennis player Lucas Pouille was a man severely overlooked.'
b'He had come to Melbourne, after all, on the heels of a 2018 season that dripped with disappointing losses, trying more than anything else to simply recapture a sense of joy on the court.'
b'Expectations? Any that existed were extremely slim, Pouille said, as he looked back Wednesday on a tournament that now stands as the most thrilling of his seven-year career. Slim, from those on the outside looking in, he said, and \xe2\x80\x9ceven from myself.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But in the world of professional tennis, slim expectations can grow Grand Slam fat with remarkable speed. They certainly have this week for Pouille. On Wednesday afternoon at Melbourne Park, the Frenchman moved into his first Grand Slam semifinal with a sharp 7-6 (4), 6-3, 6-7 (2), 6-4 victory over Milos Raonic of Canada, the lumbering former Wimbledon finalist with the massive serve who was seeded 16th.'
b'Pouille, who had never won an Australian Open match before last week, now faces a nearly impossible task. The final is within his reach. But to get there he must beat Novak Djokovic, who currently rules men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis with an iron grip.'
b'Not long after Pouille and Raonic left Rod Laver Arena, Djokovic breezed into the final four, his quarterfinal match done in just 52 minutes when the eighth-seeded Kei Nishikori, of Japan, retired with a leg injury. Djokovic led by 6-1, 4-1 at the time, and had never been pushed. It was a gift. A match that short and stress free will help Djokovic, seeking his seventh Australian Open title, keep his body fresh at the stage in this tournament when he most needs it, especially since he had struggled through a bruising, four-set win over Daniil Medvedev earlier this week.'
b'Pouille, 24 years old and seeded 28th, burst onto the scene in 2016, with quarterfinal showings at Wimbledon and the U.S. Open, where he beat Nadal.'
b'Last season, however, was tennis purgatory. True, his ranking did rise briefly to a career-high No. 10 in March. But he also failed to get past the third round of any of the major championships. He lost to players ranked outside the top 100. And as the year ended, he suffered through a string of early tournament defeats.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI lost that joy being on the court,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, reflecting on last year after his quarterfinal match, which he won behind strong serving and a steady dose of returns that left the 6-5 Raonic off balance. \xe2\x80\x9cFor some reason, I don\xe2\x80\x99t know really know why it happened. b'Searching for a solution, he last month replaced his old coach with Am\xc3\xa9lie Mauresmo, the 39-year-old former pro who is a hero in France because of her pair of Grand Slam singles titles and because she is the last French player, male of female, to reach world No. 1.'
b'Other top male players are coached by a woman, but those female coaches are relatives. b'\xe2\x80\x9cMen are coaching women, so why not the contrary?\xe2\x80\x9d Pouille said at his news conference. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not about being a man or a woman, it\xe2\x80\x99s about knowing tennis, about having the good state of mind.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He summed up the ways that Mauresmo has helped him turn a corner. She creates \xe2\x80\x9ca cool atmosphere,\xe2\x80\x9d he explained. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re not too serious. We can laugh. We can make jokes. Once we go and hit the balls, we are really into it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In other words, balance.'
b'And more: \xe2\x80\x9cI think she\xe2\x80\x99s bringing a lot of confidence to my game.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Pouille will need every ounce of cool confidence, and likely the best tennis of his life, if he is to beat Djokovic on a packed center court stadium Friday.'
b'Will Pouille be overlooked once again?'
b'Not a chance, said Djokovic. \xe2\x80\x9cI always thought he\xe2\x80\x99s a great player,\xe2\x80\x9d the Serb told the assembled reporters in the wake of his own quarterfinal win.'

b'On Tennis'
b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'MIAMI GARDENS, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 Another week on the 2019 tennis circuit, another different champion.'
b'April is just about here, and no man or woman has yet managed to win more than one singles title on the main circuit this season.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s amazing, isn\xe2\x80\x99t it?\xe2\x80\x9d Ashleigh Barty said after keeping the streak alive on Saturday with a 7-6 (1), 6-3 victory against Karolina Pliskova in the Miami Open final.'
b'But though Barty, an Australian, was the 14th WTA champion in 14 events, her winning a title of this magnitude bore no resemblance to a fluke.'
b'Her game is a varied thing of beauty, mate, and though at 5 feet 5 inches she is far from the most imposing player on tour, her tennis has been standing taller and taller in 2019.'
b'She was a finalist in Sydney, a quarterfinalist at the Australian Open with many of her sports-savvy compatriots piling on the pressure by tracking her every stroke. She was then the key figure in Australia\xe2\x80\x99s 3-2 victory over the United States on the road in the Fed Cup.'
b'Though Elina Svitolina stopped her in the round of 16 at Indian Wells by winning the longest match of the women\xe2\x80\x99s season (3 hours 12 minutes), there was no stopping Barty in Miami.'
b'There was no stopping Bob and Mike Bryan either. The twins, who have formed one of the greatest doubles teams in tennis history and will turn 41 on April 29, defended their men\xe2\x80\x99s doubles title with a 7-5, 7-6 (6) victory over Wesley Koolhof and Stefanos Tsitsipas.'
b'The title came eight months after Bob Bryan underwent hip resurfacing surgery on Aug. 2, 2018. He believed then that his playing career was over, but they have now won two titles since reuniting this season. The first came at the Delray Beach Open last month, but Saturday\xe2\x80\x99s victory was a step up, coming after they saved four match points in the semifinals against Lukasz Kubot and Marcelo Melo.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf you would have told me in August when I was getting surgery that I was going to defend the Miami Open title I would have said you are full of it, really,\xe2\x80\x9d Bob Bryan said.'
b'Barty, seeded No. 12, defeated three top-10 players: Kiki Bertens; Petra Kvitova, who had stopped her runs in Australia; and Pliskova.'
b'Already an established doubles champion, Barty will be a part of the singles top 10 for the first time on Monday, moving to No. 9 and becoming the first Australian woman to break into that group since 2013, when Samantha Stosur was at her peak.'
b'But Barty, now 22, is the undisputed leader of Australian women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis at this stage, as underscored by her 6-0, 6-3 victory over the 35-year-old Stosur in the round of 32 in Miami.'
b'Her Australian roots go deeper than most: Her father, Robert, is an Indigenous Australian, a part of the Ngarigo people. She has embraced that heritage, taking on a role as a tennis ambassador in the indigenous community, joining the former champion Evonne Goolagong Cawley, who was a part of the Wiradjuri people and who won seven Grand Slam singles titles from 1971 to 1980.'
b'Barty is, in many respects, an old-school tennis talent. Her off-court demeanor is upbeat, articulate and modest. (She favors \xe2\x80\x9cwe\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cteam\xe2\x80\x9d more than \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x9d when discussing her rise.)'
b'Her on-court demeanor is understated, close to stoic. There was barely a grunt and nary a shriek as she and Pliskova exchanged blows on the temporary main court that has been installed this year in Hard Rock Stadium.'
b'Even if there had been more shouts and murmurs, it would have been a challenge to make them out given the poor acoustics that muffle noise even when a crowd is much bigger and more boisterous than it was for Saturday\xe2\x80\x99s final.'
b'But it is Barty\xe2\x80\x99s tennis that is the true classic. She has pure technique, including a potent loop topspin forehand and a powerful, match-winning serve full of disguise and power, which she generates with great leg drive and racket-head speed.'
b'Pliskova, a former No. 1 who was seeded No. 5 in Miami, leads the tour in aces. But Barty won that duel within a duel, finishing with 15 aces to Pliskova\xe2\x80\x99s six and winning 86 percent of her first-serve points to Pliskova\xe2\x80\x99s 66 percent.'
b'Barty can also thrive at the net (she won the United States Open doubles title last year with CoCo Vandeweghe) and can drive a two-handed backhand or hit a one-handed slice with enough bite to cause a world of geometric pain for tall players, like the 6-1 Pliskova, who thrive on higher strike zones and consistent pace.'
b'Variety, it seems, is all the rage in women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis. Bianca Andreescu, the 18-year-old Canadian wild card who made a stunning run to the title at Indian Wells, also has a diverse array of weaponry and, like Barty, a pronounced midrally taste for changing rhythm.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI have always tried to bring as much variety onto the court as possible,\xe2\x80\x9d Barty said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s always about trying to neutralize what your opponent\xe2\x80\x99s doing. Obviously, there was a bit of a phase in women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis where there was this big power and first strikers that were getting on top of rallies early. But I think the physicality in tennis, especially on the women\xe2\x80\x99s side, has grown, which has allowed more players to neutralize off that big first ball and work their way into points.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She proved her point repeatedly on Saturday, displaying her improved returns and tracking down Pliskova\xe2\x80\x99s flat bolts in the corners and slicing them back into play. But she has ample punching power of her own and quite an upside. It is easy to see her thriving on clay (see the French Open) and grass (see Wimbledon).'
b'It is also easy to imagine that this breakthrough could have come earlier if she had not decided to step away from tennis after the 2014 United States Open and focus on cricket instead. But in her view, it was that break, which ended in 2016, that has allowed her to better manage the expectations and begin fulfilling her tennis potential.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think I was an average cricketer, and I\xe2\x80\x99m becoming a better tennis player,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was certainly an enjoyable time in my life. It was a time that I think I found myself a little bit more as a person, and I met an amazing group of girls and a new circle of friends, I suppose. But I think tennis was always my calling.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'So it seems after the most significant victory of her career: The Miami Open is a part of the top tier of events on the regular tour, below only the four Grand Slam tournaments and the season-ending WTA Finals in prestige.'
b'Barty might be merely one of so many tennis winners in 2019, but she has the ability and the personality to not only be a serial champion but a popular one, as well.'

b'INDIAN WELLS, Calif. \xe2\x80\x94 Back on the march as the best player in men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis, Novak Djokovic stumbled in the desert sunlight on Tuesday on his favorite surface.'
b'Djokovic flubbed some forehands and returns he normally makes in his third-round match at the BNP Paribas Open and cracked a racket in frustration. b'Now, nearly a decade later, Kohlschreiber has another upset tale to tell.'

b'\xe2\x80\x9cOf course you always need the No. 1 not playing his best tennis to beat him, but I\xe2\x80\x99m very happy with my performance,\xe2\x80\x9d Kohlschreiber said.'
b'It was a rough day all around for No. 1s. Naomi Osaka, the top player in the women\xe2\x80\x99s game, was more soundly beaten. Bencic, who just turned 22, is yet another great talent from Switzerland, land of Roger Federer and Martina Hingis. Bencic broke into the top 10 as a teenager in 2016 before left wrist surgery stopped her ascent.'
b'She broke Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s powerful serve five times in this brief encounter and proved more steady from the baseline, as well. She is now on a 11-match winning streak after winning the title in Dubai and has five victories over top 10 players in the last month.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMy injury just changed my perspective,\xe2\x80\x9d said Bencic, the No. 23 seed. \xe2\x80\x9cI learned so much from this time, and I\xe2\x80\x99m really enjoying to be on the court.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Hardcourts remain Djokovic\xe2\x80\x99s happiest hunting ground. Ten of his 15 Grand Slam singles titles have come on the surface that suits his elastic athleticism best.'
b'He also has won five singles titles at Indian Wells, but after winning three straight times here in 2015, 2016 and 2017, he has run into early-round trouble.'
b'Last year, in the midst of a deep funk and still recovering from elbow surgery, he made 58 unforced errors in an opening-match defeat to Taro Daniel, a Japanese qualifier. But this year, Djokovic arrived on an undeniable roll after sweeping to victory at the Australian Open, manhandling Rafael Nadal in the final.'
b'Djokovic has won three straight Grand Slam singles titles and will hold all four for the second time if he can prevail at the French Open in June and complete another so-called \xe2\x80\x9cDjoker Slam.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He is still in the doubles here after reaching the semifinals with partner Fabio Fognini later on Tuesday, but only the tournaments ahead will show if Djokovic\xe2\x80\x99s singles performance was a blip or a harbinger of more struggles.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI had to get over it in an hour, because I played doubles,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cI must admit I was thinking about it. It\xe2\x80\x99s part of our world, and we just have to bounce back very quickly.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Djokovic said competing in the doubles gave him \xe2\x80\x9ca chance to rectify the wrongs,\xe2\x80\x9d but that his singles performance would not affect him in the long run.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI know what I\xe2\x80\x99m capable of,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI know the quality of my tennis. It\xe2\x80\x99s just one of those days. You just have to congratulate your opponent and move on.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The timing was intriguing, coming after a week replete with tennis politicking. Djokovic, as president of the ATP Player Council, spent the days before the tournament in meetings and debate, and the ATP\xe2\x80\x99s board of directors ultimately voted last Thursday not to renew the contract of Chris Kermode, the tour\xe2\x80\x99s chairman and chief executive.'
b'There has been plenty of pushback on the decision, with Nadal and Federer both pointing out that they were not consulted by Djokovic or council members in the run-up to the Kermode decision. Federer said he had reached out directly to Djokovic who had been unable to find time on his schedule for a discussion.'
b'But then neither Nadal nor Federer are on the council at this stage, although both have served in the past. Federer, a former president, has acknowledged that the role can be draining, particularly in fraught times, and Djokovic spoke about that challenge on Sunday after defeating American Bjorn Fratangelo in his opening match.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI care about the current generation and also the future generation and future of this sport,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think that the sport is doing well, but it can also do better and better, you know, as we go along. And if I, with my status and with my position in the world of sport and tennis, can influence that positively, then why not? Yes, it takes away in energy and time, but I know I do it from the right place in my heart and with the right intent, and then I also receive a lot of energy for that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He has received some criticism, too, but appears intent on trying to push for structural reforms on the ATP Tour, which could include dividing Kermode\xe2\x80\x99s role into two separate positions, or changing the size or composition of the board.'
b'Success is far from guaranteed considering the internal tensions that exist in the ATP: an organization that is a long-running and often uneasy partnership between the players and those who own and operate the tournaments.'
b'It would be all too easy to get distracted.'
b'But some rejected any such speculation on Tuesday and emphasized Kohlschreiber\xe2\x80\x99s performance. Among them: Nick Kyrgios, the unpredictable and intermittently committed Australian who won a hardcourt title in Mexico last week in style but was beaten, 6-4, 6-4, by Kohlschreiber in the second round here.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSomething has to be wrong with him right?\xe2\x80\x9d Kyrgios tweeted on Tuesday, referring to Djokovic. \xe2\x80\x9cI lose to Kholi and get absolutely shredded \xe2\x80\x98same old kyrgios\xe2\x80\x99 how about the guy is just good? b'Kohlschreiber was unseeded here but not by much with a world ranking of 39. Quick and powerful, he has one of the prettiest one-handed backhands in the game yet does his most consistent damage with his forehand.'
b'But in truth, he needed all his tennis tools to win on Tuesday after rain suspended play on Monday night after just one game. He also needed to put 71 percent of his first serves in play and save three of four break points against the game\xe2\x80\x99s premier returner.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think I was not unhappy with the rain delay,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think the warmer conditions suited my game more today. I was fresh. I had two good wins. So everything came together.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Such moments have been hard to come by in the game\xe2\x80\x99s biggest events during Kohlschreiber\xe2\x80\x99s career, which has coincided with one of the greatest generations of stars in tennis history. Federer, Nadal and Djokovic have 52 Grand Slam singles titles between them.'
