b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'The main clay-court season is officially underway, and this time around it is particularly unclear how the dust might settle.'
b'If Rafael Nadal is truly healthy after aggravating a right knee injury three weeks ago \xe2\x80\x94 he has been training at home to prepare for the Monte Carlo Open \xe2\x80\x94 he remains the man to beat on the game\xe2\x80\x99s grittiest surface. No one else has won 11 French Open singles titles, and the rational assumption is that no one else ever will.'
b'But the women\xe2\x80\x99s game is in a wondrous state of flux, with 14 different champions in the season\xe2\x80\x99s first 14 tournaments. And none of them was named Serena Williams, Maria Sharapova or Simona Halep.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s by far the most wide-open field as far as I can remember,\xe2\x80\x9d Chris Evert, the former No. 1 and a seven-time French Open champion, said in an interview Tuesday. \xe2\x80\x9cNo one seems to have obvious momentum above the other. It\xe2\x80\x99s not only the closeness in talent and skills. Attitudes, emotions and fitness and injuries enter into it as well. I have no clue.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Serena Williams has not won a title since returning to the tour in March 2018 after giving birth to her daughter. She has played only three tournaments this season and has not finished any of them feeling healthy. She twisted an ankle while on the brink of victory in an Australian Open quarterfinal against Karolina Pliskova and lost a 5-1 third-set lead, unable to convert on four match points.'
b'In Indian Wells, Calif., Williams retired in the third round against Garbi\xc3\xb1e Muguruza, citing a viral illness. In Miami, she withdrew after winning her opening match, citing a left knee injury. Williams is 37, and her knees have long been a concern, restricting her training through the years. She does not plan to compete again until the Italian Open in Rome in mid-May, shortly before the French Open.'
b'That will leave her short of matches against an increasingly deep and confident field, which is full of young, exciting talents with all-court games who have grown up dealing with big pace. Williams\xe2\x80\x99s quest for a record-tying 24th Grand Slam singles title, which once looked like only a matter of time, is now a more complicated matter.'
b'But discounting Williams is rarely a winning proposition. She has managed to play some sparkling tennis in 2019, striking the ball very cleanly in some of the early rounds in Australia and again in her victory over Victoria Azarenka in Indian Wells.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cA healthy Serena is a dangerous Serena; she hasn\xe2\x80\x99t been healthy all year,\xe2\x80\x9d Evert said. \xe2\x80\x9cShe still has an edge in power and experience.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Williams also has the most impressive career record on clay of any active player: 170-34. Her career winning percentage of 83.3 puts her ahead of Sharapova, who is at 81.5 percent with plenty of doubt swirling about her form and her tennis future at age 31.'
b'Happy off the court but vulnerable on it, she has not competed since January because of injuries and has not reached a tour final since winning the Tianjin Open in October 2017.'
b'Halep has the best clay-court numbers over the last few seasons and leads the WTA Tour\xe2\x80\x99s clay-court power rankings, which give more weight to recent results.'
b'But even as she again closes in on being No. 1, Halep, 27, has hardly been dominant. Oui, she won last year\xe2\x80\x99s French Open, her first Grand Slam singles title. But she has not won another clay-court title since Madrid in May 2017 and has not won a tournament on any surface since the Rogers Cup in Canada in August.'
b'Without Darren Cahill as her coach this season, Halep has not looked like the same resolute and selectively aggressive force, although her run to the semifinals of the Miami Open last week was encouraging.'
b'The biggest prizes in 2019 have gone to younger women, all under age 23.'
b'Naomi Osaka, 21, won the year\xe2\x80\x99s first Grand Slam title at the Australian Open and remains No. 1 by a whisker. Belinda Bencic, 22, won the Premier 5 event in Dubai. Most surprisingly, Bianca Andreescu, 18, won the Premier Mandatory event in Indian Wells, and then Ashleigh Barty, 22, confirmed her steady rise by winning in Miami.'
b'Andreescu and Barty have the skills to thrive on clay \xe2\x80\x94 their strong topspin forehands, quick feet and ability to hit sliced backhands, well-disguised drop shots and heavy first and second serves.'
b'But the big-hitting Osaka has a losing record on clay (9-11) and likes to call herself \xe2\x80\x9ca hardcourt player.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She also has lost momentum since her surprising split with her coach, Sascha Bajin, after the Australian Open. She has hired Venus Williams\xe2\x80\x99s former hitting partner, Jermaine Jenkins, a college star with a reassuring courtside demeanor. But for now, Osaka is only 3-3 since winning in Melbourne, with losses to Kristina Mladenovic in Dubai, to Bencic in Indian Wells and to the changeup artist Hsieh Su-wei in Miami.'
b'Novak Djokovic, the men\xe2\x80\x99s No. 1, also has the wind in his face after losing early in Indian Wells and Miami. But he has won three Grand Slam singles titles in a row, and it is difficult to disregard the memory of Djokovic having his way from the baseline against Nadal in the Australian Open final.'
b'Nadal, 32, continues to battle his body. A recurrence of tendinitis in his right knee caused him to withdraw before his semifinal against Roger Federer in Indian Wells. At this stage, he knows too well the price of pushing through pain, although pain has been a constant. How much longer can he do it?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWho knows? b'Nadal is back training hard in Majorca on a surface that is more forgiving to his joints than hardcourts. He is on schedule to defend his title in Monte Carlo this month. So is third-ranked Alexander Zverev, who has a fine clay-court record and the talent to win multiple majors but has been slumping.'
b'Federer, back on a roll at age 37 after winning in Miami and intent on returning to clay after a three-year break, plans to come back in Madrid in early May after training in Switzerland.'

b'INDIAN WELLS, Calif. \xe2\x80\x94 It was 2011. Ivo Karlovic was already an ATP Tour veteran with graying temples, and his close friend and former coach Tarik Benhabiles was talking about Karlovic\xe2\x80\x99s serve, and his future.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe has a huge weapon,\xe2\x80\x9d Benhabiles told me. \xe2\x80\x9cHe can play until he\xe2\x80\x99s 40 years old, no problem.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Kudos to Benhabiles, who once helped Andy Roddick become a force, for knowing his tennis. But, above all, kudos to Karlovic, the 6-foot-11 Croatian, for finding a way to fight and serve through everything life has thrown at him.'
b'It has hardly been \xe2\x80\x9cno problem,\xe2\x80\x9d but Karlovic turned 40 on Feb. 28, and he is definitely still playing.'
b'He has won three rounds at the BNP Paribas Open this year and is now the oldest man to win a singles match at a Masters 1000 event. On Wednesday, with plenty of gray in his beard now as well as in his temples, Karlovic will deploy his fearsome weapon against Dominic Thiem, the No. 7 seed, for a place in the quarterfinals.'
b'At 25, Thiem is 15 years younger than Karlovic \xe2\x80\x94 but then just about everybody on tour is younger than Karlovic, including some of his former rivals who are now coaches.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s older than me!\xe2\x80\x9d said Ivan Ljubicic, the 39-year-old co-coach of Roger Federer, who remains the most prominent graybeard in men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis but is still Karlovic\xe2\x80\x99s junior at 37.'
b'Karlovic has remained a factor by overcoming a major Achilles\xe2\x80\x99 tendon injury in 2010 and encephalitis in 2013, which caused debilitating headaches and left him temporarily without feeling in his right arm.'
b'He has remained a force by focusing on fitness and dropping weight to take the pressure off his knees and other joints. He is down to 225 pounds, from 245 in 2011.'
b'On court, Karlovic has learned to maximize his strengths and accept his weaknesses. He will never have a drive backhand, but his one-handed slice is crisp enough. And though his lateral mobility remains limited compared to his competitors, his forehand is huge and his serve-and-volley style is even more unusual and disorienting in this baseline-focused era.'
b'In truth, his style is often serve-and-no-volley. He has slammed an ATP record 13,235 aces. Along the way, he has definitively proven, like it or not, that there is a place in a movement-based game for players of towering height like the 6-10 John Isner, the 33-year-old American star, and the 6-11 Reilly Opelka, a 21-year-old from the U.S. who is hitting aces at a rapid clip of his own.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf you look at any sport, everywhere there are taller guys, so I know that is the future in tennis,\xe2\x80\x9d Karlovic said, as he has said for years.'
b'Ljubicic, who had a huge serve of his own and will turn 40 this month, grew up playing junior tournaments with Karlovic in Croatia and elsewhere. It was a time of war in the former Yugoslavia, and tennis was often the least of the youngsters\xe2\x80\x99 concerns.'
b'Fearing for their lives, Ljubicic\xe2\x80\x99s family fled Bosnia and ended up briefly in a refugee camp in Croatia. Ljubicic eventually ended up honing his game in an Italian tennis club and reaching No. 3 in the world in 2006 before retiring in 2012.'
b'Karlovic stayed in Zagreb, the Croatian capital. He was the son of well-educated professionals: his father a meteorologist; his mother an agronomist.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn Zagreb, there were not a lot of airstrikes, but I spent a lot of time in the bomb shelters,\xe2\x80\x9d Karlovic said of his early teens. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was always airstrike warnings.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Funds were short, and so was quality coaching and court time. Karlovic had already decided he preferred tennis to basketball despite attempts to recruit him. He would wait until the evening when the tennis courts in Zagreb were empty and then use the balls he could find and hit serves on his own, sometimes after dark.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was the only way I could practice,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI would like people to know that my serve is not only that good because of my height. I worked on it a lot.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He did not find a regular coach until his early 20s, and despite his imposing presence he managed to fly far below the radar until the first round of Wimbledon in 2003, where, as an all-but-unknown qualifier in an age before social media, he upset the defending champion Lleyton Hewitt in four sets on Centre Court.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was not easy: I was looking around at all these huge courts I never had a chance to play on before,\xe2\x80\x9d Karlovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cI lost the first set 6-1, but after that I just kind of calmed down and started playing my game, and then after the match, it was not easy because everybody wanted to know, who am I?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'What made it harder was the pronounced stammer that Karlovic has had since boyhood, which made public speaking excruciating.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was just thinking to myself, this is what you have to do if you want to become a good player,\xe2\x80\x9d he said of post-match news conferences. \xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99re going to have to do it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Nearly 16 years later, the stammer is much less pronounced, and Karlovic has become not only an excellent player but an enduring one. He peaked in the rankings at No. 14 in 2008 but was still in the top 20 last year before injuries contributed to him dropping to No. 138 in September.'
b'Instead of calling it a career, Karlovic chose to head back to tennis\xe2\x80\x99s minor leagues with the goal of making the main draw of the Australian Open. If he didn\xe2\x80\x99t achieve that goal, he would retire. He played in a series of ATP Challenger events in the final months of 2018, winning one in Calgary.'
b'Australia beckoned. But Karlovic, now based in Plantation, Fla., said one of the biggest challenges has been leaving his family behind. He and his wife, Alsi, have two children: a 7-year-old daughter, Jada, and an 18-month-old son, Noah.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI had to leave on Christmas Day to get to a tournament in India,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cSo everybody was home. We had friends over, family, and then after lunch I was on the way to the airport. It was really difficult. My kids were crying and stuff, so it wasn\xe2\x80\x99t easy, but on the other hand, I am doing this also because of them, you know? So they don\xe2\x80\x99t have it as hard as I had it. So maybe that evens out the pain for me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He wanted Jada to have a memory of him as a professional tennis player.'

b'Presumably not even Benhabiles is ready to predict that.'

After winning the title in Rotterdam, the Netherlands, in February and briefly reclaiming the No. 1 ranking, Federer went without another tournament championship until October. After skipping the clay-court season for the second year in a row, he lost in the quarterfinals at Wimbledon after holding a match point against Kevin Anderson, and in the fourth round of the United States Open to John Millman.'
b'Federer played down the doomsday talk that accompanied his stagnation in the second half of the year.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI wasn\xe2\x80\x99t too disappointed,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI was more surprised to hear that there was sort of concern, or people were saying, \xe2\x80\x98What a bad second half to the year.\xe2\x80\x99 \xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Federer conceded disappointing finishes at the Grand Slam events but thought he otherwise played well, including a loss in a third-set tiebreaker to Novak Djokovic in the semifinals of the Paris Masters in November.'
b'He said what he needed to do better this year \xe2\x80\x9cis really play well when it really comes down to the crunch.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Federer said he trusted his own evaluations of his play as well as input from his coaches, Ivan Ljubicic and Severin L\xc3\xbcthi.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI can analyze \xe2\x80\x94 with my age, very well \xe2\x80\x94 my own matches and my own feelings,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI have two great coaches, two of the best in the game, who give me their fair assessment, and I have a fitness coach who tells me if I\xe2\x80\x99m moving good or not. They\xe2\x80\x99re all open and honest towards me. I don\xe2\x80\x99t want any sugarcoating; I want it real, and straight. That\xe2\x80\x99s it. I know, always, where I\xe2\x80\x99m at.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s very clear in my team where I stand. And from that standpoint, I\xe2\x80\x99m happy where I am right now. I\xe2\x80\x99m in a great position.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mauresmo longs to learn more about what Federer does in his off-seasons.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI hope one day he will explain to everyone everything,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe little details, everything that he\xe2\x80\x99s put together to be able to play this well at his age, to move this well.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Federer is not exactly clandestine about his routines. He prefers, for example, to do his off-season movement drills on a tennis court, rather than indoors as many players do, to better simulate the footing and friction of match conditions.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI do a bit of weights, too,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, grinning and gesturing toward his lithe frame. \xe2\x80\x9cI know we don\xe2\x80\x99t see it, but I do.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Federer started his season auspiciously, winning all eight sets he played at the Hopman Cup last week, never dropping serve in any of the matches.'
b'But he considers the top-ranked Djokovic the clear favorite at the Australian Open. Djokovic, a six-time champion in Melbourne, has won the last two Grand Slam tournaments.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe know who the usual are,\xe2\x80\x9d said Federer, who is seeded third, \xe2\x80\x9cand I\xe2\x80\x99m part of that bunch.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The longevity of that oligarchy, which also includes Rafael Nadal, has blocked several younger players from breaking through on tennis\xe2\x80\x99s biggest stages. No player currently younger than 30 has won even a set in a Grand Slam final.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re all tired of you guys already, but what can we do?\xe2\x80\x9d fourth-ranked Alexander Zverev, 21, said during the trophy ceremony of the Hopman Cup on Saturday, when he lost to Federer in singles and mixed doubles.'

b'A flash spotted on livestreams was likely caused by the crash of a tiny, fast-moving meteoroid left behind by a comet.'
b'By Robin George Andrews'
b'On Sunday and Monday, those in the Western Hemisphere with clear skies were fortunate enough to see the last total lunar eclipse of the decade. As the moon took on a distinctly redder shade just before midnight Eastern Time, livestreams of the phenomenon showed a flash of light suddenly and briefly emanating from the lunar surface.'
b'Anthony Cook, an astronomical observer at Los Angeles\xe2\x80\x99 Griffith Observatory which streamed the eclipse, thought it could have just been the camera\xe2\x80\x99s random electronic noise. Then astronomers and citizen scientists started to share their detection of the flash on Reddit and Twitter.'
b'The only explanation was that something slammed into the lunar surface and obliterated itself.'
b'[Sign up to get reminders for space and astronomy events on your calendar.]'
b'The moon is a multi-billion-year-old library of impact events, with fresh collisions still taking place frequently today. Capturing a lunar impact on video is rare enough, but this event \xe2\x80\x94 a collision during a total lunar eclipse \xe2\x80\x94 may be a first.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI have not heard of anyone seeing an impact like this during a lunar eclipse before,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sara Russell, a professor of planetary sciences at the Natural History Museum in London.'
b'Dr. Russell said that flashes can only be seen from Earth when the lunar surface is in shadow, which is normally just a few days before and after the new moon. A luminous full moon is anathema to such detections, but a total lunar eclipse, painting our pale celestial companion in darkness, changed that.'
b'Justin Cowart, a graduate student in geosciences at Stony Brook University in New York who spotted the flash, managed to narrow down the impact location. Using images from an amateur astronomer, Christian Fr\xc3\xb6schlin, Mr. Cowart determined that the flash took place somewhere in the lunar highlands, south of Byrgius crater.'
b'NASA\xe2\x80\x99s Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter, which studies the moon\xe2\x80\x99s surface, may soon spot the fresh crater. But the impact flash itself can be used to roughly estimate the size of the object that crashed on the moon, and its momentum. Based on NASA and European Space Agency databases of impact flashes, Mr. Cowart guesses that \xe2\x80\x9cit was probably somewhere between the size of an acorn and tennis ball.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Detection data from the Moon Impacts Detection and Analysis System, or MIDAS, found that the space rock was a pipsqueak of a meteoroid, only weighing something like 22 pounds, and measuring no more than 12 inches across.'
b'The provenance of the meteoroid remains an open question. According to Jose Maria Madiedo, an astrophysicist at the University of Huelva in Spain who is a co-director of the MIDAS system, most objects that hit Earth come from comets and not asteroids, and the same applies to the moon'
b'With that in mind, he said, \xe2\x80\x9cthe most likely situation is that the impactor was a rock from a comet.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'Considering its tiny dimensions, it must have been moving at an incredible speed to create a flash of light visible from Earth. Indeed, Dr. Madiedo said that the impact velocity would be in the range of 38,000 miles per hour. That is just over twice the speed that NASA\xe2\x80\x99s old space shuttle had to move after launch to achieve orbit of Earth.'
b'A total lunar eclipse is always something to marvel at, but one being gate-crashed by a hypersonic cometary shard is something else entirely.'
b'An earlier version of this article, using information from an astronomer, misstated where on the moon a flash of light was seen. It was south of the Byrgius crater, not west of Legendre crater.'

b'On Tennis'
b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'Andy Murray is not the youngest of the tennis supergroup known as the Big Four. Novak Djokovic was born a week later than Murray was.'
b'But it is still quite an unpleasant surprise to realize that Murray, 31, very likely will be the first of the remarkable quartet to retire.'
b'Roger Federer is somehow still gliding at 37. Rafael Nadal is somehow still persevering at 32.'
b'But Murray has been in too much pain for too long with no relief in view, and on Friday in Melbourne, Australia, all of those who have followed his career from up close or a great distance could share some of his pain, too.'
b'It was not what he said. It was what he couldn\xe2\x80\x99t say.'
b'Murray, like all tennis stars of his stature, has spent as much time in news conferences as most of us have spent at the coffee shop. They are an artificial construct that has become a natural habitat for Murray, a droll, strong-minded Scotsman with the voice that sounds like a low-flying drone \xe2\x80\x94 a voice he once called \xe2\x80\x9cmy least favorite thing about me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But as he sat down behind the table on Friday, his cap pulled low and his lips pursed, reporters placed digital recorders on the table in front him to capture the words. There was soon nothing to capture.'
b'Asked how he and his ailing hip were feeling, he answered, \xe2\x80\x9cYeah, not, not great.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He then sighed, averted his glance, dropped his chin, touched the bill of his cap and his face, fought for composure and was unable to utter another word for nearly a minute before finally grabbing his credential off the desk and leaving the room.'
b'Though he soon returned, nothing he explained then was nearly as eloquent as those 45 seconds of silence.'
b'What mattered most was all in there: the sensitivity, the humanity, the competitive fire reduced to anguish at not being able to solve his hip problem despite all the medical expertise, financial resources and iron will at his disposal.'
b'Murray plans to play on, hopefully until Wimbledon this summer, although there are no guarantees. He acknowledged that this Australian Open, which begins Monday, could be the finish line, and surely the poignancy of making such an announcement in Melbourne was not lost on him.'
b'[Update: Andy Murray loses in his first-round match at the Australian Open.]'
b'Sir Andrew Barron Murray has had many triumphs in his 31 years: back-to-back Olympic gold medals and three Grand Slam titles, none more resonant than his winning Wimbledon in 2013 to end a 77-year drought for British men in singles. Many other worthies, including Bunny Austin and Tim Henman, had embarked on the same quest and faltered.'
b'But Australia is where Murray has had to face his own tennis limitations.'
b'He broke down in tears during the awards ceremony after losing the final to Federer in 2010, but though he has, in his own words, \xe2\x80\x9ckept it together\xe2\x80\x9d since then in Melbourne, 2010 was only the beginning of the disappointment. He lost the final again in 2011, 2013, 2015 and 2016.'
b'No other man has gone 0-5 in singles finals at the same major tournament, and he shares the blame with Djokovic, his one-time doubles partner, who has beaten Murray in the last four of those finals.'
b'So close in age and skill sets, they first played as 13-year-olds at Les Petits As junior tournament in France. Murray won in a hurry, but they have played 36 times as professionals, more than enough to make it clear that Djokovic is the greater player.'
b'He leads their series by 25-11 and has 14 Grand Slam singles titles (and counting). For many, the Big Four has become the Big Three. And doesn\xe2\x80\x99t Stan Wawrinka have \xe2\x80\x94 like Murray \xe2\x80\x94 three major titles of his own?'
b'Such arguments have merit: Federer and Nadal also have winning records against Murray, and there is no doubt now that in the final analysis of this golden tennis era, Federer, Nadal and Djokovic will be the central figures and the statistical leaders.'
b'But Murray earned his place in tennis\xe2\x80\x99s great modern foursome, with his week-to-week consistency, his resilience, his all-surface brilliance and his ability to excel at Wimbledon with the equivalent of the Centre Court roof on his shoulders.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNever motivated by money, only by his rivals; he didn\xe2\x80\x99t need people\xe2\x80\x99s respect, but he earned it,\xe2\x80\x9d Mark Petchey, Murray\xe2\x80\x99s former coach, said in the wake of Murray\xe2\x80\x99s announcement.'
b'Murray might not have been here at all. He and his older brother, Jamie, were young students at Dunblane Primary School in their Scottish town in 1996 when a local resident entered the grounds and murdered 16 of their schoolmates and a teacher before shooting himself.'
b'The Murray brothers survived, though not without invisible scars, and they both grew up to become No. 1 in the world: Andy in singles, Jamie in doubles.'
b'That is a tribute to their childhood sibling rivalry, their talent and their work ethic, and also to their formidable tennis mother, Judy, a former Scottish professional player who has been a driving force with her intuition, her ambition, her sharp wit and her informed passion for the game.'
b'Jamie, 32 and still in the top 10 in doubles, plans to play beyond 2019. Andy, at this stage, does not.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe was a kaleidoscope of talent, of emotion, of movement, spirit and authenticity,\xe2\x80\x9d said Petchey, a former British player who introduced Murray to Kim Sears, who would become Murray\xe2\x80\x99s wife. \xe2\x80\x9cHe was a winner, but he became a champion. A champion not just on the court but a champion of causes off it. He leaves as he arrived. Tennis never changed him, but he changed tennis.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Murray, in part (but only in part) because of his mother\xe2\x80\x99s impact on his career, has been the rare men\xe2\x80\x99s No. 1 to speak out frequently in support of gender equality and women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis, whose results he actually seems to follow. He has also walked the walk, hiring a woman as a coach: Am\xc3\xa9lie Mauresmo.'
b'That has endeared him to a wider audience and only underscored the gulf between on-court Murray and off-court Murray. Under pressure and between the lines, he has often been far from endearing: barking at his entourage, using language better suited to the Glasgow docks, and muttering, muttering, muttering as he chased perfection in a sport that refused to cooperate.'
b'Watching him at work, it all has often seemed more a burden than a pleasure. His service motion resembles heavy lifting, and long before his hip problems became career threatening, his walk between points looked closer to a hobble.'
b'But that was before he sensed an opportunity and sprang into action: a short ball he could pounce on for a winner, a wide ball he could chase down that hardly anyone else in the game could have reached.'
b'Murray in his prime was above all a supreme athlete, possessed of quickness, coordination, feathery touch and selective striking power.'
b'As recently as 2016, he had his finest season, winning nine titles and reaching No. 1 for the first time. It still seems premature to believe that he is just about done. After all, retirement in tennis has long been a euphemism for a sabbatical, and one of Murray\xe2\x80\x99s peers who has dealt with pain offered words of encouragement on Friday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPlease don\xe2\x80\x99t stop trying,\xe2\x80\x9d Juan Mart\xc3\xadn del Potro wrote on Twitter. \xe2\x80\x9cKeep fighting. I can imagine your pain and sadness. I hope you can overcome this. You deserve to retire on your own terms, whenever that happens.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Del Potro speaks from experience; multiple wrist operations nearly snuffed out his career. His is a voice to be heeded. But unfortunately so is Murray\xe2\x80\x99s, especially when the emotions are so powerful that the words just won\xe2\x80\x99t come.'

b'INDIAN WELLS, Calif. \xe2\x80\x94 Belinda Bencic is making a tricky game look easy at the moment, redirecting her big-swinging opponents\xe2\x80\x99 best shots into the corners, conjuring defensive lobs and flicking reflex returns from inside the baseline.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m trying not to think who is on the other side of the court,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'But there is no ignoring the quality of her recent tennis victims. From Dubai to Indian Wells, Bencic has been taking on the best in the women\xe2\x80\x99s game and emerging again and again with a broad smile on her face.'
b'On Thursday, she ran her winning streak to 12 matches by defeating her sixth top-10 opponent in less than a month. On Tuesday she had routed Naomi Osaka, the new world No. 1, in little more than an hour at the BNP Paribas Open, but in Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s quarterfinal, Bencic met with a great deal more resistance from No. 5 seed Karolina Pliskova before prevailing, 6-3, 4-6, 6-3, in 2 hours 16 minutes.'
b'It was a match of fluctuating quality but no shortage of bravura shotmaking in the breeze, Pliskova\xe2\x80\x99s flat power against Bencic\xe2\x80\x99s fast-twitch counterpunching.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think Belinda\xe2\x80\x99s the best in the world at redirecting power, I really do,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mary Joe Fernandez, the ESPN analyst and a former champion at Indian Wells.'
b'That is quite a statement, considering that women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis is full of talented counterpunchers, including the reigning French Open champion, Simona Halep, and the reigning Wimbledon champion, Angelique Kerber, who will face Bencic in the semifinals after defeating Venus Williams, 7-6 (3), 6-3, on Thursday.'
b'But Bencic, a Swiss extrovert who turned 22 on Sunday and is returning to the fore after injury, has long been considered one of the game\xe2\x80\x99s most sparkling talents. She was taught to see the game in full by her father, Ivan, and also by Melanie Molitor, the mother and coach of Martina Hingis, the Swiss wunderkind who rose to No. 1 by treating a tennis court like a chessboard.'
b'Switzerland\xe2\x80\x99s tennis star-in-chief, Roger Federer, has played a supportive role in Bencic\xe2\x80\x99s career of late, partnering with her in the Hopman Cup team event and sending encouraging messages.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s worked a lot for this moment, and the big reward is coming now,\xe2\x80\x9d Federer said. \xe2\x80\x9cI got to know her at the Hopman Cup and tried to give her as much advice as I could. She\xe2\x80\x99s got a different game and is in a different stage of her career. Hopefully I helped. But the credit is hers and her team\xe2\x80\x99s.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'When Ivan Bencic first became interested in having his daughter play the game, Federer had not yet broken through to the elite level. Hingis was the Swiss player he watched and admired, and their families had more in common than an attraction to tennis. Molitor and Hingis had immigrated to Switzerland from the Slovakian side of the former Czechoslovakia. So had Ivan Bencic, whose family fled the country in 1968 after the Soviet invasion.'
b'Ivan Bencic telephoned Molitor when Belinda was 5 years old and asked her to take a look at his daughter\xe2\x80\x99s nascent game. Molitor was impressed enough to offer to help from time to time. It became a much more profound connection after Molitor started her own academy, and Hingis later added her own counsel to the mix.'
b'Though Bencic has more natural power and a more potent serve than her mentor did in her prime, she shares the ability to read tennis tea leaves even in the midst of a fast-paced rally.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cShe was helping me a lot,\xe2\x80\x9d Bencic said of Hingis, who retired in October 2017 as the world\xe2\x80\x99s No. 1 doubles player.'
b'At that stage, Bencic was still coming back from an operation on her left wrist. Though she is right handed, the pain had kept her from hitting her two-handed backhand effectively.'
b'She had appeared to be on a fast train to the top after defeating Caroline Wozniacki, Ana Ivanovic, Serena Williams and Halep in 2015 at age 18, on her way to the Rogers Cup title in Toronto and to later reaching the top 10.'
b'But her wrist injury changed that career arc, causing her to miss five months in 2017 and fall outside the top 300. She returned at low-level professional tournaments in Europe rather than use a protected ranking and return at the highest level.'
b'Less than two years later, that looks like the right move. There have been some stumbles, but she has found her footing and is guaranteed to re-enter the top 20 on Monday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI played those small events and built my confidence back up with my ranking,\xe2\x80\x9d she said of 2017. \xe2\x80\x9cBecause with the wrist, you never know if it\xe2\x80\x99s going to be good or going to hold. So definitely the first tournaments, it\xe2\x80\x99s always a test to see if you can keep up. I didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to play a big tournament with all the people right away and have the comeback in the public eye. I definitely needed matches and confidence.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'She is getting both in large quantities now. She beat four top-10 players on her way to the title in Dubai last month: Aryna Sabalenka, Halep, Elina Svitolina and Petra Kvitova. b'This is a fascinating, power-shifting phase in women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis. Osaka, 21, has been the player of the moment for the last six months, winning the singles titles at the 2018 United States Open and this year\xe2\x80\x99s Australian Open.'
b'But fresh threats to the new and fragile order continue to surface. Bianca Andreescu, an 18-year-old Canadian wild card, has reached the semifinals here and has a 25-3 record in tour-level matches this year.'
b'Bencic is not emerging, of course. b'Naomi Osaka, the half-Haitian, half-Japanese tennis champion, is the star of a new Japanese anime-style advertisement.'
b'The problem? The cartoon Ms. Osaka bears little resemblance to her real, biracial self.'
b'Her skin was unmistakably lightened, and her hair style changed \xe2\x80\x94 a depiction that has prompted criticism in Japan, where she has challenged a longstanding sense of cultural and racial homogeneity.'

She became the first Japanese-born tennis player to win a Grand Slam singles championship in September when she defeated Serena Williams in the U.S. Open, a victory that supercharged her celebrity ascent.'
b'That win prompted a cartoon in an Australian newspaper that was criticized for its depiction of Ms. Williams, which many saw as a racist caricature. While most of the condemnation focused on how the Australian cartoonist drew Ms. Williams, critics also noted that Ms. Osaka was depicted with blond hair and light skin.'
b'Black characters aren\xe2\x80\x99t frequently found in anime, but artists in the medium have successfully depicted their skin tones before.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen there is a black character, it\xe2\x80\x99s clearly a black character,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. McNeil said.'
b'The discussion of biracial identity in Japan got a boost in 2015 when Ariana Miyamoto, who is half-Japanese, half-African-American, won the Miss Universe Japan pageant. She used her fame to discuss the plight of \xe2\x80\x9chafus,\xe2\x80\x9d but some in Japan were unwilling to accept her as a model of Japanese beauty. '
b'In interviews, Ms. Osaka has embraced her multicultural background.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMaybe it\xe2\x80\x99s because they can\xe2\x80\x99t really pinpoint what I am,\xe2\x80\x9d she said in 2016, \xe2\x80\x9cso it\xe2\x80\x99s like anybody can cheer for me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'An earlier version of this article misstated who drew the anime-style advertisement that featured Naomi Osaka with lighter skin. It was a team that Nissin commissioned, not the manga artist Takeshi Konomi, though the ad was based on Mr. Konomi\xe2\x80\x99s work.'

b"MONACO \xe2\x80\x94 Rafael Nadal is unsure how his latest injury return will go this week, even though it will be on the clay-court king's favorite surface."
b'The second-ranked Spaniard is coming back at the Monte Carlo Masters, a tournament he has won a record 11 times along with the French Open and Barcelona.'
b'"It has been a tough year and a half for me, so it\'s tough to have a clear view about how I am," Nadal said Monday at the French Riviera tournament, where he plays Spanish countryman Roberto Bautista Agut in the second round on Wednesday.'
b'"I had too many stops; I didn\'t find a way to play three weeks in a row without problems. So it has been hard for me. When you have these things going on, on the mental side it\'s up and down. It\'s always like a comeback."'
b"Even Toni Nadal, his uncle and former coach, was skeptical about Nadal's long-term future in tennis in an interview with El Pais last month."
b'"Rafael wants to continue playing, despite his physical problems," Toni said. "That is what will continue to be decisive. Until when, who knows? Maybe two or three more years. What I\'m saying is that Rafael is not a tennis player, he\'s an injured person who plays tennis."'
b'Responding on Monday, the 32-year-old Nadal said his uncle had apologized for the comments.'
b'"He came to the court and felt sorry for that. Toni wanted to say it in a positive way because of course I had many issues," Nadal said. "Toni has conferences for companies every week. So when you talk a lot, sometimes you make some mistakes."'
b'Bautista Agut beat top-ranked Novak Djokovic at the Miami Open last month \xe2\x80\x94 where Nadal did not play. His troublesome right knee had flared up again the previous tournament, forcing him to pull out of his semifinal against Roger Federer at Indian Wells.'
b'Nadal resumed practice two weeks ago and his knee is holding up.'
b'"My knee is quite good. Happy for that. Now I need to work on the tennis," he said. "I hope the competition puts me in the rhythm I need."'
b'Nadal usually finds his rhythm quicker than anyone on clay.'
b'Last year, he missed February and March after retiring in the fifth set of his Australian Open quarterfinal against Marin Cilic with a hip injury.'
b'However, it did not stop him reeling off 14 straight wins on clay without dropping a set \xe2\x80\x94 winning two Davis Cup matches, the Monte Carlo and Barcelona titles before Dominic Thiem stopped him in the Madrid Masters quarterfinals.'
b'Nadal went on to win the Rome Masters and French Open and reached the Wimbledon semifinals on grass, losing an epic five-setter to Djokovic.'
b'Then his body let him down, again.'
b'After retiring from the U.S. Open semifinals against Juan Martin del Potro because of a right knee injury, he did not play again last season \xe2\x80\x94 pulling out of the Paris Masters and the season-ending ATP Finals with an abdominal problem.'
b'"I don\'t like to talk about frustration," Nadal said. "Because life has been too good to me to be frustrated."'
b"Nadal has won more than $100 million in prize money and 80 titles, including a record 33 Masters events. His tally of 17 Grand Slams is second to Federer's 20."
b'But nagging doubts persist.'
b'"At some point, even if I appreciate everything this sport has given to me, sometimes it\'s tough to accept when you have problems in a row," he said. "Since the beginning of the season again it has been tough. You need to be strong mentally and keep the passion very high."'
b'But Nadal did manage a lighter note about his uncle\'s "overdramatic" prognosis.'
b'"Being No. 2 in the world, it is maybe difficult to be where I am being an injured person," Nadal said, smiling. "I have more problems than almost the rest of my competitors, but I was able to manage it well all my life."'

b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 Amanda Anisimova is seen by many as the future of American tennis, but she sometimes yearns for a second opinion from a third eye.'
b'She drives by so many psychic readers around her home in South Florida. \xe2\x80\x9cI always want to go in,\xe2\x80\x9d Anisimova, 17, said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m kind of scared, because I don\xe2\x80\x99t want to know what my future is going to look like: I want it to be a surprise,\xe2\x80\x9d she added. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I want to hear what they have to say.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'No clairvoyance was necessary to see Anisimova\xe2\x80\x99s potential as she dominated 11th-seeded Aryna Sabalenka, 6-3, 6-2, on Friday to reach the fourth round of the Australian Open. That victory made Anisimova the first player born this century to reach the second week of a Grand Slam tournament, and the youngest American to do so since Serena Williams at the 1998 French Open.'
b'Not all forecasts were accurate, however: Before the match began, a Tennis Australia \xe2\x80\x9cWin Predictor\xe2\x80\x9d graphic gave Anisimova only a 9 percent chance of beating Sabalenka, who was a popular pick to win the tournament among many pundits and the oddsmakers\xe2\x80\x99 third favorite behind only Williams and Angelique Kerber.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s a pretty rough number \xe2\x80\x94 I\xe2\x80\x99m surprised by that,\xe2\x80\x9d Anisimova said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut she\xe2\x80\x99s a top player; she\xe2\x80\x99s had such a great year. I was just playing really well, and she was playing really well, too. We had a great match, and it just ended up going my way today.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Anisimova, ranked 87th, is likely to be undaunted by her next opponent: sixth-seeded Petra Kvitova, whom she beat last year in Indian Wells, Calif.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEvery player here is going to be great, and every round is going to be tough,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cI just focus on myself, and I\xe2\x80\x99m not really scared of anyone. I don\xe2\x80\x99t fear anyone. I just have a lot of confidence in myself, and I\xe2\x80\x99m ready for tough matches.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Although Anisimova\xe2\x80\x99s ability to dictate play against the ultra-aggressive Sabalenka gained more attention, one of her hardest matches came in her first round against the tricky veteran Monica Niculescu, who plays a game chock-full of funky slices that have driven many more established players crazy.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere isn\xe2\x80\x99t a teenager who would have won the first round against Niculescu besides Amanda,\xe2\x80\x9d said her agent, Max Eisenbud. \xe2\x80\x9cThat match, until today\xe2\x80\x99s match, was her most impressive win. The way Niculescu slices and throws everything at you, it was getting tight, and she was able to perform. A crafty, experienced girl who threw everything at her, and she still won in straight sets.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Eisenbud also represents the player to whom Anisimova is most often compared: Maria Sharapova. While he said that comparisons between the two \xe2\x80\x94 blondes with Russian roots who stormed the tennis stage at a young age \xe2\x80\x94 were unfair to both, he observed that Anisimova and Sharapova did share a diligent work ethic and an ability not to be fazed in the biggest moments.'
b'Frances Tiafoe, who also reached the second week of a Grand Slam for the first time on Friday, gushed over Anisimova, in his own way.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s like she\xe2\x80\x99s been a veteran,\xe2\x80\x9d Tiafoe said. \xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s going out here, and Sabalenka is playing great tennis \xe2\x80\x94 she routined her like it was nothing. It was barbecue chicken for her. It\xe2\x80\x99s unbelievable.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In her news conference Friday, Anisimova said that her confidence was growing.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI believe in myself so much more than I ever did in this tournament,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s just trusting myself. That\xe2\x80\x99s why I have been also playing really well.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That confidence leads her to hope she can follow in Sharapova\xe2\x80\x99s footsteps in another way: by becoming a Grand Slam champion as a teenager. Asked what her dream was for her career, Anisimova expressed a desire for instant gratification.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI want to win this tournament \xe2\x80\x94 right now,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, smiling.'
b'Anisimova, who broke through at the junior level by winning the 2017 United States Open girls\xe2\x80\x99 title, complements her desire for immediacy with an uncommon curiosity about the past, expressing her admiration for Billie Jean King, the pioneer who played a formative role in getting women\xe2\x80\x99s professional tennis off the ground.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBack then it was so different and so difficult,\xe2\x80\x9d Anisimova said. \xe2\x80\x9cHow much she worked, it was just crazy. Everything that she was doing just really surprised me. And that\xe2\x80\x99s something also I remember: I tell myself I\xe2\x80\x99m tired after an easy day \xe2\x80\x94 then seeing how much stuff she was doing? It was amazing how much she\xe2\x80\x99s done for the WTA and women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Modern issues are also a concern for Anisimova. She was particularly affected by the shooting last February that killed 17 at Marjory Stoneman Douglas High School in Parkland, Fla., near where she trains.'

b'While Caroline Wozniacki and Roger Federer aim to defend their singles titles in Melbourne, some younger players have shown signs that they can make a run. '
b'By Geoff Macdonald'
b'Khachanov, a 22-year-old Russian, began 2018 ranked 45th in the world and enters the Australian Open as the No. 10 seed. He gave Rafael Nadal all he could handle in a hugely entertaining four-set match in the third round of the United States Open, and then won the Paris Masters  by defeating four straight top-10 opponents: John Isner, Alexander Zverev, Dominic Thiem and top-ranked Novak Djokovic. Khachanov, who is 6-foot-5, has a huge serve and a Western forehand with a long, flowing backswing that suddenly accelerates at the ball, giving the impression that he is a cracking whip. It makes the shot nearly impossible to read. '
b'Coric, 22, has not won a match in four previous trips to the Australian Open, but he had an extraordinary 2018: reaching a career-high ranking of 12th,  defeating Roger Federer twice and, with Marin Cilic, leading Croatia to its second Davis Cup title. A left-hander by nature who plays right-handed, Coric is 6-2 with a game that has evolved from a defensive, counterpunching style to a more aggressive, opportunistic brand of tennis. He has developed a superb serve, and his return of serve puts enormous pressure on his opponent. His two-handed backhand is considered one of the best in the game. His forehand, once a liability, is much improved. '
b'Medvedev, a 22-year-old Russian,  rose from No. 65 to No. 16 in the world in 2018 and attributes his ascent to a better serve and more control of his temper. He won in Tokyo in October with dominant serving, dropping just one set as he captured his third tour title. Last week, he reached the final in Brisbane with wins over Andy Murray, Milos Raonic and Jo-Wilfried Tsonga, then lost in three sets to a resurgent Kei Nishikori. A lanky 6-6, Medvedev does not look powerful, but he hits the ball cleanly with perfect timing and with great disguise. He can serve bombs and also hit wide serves with a spin that opens up the court for his second shot. '
b'Sabalenka, a 20-year-old from Belarus, opened her 2019 season with a stirring three-set victory over Alison Riske to win the Shenzhen Open. Sabalenka began 2018 ranked 73rd, but under the tutelage of Dmitry Tursunov, a former tour player, she has risen to No. 11 by harnessing her prodigious power game and staying in points longer with improved shot selection. Her breakthrough came in the Cincinnati event in August, when she reached the semifinals with wins over Johanna Konta, Karolina Pliskova, Caroline Garcia and Madison Keys. She followed that by winning the Connecticut Open in New Haven, and then upsetting Petra Kvitova to reach the fourth round at the United States Open. The 6-foot Sabalenka serves with power and heavy spin, backing that up with a fearsome Western forehand. But what really makes her a threat is the way she plays fearlessly in the big moments of a close match.'
b'Barty, a 22-year-old Australian, had a breakout season in 2018, winning her first Grand Slam doubles title at the United States Open (with CoCo Vandeweghe), and reaching a career-high singles ranking of 15th. In Sydney last week, she upset world No. 1 Simona Halep in straight sets. Barty has an exceptional all-court game, using her athleticism and wide array of shots to confound opponents. Although she is only 5-5, Barty leads the WTA Tour in second serve points won, using her heavy kick serve to pull the returner out of position and then attacking the first ball with her powerful forehand. With her superb volleys and overhead, Barty looks to attack the net, often approaching behind her one-handed slice backhand, which is considered the best in the game. Expect the Australian fans to turn Barty\xe2\x80\x99s matches into rollicking events.'
b'Keys, a 23-year-old American who was the runner-up to Sloane Stephens in singles at the 2017 United States Open, last year reached the quarterfinals of the Australian Open, as well as the semifinals of the French Open and the United States Open. But her other results were somewhat lackluster, and she enters this week ranked 17th. Keys struggled to find a coach to replace Lindsay Davenport, who stopped traveling to spend more time with her family. In December, Keys hired Jim Madrigal, who guided Tennys Sandgren on his run to the quarterfinals in Melbourne a year ago. At 5-10, Keys has one of the game\xe2\x80\x99s best first serves, and she generates astonishing pace with her ground strokes. But she ranks only 27th on tour in second serve points won, at just over 47 percent. An improvement in this area could pay off for Keys. '
b"Geoff Macdonald is the women's tennis coach at Vanderbilt University.  "

b'On Tennis'
b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'INDIAN WELLS, Calif. \xe2\x80\x94 Deservedly No. 1 in the world at age 21, Naomi Osaka has not made it past the round of 16 in her first two tournaments wearing the crown.'
b'After stumbling at the first hurdle in Dubai last month, she won two matches here in Indian Wells before running into Belinda Bencic.'
b'Though it is too early to start scurrying around the halls and sounding the alarms, it is not too early to observe that Osaka is in the midst of an adjustment process that could take more time to work through than she imagined.'
b'In a little more than six months, the Japanese-American with Haitian roots has become a multicultural star with global reach, fired the coach who helped her zoom to No. 1 by winning two Grand Slam singles titles in a row, and hired a new coach who had yet to be a head coach at this level.'
b'It is a lot to handle, a lot to digest, particularly with people like me poised to parse every performance for signs of trouble.'
b'Bencic gave her plenty to digest, beating Osaka at her own game on Tuesday by taking time and the initiative away as she ended Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s title defense in just 66 minutes in the round of 16 by the no-argument score of 6-3, 6-1.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNaomi was rushed and didn\xe2\x80\x99t have time to dictate,\xe2\x80\x9d said Chris Evert, an 18-time Grand Slam singles champion. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think Naomi had come across a player like that. All these big hitters like Aryna Sabalenka, and even Serena, are not that close to the baseline. They are two or three feet back. But Bencic plays an entirely different game, and she played a flawless match. She\xe2\x80\x99s back, very back.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The proof is in her 11-match winning streak, which includes a title in Dubai and five victories over top-10 players. Born in 1997, the same year as Osaka, Bencic has the skills to challenge her often in the seasons to come if she can keep her head and health together. Bencic will play fifth-seeded Karolina Pliskova in the quarterfinals on Thursday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think at a time like this with that score line, I would usually feel very depressed and sad,\xe2\x80\x9d Osaka said at her surprisingly upbeat post-match news conference. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I feel pretty good right now, because I think given the circumstances I tried my best, and I don\xe2\x80\x99t really have any regrets. I tried to be positive throughout the entire match. Honestly, she was just playing so well.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It was not Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s first look at Bencic, who turned 22 this month. They first played in a small-money event in Alabama on clay in 2013, and Osaka beat Bencic, 6-3, 6-3, which came as a shock considering that Bencic already was a highly regarded junior player from Switzerland and that Osaka had barely played junior tennis at all.'
b'But there was no catching Bencic by surprise on Tuesday. She already had beaten Osaka in straight sets at the 2018 Hopman Cup team event, which is technically an exhibition. And after reaching the top 10 in 2016 and then dropping back because of wrist surgery, she is playing with the point-by-point focus of someone who knows that tennis success, with all its trappings, is not a given.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI know how frustrating it was when I wasn\xe2\x80\x99t able to play at all,\xe2\x80\x9d Bencic said, sounding sage beyond her years.'
b'Osaka sounds a bit wiser herself. The meandering, sometimes cryptic interviews of 2018 have given way to something more considered and open with occasional dashes of her trademark whimsy.'
b'This is not a coincidence. She watched clips of her past news conferences and did not like some of what she saw: the \xe2\x80\x9cums,\xe2\x80\x9d the \xe2\x80\x9clikes.\xe2\x80\x9d At this new stage, she greets questions, of which there are many, with respect, giving the impression that she is weighing each one before answering.'
b'Asked to compare herself now with when she won Indian Wells as an unseeded player in 2018, she gave another measured response, even in defeat.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI guess one of the biggest things is I wanted to be more mature,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cI feel like this is something I\xe2\x80\x99m still working on \xe2\x80\x94 on and off the court. It\xe2\x80\x99s one of the biggest goals that I have had in my entire life.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI might have thrown a few tantrums last year,\xe2\x80\x9d she added. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd this year it\xe2\x80\x99s something that I\xe2\x80\x99m working on improving, and I feel like it\xe2\x80\x99s going well. I think I\xe2\x80\x99m just more confident in myself.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Dismissing Sascha Bajin, her silken-voiced German coach, was certainly a bold move. Under his guidance, she defeated Serena Williams, Bajin\xe2\x80\x99s former employer, twice in 2018: once in the first round in Miami and once under much more duress in the United States Open final. With Bajin still by her side, but apparently no longer in her confidence, Osaka fought through another rough-and-tumble draw to win the Australian Open in January.'
b'Neither has explained their split in detail, although Osaka has said it was not a matter of money. She or some members of her team were looking for a lower-profile coach, but there were clearly personal issues at work, too.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSomething happened that must not have been good, although that\xe2\x80\x99s just speculation,\xe2\x80\x9d said Evert, who often watched Osaka and Bajin train in Boca Raton, Fla. \xe2\x80\x9cThey were laughing and having fun practices and teasing each other, and it was great, and then just before the Australian and after the Australian, it was tense.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Bajin is gone now, replaced by Jermaine Jenkins, a former standout at Clemson University who spent several years as the main hitting partner for Venus Williams, who dismissed her coach, David Witt, and Jenkins in the off-season.'
b'Jenkins was quickly hired as a national coach by the United States Tennis Association to work out of its national campus in Orlando. He was just settling in when he got a text message from Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s agent, Stuart Duguid, inquiring about his availability.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI had a great new gig at the U.S.T.A., and I was doing my expense report and I get that text message,\xe2\x80\x9d Jenkins said with a chuckle this week. \xe2\x80\x9cWhen a great adventure is offered to you, you cannot refuse it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Jenkins, 34, knows full well that job security at this level is fragile, which is one of the big reasons he was drawn to the U.S.T.A. post.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMy wife and I live there in Lake Nona,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cPlus, with the coaching carousel, I didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to go back out with another player and then they wake up on the wrong side of the bed and say, \xe2\x80\x98Hey I\xe2\x80\x99m not feeling this.\xe2\x80\x99 I was thinking more about security because there are only a few, I feel like, out there that are worth being out here for.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Osaka, with her talent and star power, is certainly on that short list, and she and Jenkins are now 2-1 after their first tournament together, which included one on-court coaching visit that Osaka jokingly began by suggesting she was having a midlife crisis.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI just wanted to break the ice,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Keeping the mood light and keeping tennis in perspective seem like the right idea when there are all sorts of new and powerful forces at work, including celebrity and megamillions.'
b'This also seems a good time for Osaka to remember that the controlled power and controlled emotion that she displayed to win in New York and again in Australia were anything but a fluke.'

b'On March 2 in Dubai, Roger Federer joined Jimmy Connors as the only male tennis players in the open era with 100 career titles. With a victory on Sunday over John Isner in the final of the Miami Open, Federer, 37, is now eight titles behind Connors\xe2\x80\x99s record of 109. '
b'Here\xe2\x80\x99s a look at Federer\xe2\x80\x99s 101 titles.'
b'The date Federer won his first career title, at age 19, in Milan, defeating Julien Boutter of France, 6-4, 6-7 (7), 6-4. Federer was ranked 27th at the time, Boutter 67th. Boutter reached only two finals on the ATP Tour, winning one, and reached a career-high ranking of 46th. His last tour event was Wimbledon in 2004, a tournament Federer won. (The Milan tournament no longer exists.)'
b'Number of Grand Slam titles \xe2\x80\x94 eight at Wimbledon, six at the Australian Open, five at the United States Open and one at the French Open. His most recent came at the 2018 Australian Open.'
b'The number of times he has won the tournaments in Halle, Germany, and his hometown, Basel, Switzerland \xe2\x80\x94 his most of any events. '
b'Number of titles on hard courts, most of any surface. (Hard courts are the most common surface on tour.) He has won 18 tournaments on grass and 11 on clay. His first title, in Milan, is one of only two on indoor carpet.'
b'Most titles in one year, in 2006. The first came against Ga\xc3\xabl Monfils in Doha, Qatar, in January; the last against James Blake at the Masters Cup, the former name of the year-end finals, in Shanghai in November.'
b'The only year since 2001 in which Federer has not won a tournament. He sustained a knee injury in January and shut down his season in late July in order to fully recover. '
b'Number of countries in which Federer has won a title, including Japan, Qatar, Sweden, Canada, Portugal, Turkey and the Netherlands. '
b'Number of different opponents, from 25 different countries, who Federer defeated in finals \xe2\x80\x94 including Novak Djokovic, Jiri Novak, Philipp Kohlschreiber, Mark Philippoussis, Andre Agassi, Igor Andreev, David Nalbandian and Nikolay Davydenko. Twenty-five of those opponents are now retired, according to the ATP. '
b'Number of times he has beaten Rafael Nadal in a final, most of any opponent. Who\xe2\x80\x99s No. 2? Andy Roddick, with seven. '
b'Number of times he won a tournament final in straight sets. '
b'Length of his shortest title-clinching win, a 6-2 6-2 victory over David Goffin in Basel in 2014.'
b'Length of his longest title-clinching win, a 5-7, 7-6 (6), 7-6 (5), 3-6, 16-14 victory over Roddick in the 2009 Wimbledon final. The victory gave Federer his 15th major title, breaking Pete Sampras\xe2\x80\x99s record.'
b'His lowest ranked opponent in a final, but it was a familiar name. On Oct. 2, 2005, Federer, then 24, defeated 18-year-old Andy Murray, 6-3 7-5, in the final of the Thailand Open in Bangkok. It was the first of 25 career meetings between the two, and the first ATP Tour final of Murray\xe2\x80\x99s career. '
b'Number of times Federer defeated Ivan Ljubicic in a tournament final. Ljubicic, 40, is now one of Federer\xe2\x80\x99s coaches. '
b'Number of times Federer has lost in a tournament final, missing a chance to add to his trophy case. '
b'Ben Rothenberg contributed reporting.'

b'On Tennis'
b'By Kurt Streeter'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 With the benefit of hindsight it is easy to see that these past two weeks at the Australian Open have been nothing more than a warm-up for Rafael Nadal and Novak Djokovic.'
b'Maybe we should have kept from wasting time on the men\xe2\x80\x99s side and gone straight to the showcase, the final on Sunday, when two titans will revive their rivalry and battle once again for the Australian Open crown.'
b'The question of who would meet in the final became clear on Friday evening, as Djokovic cruised past the French underdog Lucas Pouille, winning, 6-0, 6-2, 6-2.'
b'It was a demolition both thorough and brief, and it mirrored what Nadal had done in his final four clash the night before, when he dismantled fast-rising Stefanos Tsitsipas of Greece.'
b'Nadal took 106 minutes, lightning fast for a match at that stage of a Grand Slam. Djokovic versus Pouille lasted only 83 minutes, with Djokovic riding his precision groundstrokes and feline quickness to the win.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cA perfect match for me,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic described it. \xe2\x80\x9cFrom the first to the last point.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He looked calmly self-assured as he said this \xe2\x80\x94 nothing like the doubtful athlete who struggled through a nasty elbow injury and upset losses in Melbourne in 2017 and 2018, during the one confounding low period in his career. His performance on Friday had a transcendent quality, he said, and he called such a feeling \xe2\x80\x9cdivine\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cin the zone, where everything flows so effortlessly and you are executing everything you are intending to execute.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He added that the semifinal was one of the best matches he had played on the sea blue center court at Rod Laver Arena.'
b'That\xe2\x80\x99s saying a lot.'
b'He was speaking, after all, of the court on which he will soon be aiming for a record seventh Australian Open title; of the court on which he won the first of his 14 major titles, when he beat another French player, Jo-Wilfried Tsonga, in 2008.'
b'It is also the court where he played one of the most stirring, and still the longest, Grand Slam finals in tennis history: the 5-hour-53-minute war of wills he won against Nadal in 2012, one of the greatest matches ever played, after which both players struggled to stay upright at the trophy ceremony.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHopefully,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic cracked, \xe2\x80\x9cwe don\xe2\x80\x99t go that long this time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'You never know.'
b'Djokovic brawling against Nadal for the 53rd time \xe2\x80\x94 Djokovic leads, 27-25 \xe2\x80\x94 is expected to scintillate. It may awaken memories of when the two were younger, fresher, but not necessarily better, versions of what they are today, when they seem far and away the two best on the planet, their old rivals diminished or injured or close to retirement, their new rivals not ready yet.'
b'For sports fans in the United States, this is one of those events worth setting the clock for, a match scheduled to start at the very uncivilized time of 3:30 a.m. Eastern on Sunday.'
b'Just as in the run-up to the 2012 final, the Serb, Djokovic, is ranked No. 1 in the world, and the Spaniard, Nadal, is No. 2 and nipping at his heels.'
b'But seven years on, they are also very different. The Nadal of Melbourne 2019 is riding a game he has clearly modified for this event \xe2\x80\x94 a change made, he has acknowledged, as an adaptation to being 32.'
b'Here, at a tournament in which he has not lost a single set, he is looking to keep his legs spry, his troublesome knees healthy. He is hitting more balls on the short hop, sticking closer to the baseline, volleying more. He has also streamlined his service motion, cutting fat from his windup in a search for more accuracy and greater pop.'
b'Djokovic can see the difference. Speaking of the man he described as his primary rival (take that, Roger Federer), Djokovic noted that the changes were working for Nadal.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think he\xe2\x80\x99s backing his first shot up with that great serve, saving energy, and then he can go for more in the return game,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cWith everything he possesses, all the qualities in his game, adding a lot of free points on the serve makes him much tougher to play against.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Both players have had to adapt, had to overcome recent difficulty, to get to this point. Nadal arrived in Melbourne with low expectations, having taken a hiatus from the tour after last fall\xe2\x80\x99s United States Open, where he withdrew in the semifinals, citing a leg injury. In November, he had ankle surgery.'
b'Dogged by his injured elbow at last year\xe2\x80\x99s Australian Open, Djokovic was routed in the quarterfinals by Hyeon Chung, a South Korean ranked No. 58 at the time. That loss was one of a batch of stunning upsets he suffered in major championships after winning the French Open in 2016. Plenty of questions were swirling around him at the time. He often wore a hangdog, puzzled look on his face during matches, where once there had been nothing but ice-cold surety.'
b'Would he ever return to form?'
b'But then, last summer, after elbow surgery and a remodeling of his priorities and his coaching team, the old Djokovic emerged. His health returned. So, too, did his steel-trap resolve. He won Wimbledon, beating Nadal in a five-set marathon that Djokovic credited here with giving \xe2\x80\x9ca different, more confident self.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Later in the summer, he won his 14th Grand Slam at a sweltering U.S. Open, tightening his grip on the top of the men\xe2\x80\x99s rankings.'
b'Now he finds himself again in a Melbourne final, with a chance to repeat the glory of 2012, a chance for a 15th Grand Slam, just two behind the Spaniard\xe2\x80\x99s haul of 17, within striking distance of Federer, who sits at 20 for most in a career.'
b'At his postmatch news conference, I asked Djokovic to imagine a future conversation with his two children, who were not yet born seven years ago, and how he would describe that last epic Melbourne night against Nadal.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHow would I describe it?\xe2\x80\x9d he said, pausing before adding a touch of humor. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll probably not have them sit down and watch it because I don\xe2\x80\x99t like my children to watch TV that long.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Then he grew serious.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI would probably present it in more a general concept of our rivalry. That match would be icing on the cake.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'On Sunday, seeking a seventh Australian Open title, he will have the chance to add more icing, indeed a whole extra layer, to that cake, to the legacy of a glorious career.'
b'An earlier version of this article misidentified the tournament Novak Djokovic won in 2016 before suffering a batch of upsets in major tournaments. It was the French Open, not Wimbledon.'

b'By Ben Rothenberg'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 To show a fuller picture of the sport, women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis is shining the spotlight on the coaches who travel the tour with its players.'
b'For 10 years, the WTA has allowed on-court coaching at regular tour events. At this year\xe2\x80\x99s Australian Open, coaches have given news conferences of their own, following their players to the podium after matches. Last season, for the first time, the WTA awarded a Coach of the Year Award, which went to Naomi Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s coach, Sascha Bajin.'
b'But nothing drew more attention to tennis coaches than one getting in trouble. Coaching during a match is not allowed at Grand Slam tournaments, and Serena Williams was assessed a code violation in the women\xe2\x80\x99s final at the United States Open in September when the chair umpire, Carlos Ramos, spotted her coach, Patrick Mouratoglou, gesturing toward her from his seat. His hand movements were replayed as much as any shot from the tournament.'
b'Williams\xe2\x80\x99s ire over the penalty, which she felt was akin to calling her a cheater, set off a series of penalties that overshadowed the match, which was won by Osaka.'
b'Afterward, Mouratoglou admitted to making the signals, but added, \xe2\x80\x9cEveryone is doing it, 100 percent of the time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Four months later, at the Australian Open, he continued to insist that the rules should change because coaching from the stands is already \xe2\x80\x9ccompletely tolerated \xe2\x80\x94 except for one or two people who think they\xe2\x80\x99re different.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ramos is officiating matches at this tournament, but he was not assigned to one featuring Williams, who lost in the quarterfinals on Wednesday. At least one prominent player \xe2\x80\x94 the men\xe2\x80\x99s semifinalist Stefanos Tsitsipas \xe2\x80\x94 has been cited for illegal coaching in Melbourne.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think it should become legal because we stop hypocrisy, first of all,\xe2\x80\x9d Mouratoglou said. \xe2\x80\x9cSecond, because it\xe2\x80\x99s great for the show, and we want to have viewers who are not 50 years old. We want to attract the young generation, and we\xe2\x80\x99re not. Tennis is not attracting the young people. And third, I think it\xe2\x80\x99s good for the players.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Despite the WTA\xe2\x80\x99s calling for coaching to be allowed across the sport after the incident at the U.S. Open, neither the men\xe2\x80\x99s tour nor the Grand Slam tournaments have moved in that direction.'
b'Steve Simon, the WTA chief executive, said that coaches \xe2\x80\x9ccontribute an integral element to the on-court and off-court WTA story.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Simon\xe2\x80\x99s predecessors have seen coaches as resources for enriching its product before. Allowing on-court coaching 10 years ago was motivated more by entertainment considerations than any desire for improving tactics.'
b'Larry Scott, then the tour\xe2\x80\x99s chief executive, said the rule change came from a desire for \xe2\x80\x9cbeing as fan-friendly as possible and being as responsive to television as possible without altering the fundamentals of the sport.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Holding news conferences with coaches is part of an initiative spearheaded by the tour\xe2\x80\x99s communications manager, Chase Altieri, who came to the WTA in 2017 after working in the N.F.L., where coaches\xe2\x80\x99 briefings have long been a feature of news media coverage.'
b'WTA coaches have embraced the program, both for the chance to articulate their views and to ease the burden on their players. Bajin has made television appearances in lieu of Osaka to lighten her schedule of obligations during tournaments.'
b'A new section of the WTA website includes profiles of the coaches, with details like their current and previous partnerships and off-court interests. Simon said the goal was to \xe2\x80\x9cbring our fans inside our sport.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In recent years, the U.S. Open and the Australian Open have begun with allowing coaching during the qualifying rounds, with players able to walk to the side of the court where their coach is sitting during changeovers if they desire a consultation.'
b'Mouratoglou is one of the strongest advocates for on-court coaching, even though his player never uses it. He said Williams\xe2\x80\x99s sense of self-reliance was a weapon he would not dare muzzle.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think that her No. 1 quality is to be the best competitor ever, and I don\xe2\x80\x99t want her to think that suddenly she needs someone to be a better competitor; that would make her weaker,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cSo, for me, it doesn\xe2\x80\x99t make sense for someone like her.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mouratoglou, who has worked with Williams since 2012, owns a tennis academy that bears his name in France and has been a television analyst for ESPN and Eurosport. He said tennis had many untapped areas that could be mined for entertainment purposes.'

b'Bajin, who worked alongside Mouratoglou for years when he was Williams\xe2\x80\x99s hitting partner, comes down on the opposite side of the coaching debate, saying the rule should not be changed \xe2\x80\x9cto make it more interesting\xe2\x80\x9d to watch tennis.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think it takes away the purity that tennis was,\xe2\x80\x9d Bajin said. \xe2\x80\x9cMy father put me out there on the court in order to become more independent, to learn how to handle problems, to learn how to be by myself, so that nobody can help me \xe2\x80\x94 and I think that still parents do that for their kids.
