b'Dylan Alcott, a Grand Slam champion in wheelchair tennis, is a celebrity in his native Australia, extending his influence far beyond the court. '
b'By Ben Rothenberg'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 It can take a long time for Dylan Alcott, a paraplegic 28-year-old from a nearby suburb, to maneuver his wheelchair from one place to another around the Australian Open.'
b'He\xe2\x80\x99s not slow; he\xe2\x80\x99s just popular.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPeople used to stare at me when I was growing up because I was in a wheelchair, and I hated it,\xe2\x80\x9d Alcott said. \xe2\x80\x9cNow they\xe2\x80\x99re staring at me because they know me. How amazing is that? It\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x98Oh, that\xe2\x80\x99s Dylan!\xe2\x80\x99 Not, \xe2\x80\x98Oh, there\xe2\x80\x99s a guy in a wheelchair.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After first gaining recognition for winning a 2008 Paralympic gold medal in wheelchair basketball at 17, Alcott has come to dominate the quad division of wheelchair tennis, winning seven Grand Slam singles titles, including five at the Australian Open. He won his fifth in a row here on Saturday at Rod Laver Arena, which seats 15,000.'
b'Quad tennis is a small and obscure world, often featuring only four players at major tournaments. But Alcott\xe2\x80\x99s visibility extends far beyond the reach of a tennis stadium. He is the face of ANZ, a bank that is one of the Open\xe2\x80\x99s major sponsors, and appears in advertisements around the grounds and on television. Alcott also served as a courtside analyst for Nine, the Australian network that broadcasts the tournament. During the rest of the year, he works as a radio host for national music stations.'
b'When the broadcaster Gerard Whateley introduced Alcott at a meet-and-greet event on Monday, he made it clear Alcott needed no introduction: \xe2\x80\x9cYou, sir, are inescapable!\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Being seen and heard as much as possible is a mission in itself for Alcott.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen I was a kid and I was getting bullied at school and I was really upset, I\xe2\x80\x99d say, \xe2\x80\x98I don\xe2\x80\x99t know anyone like me, I don\xe2\x80\x99t see anyone like me on the TV or on the radio or the newspaper, and that sucks! That\xe2\x80\x99s not fair,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d he said. '
b'Alcott said he did not grasp the power of his celebrity until his commercials began to air last year.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe got videos of a little kid in a wheelchair, and every time the ad comes on, he rolls over to the TV and hugs it, because he saw someone like him on TV,\xe2\x80\x9d Alcott said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe get hundreds like that, and that\xe2\x80\x99s so cool.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The attention can be exhausting, especially in the midst of competing in a Grand Slam event. Everywhere he goes around Melbourne, people stop, turn and smile in recognition. Though it can eat up hours of his day, Alcott swerves toward those people, rather than away from them, introducing himself and offering to take a photograph.'
b'Alcott also has savored the acceptance of his fellow athletes with whom he has shared the locker room, especially the Australian ones who he sees year-round at Melbourne Park. Last Saturday, Alcott chatted with the 20-time Grand Slam champion Roger Federer at the net when their sessions overlapped on a practice court.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s like you\xe2\x80\x99re just one of them,\xe2\x80\x9d Alcott said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey treat me so well, it\xe2\x80\x99s amazing. It\xe2\x80\x99s cool, and I don\xe2\x80\x99t think any other wheelchair athletes have that. They say, \xe2\x80\x98Hi,\xe2\x80\x99 and it\xe2\x80\x99s like they don\xe2\x80\x99t even know you\xe2\x80\x99re in a wheelchair.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'They do notice Alcott\xe2\x80\x99s popularity. Even Stefanos Tsitsipas, who became the Open\xe2\x80\x99s breakthrough star when he beat Federer in the fourth round, deferred to Alcott\xe2\x80\x99s celebrity.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI introduced myself to Tsitsipas,\xe2\x80\x9d Alcott said, \xe2\x80\x9cand he said, \xe2\x80\x98Mate, you\xe2\x80\x99re the most famous guy here, of course I know who you are!\xe2\x80\x99 I\xe2\x80\x99ll take that. That\xe2\x80\x99s surreal.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Kris Dent, an executive with the International Tennis Federation, said Alcott\xe2\x80\x99s appeal transcended sports.'
b" \xe2\x80\x9cYou can't fail to notice that when you come to Australia,\xe2\x80\x9d Dent said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe's become much more than just an athlete. It's a phenomenal story that he has.\xe2\x80\x9d "
b'The top-ranked man in able-bodied tennis, Novak Djokovic, has tried his skills in a wheelchair across the net from Alcott, which he said made him appreciate the challenge and the craft of the discipline.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cDylan deserves the popularity,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s a very great guy, very charismatic. I\xe2\x80\x99ve said it before, these guys are heroes to me, they really are. They make the game of tennis more beautiful and more unique because of what they do and how they do it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After winning Paralympic gold medals in singles and doubles in 2016, Alcott was presented Tennis Australia\xe2\x80\x99s Newcombe Medal, which goes annually to the country\xe2\x80\x99s top player. Alcott said winning an award in a general category rather than one designated for disabled athletes \xe2\x80\x9cfelt like breaking through.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Alcott was born with lipomeningocele, which caused a large tumor against his spinal cord. He underwent his first of many surgeries at five weeks old. Health struggles continued throughout his childhood, with his ability to use his extremities worsening at times, both gradually and suddenly.'
b'In 2012, an inebriated acquaintance tried to pick up his chair and dumped him onto the floor, which was covered in broken glass; Alcott severed an artery in his hand in the fall, damaging his ability to use his right hand fully, which is one of the reasons he competes in the quad division. That spelled the end of his wheelchair basketball career and led him to focus on tennis, which he had started playing around age 9 or 10.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe biggest thing is being really proud of my disability, which is kind of different,\xe2\x80\x9d Alcott said. \xe2\x80\x9cMost people don\xe2\x80\x99t want to talk about it. I always say, \xe2\x80\x98Nah, let\xe2\x80\x99s talk about it, openly and all the time.\xe2\x80\x99 People buy into that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Though frank and candid about his challenges, Alcott also has tried to share the fullness of his life. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPeople that have a car accident think their life is over, because road safety ads say, \xe2\x80\x98If you drink and drive and end up in a wheelchair, your life\xe2\x80\x99s over,\xe2\x80\x99 as a deterrence,\xe2\x80\x9d Alcott said. \xe2\x80\x9cPeople look at me and think it\xe2\x80\x99s the same.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That\xe2\x80\x99s why in his autobiography, \xe2\x80\x9cAble,\xe2\x80\x9d a best seller published last fall, he said, \xe2\x80\x9cI talk about the first time I had sex, when I travel, everything. To be given the platform to do that, that\xe2\x80\x99s so cool.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The platform for Alcott\xe2\x80\x99s tennis also is growing. His second round-robin match, a 6-7 (3), 6-4, 7-5 victory over David Wagner, was broadcast live on national television. In his on-court interview, Alcott seemed more ecstatic about the viewership than the victory, hoping that disabled people around Australia had watched and drawn inspiration. (By contrast, he won the United States Open in September on an indoor practice facility rather than a main stadium because of rain.) '
b'Alcott, a hip-hop fan who has rapped on stage with Ghostface Killah, started his own music festival, Ability Fest, which catered to the needs of disabled people often left out of such events. The event featured interpreters for the deaf and elevated platforms for seated viewers.'
b'Alcott also founded Get Skilled Access, a consulting group that works to improve how governments and corporations interact with disabled people. His foundation finances opportunities for disabled people because, he noted, he needs $8,000 for a wheelchair while his brother needed only $100 pair of shoes to play Australian Rules Football.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt might not be Paralympics; it might be a cello, it might be a scholarship to go to university and become a lawyer,\xe2\x80\x9d Alcott said. \xe2\x80\x9cWhy don\xe2\x80\x99t we see people with disabilities in boardroom, in the mainstream? It\xe2\x80\x99s because they haven\xe2\x80\x99t been given the opportunities, and we want to provide that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Alcott had a 28-3 record last year on quad tennis circuit, which is for players with at least three extremities affected by a permanent physical disability. He hopes he, too, can grow into something bigger and more powerful than just a tennis player.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI could win 20 Grand Slams and I\xe2\x80\x99d be happy,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I\xe2\x80\x99d regret not doing what I love the most, which is changing perceptions of disability, which broadcasting helps.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Alcott said he would like to move to New York or London to reach a wider audience.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhy couldn\xe2\x80\x99t a guy in a wheelchair be the next Jimmy Fallon, or whatever it is?\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'As he started to expand on his vision for success in America, Alcott stopped and gestured to something much closer: a girl standing a few meters away, staring at him with a huge smile and tears in her eyes.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHello! I\xe2\x80\x99m Dylan,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cHow are you, what\xe2\x80\x99s your name? Jessica, what\xe2\x80\x99s going on? Want to get a photo?\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 The first point of the Australian Open men\xe2\x80\x99s final on Sunday told the story of all that was to come.'
b'With his opening serve, Novak Djokovic stretched Rafael Nadal wide, sending the Spaniard sprawling. Djokovic quickly had his longtime rival exactly where he wanted: off balance and unglued.'
b'In a flash, as Nadal spun 360 degrees and scrambled to recover, Djokovic took a half-dozen confident steps forward. He lined up a backhand and then unleashed a buzzing winner that Nadal did not even try for.'
b'Point won. Point made. Rafael Nadal: toast.'
b'The match, held at Rod Laver Arena on a warm and slightly breezy evening, finished just 2 hours 4 minutes later, Djokovic winning in a full-blown knockout, 6-3, 6-2, 6-3.'
b'This was a win that tightened the 31-year-old Serb\xe2\x80\x99s hold on the top spot in men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis. It also elevated his name once again in the annals of tennis history. He now has a record seven Australian Open titles and has moved to sole possession of third place for major titles, with 15, breaking a tie with Pete Sampras.'
b'The three powerhouse sets were as fine and dominating as Djokovic \xe2\x80\x94 or anyone \xe2\x80\x94 has ever played in a major tournament final.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt ranks right at the top,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said, assessing his performance at a news conference. \xe2\x80\x9cAt this level, under these circumstances, it was truly a perfect match.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He could not have seen this coming. Nobody could.'
b'Djokovic versus Nadal, No. 1 vs. No. 2, was arguably the most anticipated match of the tournament. It was the first occasion in which these two tense rivals \xe2\x80\x94 who have now played 53 times on tour, with Djokovic winning 28 \xe2\x80\x94 had met in the finals of a Grand Slam event since 2014, when Nadal slipped by Djokovic in four sets at Roland Garros in Paris.'
b'Given the scintillating way both had performed throughout the tournament, with Nadal winning every set he played in his first six matches and with Djokovic winning all but two, it seemed certain that they would duel once again deep into the Melbourne night.'
b'It was a match that was expected to dust off hallowed memories of what might have been their greatest combined moment of glory. In 2012, the two played one of the most epic finals in Grand Slam history, right on Laver\xe2\x80\x99s sea-blue center court: a 5-hour-53-minute marathon won by Djokovic, the longest major final ever.'
b'But a reprise was not to be. What unfolded was not even a reasonable facsimile.'
b'Still, the night had its own way of being unforgettable. The final failed to offer drama, but it did present beauty \xe2\x80\x94 that of a top-flight athlete, among tennis\xe2\x80\x99s greatest champions, operating at the very peak of his powers.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThings started so quick,\xe2\x80\x9d Nadal said, snapping his fingers twice to emphasize the point. \xe2\x80\x9cHe was pushing me to every ball. He played so well. He hit so long. His return was fantastic. He was super quick.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Nadal, 32, did not appear particularly downcast after the match. Instead, it seemed as if he had simply resigned himself to the result. He noted that he had been injured and had not been able to prepare for the tournament as he had wished. Indeed, after pulling out of his semifinal match at the United States Open last September and then having ankle surgery, he had not played a match on tour until this tournament began.'
b'But he also allowed that there had been nothing he could really do on Sunday against Djokovic, saying it \xe2\x80\x9cwas unbelievable, the way that he played, no doubt about that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Djokovic made only nine unforced errors. He lost just one point on his serve in the first set. He aggressively shortened every rally he could, keeping them to an average of five shots, a stunningly low number considering the long-distance finals he and Nadal have slugged out in the past. Riding pinpoint accuracy and depth, he so flummoxed Nadal that the Spaniard once swung and whiffed on a forehand.'
b'Nadal, whose tally for major titles remains at 17, three behind Roger Federer\xe2\x80\x99s record, threw all he could muster at the match, especially as it drained from his grip. He worked in as many drop shots as he could. He altered positioning on his returns. He moved early, trying to guess which way Djokovic was serving.'
b'Nothing worked.'
b'Djokovic led early in every stanza and never looked back. There was no tension. The match was shorter by 23 minutes than Saturday\xe2\x80\x99s stirring women\xe2\x80\x99s final between Naomi Osaka and Petra Kvitova, which also unfolded in three sets but was blessed by tension at every turn.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFor me, one of the most important objectives for the match was to start off well and bring the intensity and make sure that he also feels my presence,\xe2\x80\x9d said Djokovic, who looked remarkably calm and centered, both during the match and afterward. \xe2\x80\x9cHe always makes sure that the opponent across the net feels his presence. That is how he plays. That\xe2\x80\x99s how he behaves. He brings so much energy, jumping around, sprinting.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was crucial for me to start off with an early break. Having a set under my belt just made me relax a bit more, not really worry too much. After that, it was smooth.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Smooth. Perfect summary.'
b'It was a rare lopsided Grand Slam final between men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis greats, reminiscent of Nadal\xe2\x80\x99s wipeout of Federer at the 2008 French Open and John McEnroe\xe2\x80\x99s rout of Jimmy Connors at Wimbledon in 1984.'
b'But it should not be forgotten how far the two came to get to the finals, the hurdles overcome. There is Nadal with his injuries, which have piled up over the years, especially on hard courts. There is Djokovic with the way he struggled with his confidence and his health after winning the French Open in 2016. For two full tennis seasons, it felt as if he was lost in the wilderness, in matches including a fourth-round loss at Melbourne Park last year to the unseeded South Korean Hyeon Chung.'
b'Djokovic underwent elbow surgery not long after that match. At first, the operation did not help his on-court results. He appeared to be a doubting and unhappy shadow of his self. Improbably, he found his game on the Wimbledon grass, winning the title there and then following that up with another championship at the U.S. Open in September.'
b'According to the International Tennis Federation, Djokovic is the first man to record three streaks of three or more Grand Slam titles in a row. He won four straight from Wimbledon in 2015 to the 2016 French Open, and three in a row from Wimbledon in 2011 to the 2012 Australian Open.'
b'His chance to hold all four major titles at the same time will come in four months at the French Open, which he has won only once (Nadal has been the champion at Roland Garros 11 times).'
b'Sustain this level through the United States Open, and it is not impossible to imagine him winning a calendar-year Grand Slam. No man has done that since Rod Laver in 1969.'
b'And what about reaching Federer\xe2\x80\x99s record 20 Grand Slam titles?'
b'Asked about those milestones on Sunday, Djokovic was his typically reflective self.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI am aware that making history of the sport that I truly love is something special,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'He then gave a nod to the kind of uncertainty that he knows very well, firsthand: the way injuries and loss of confidence can shake the very best of foundations. There are no sure bets.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHow many seasons are to come? I don\xe2\x80\x99t know,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, noting that he was trying hard not to get too far ahead of himself. \xe2\x80\x9cI do want to definitely focus myself on continuing to improve so I would be able to compete at such a high level for the years to come \xe2\x80\x94 and have a shot at eventually getting closer to Roger\xe2\x80\x99s record.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s still far.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'True, but if he keeps playing in the fluid, focused way he did on this Sunday evening in Melbourne, 20 Grand Slams will come into focus soon enough.'

b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 Could the 2019 Australian Open be the Grand Slam tournament in which a budding cast of young American men breaks through?'
b'The odds remain against that happening \xe2\x80\x94 thanks in part to a guy named Roger Federer \xe2\x80\x94 and there remains much tennis to be played. But after a pair of second-round upsets by Frances Tiafoe and Taylor Fritz on Wednesday, the stage just might be set.'
b'The first surprise came when Tiafoe, who turns 21 on Sunday, finished off fifth-seeded Kevin Anderson behind powerful forehands and serves. It was the biggest win of Tiafoe\xe2\x80\x99s young career and the biggest shock of the tournament so far.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cC\xe2\x80\x99mon!\xe2\x80\x9d he shouted, rolling up his right shirt sleeve, then thumping his right biceps repeatedly with his left hand, a move that seemed freighted with both bravado and relief. Tiafoe, the son of immigrants from Sierra Leone who learned the game at the Maryland tennis club where his father was a custodian, has long been touted as a prodigious talent. But he has also seemed burdened by the weight of expectations.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt means the world to me,\xe2\x80\x9d Tiafoe told a crowd he had clearly won over during the tense three-hour match.'
b'The arena scoreboard flashed with the final score, 4-6, 6-4, 6-4, 7-5, telling a story of its own. Early on, Anderson had pushed ahead, leading by 3-0 in the second set after winning the first. Then Tiafoe turned the tide.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI lost to Kevin three times last year,\xe2\x80\x9d Tiafoe, ranked No. 39, explained in an on-court interview. \xe2\x80\x9cI was down a set and break today. I went to a different place. I dug deep. It\xe2\x80\x99s just how bad you want it, and I wanted it bad.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Indeed, in the beginning, it looked as if Tiafoe might soon be flying home for more practice at the United States Tennis Association\xe2\x80\x99s campus in Orlando, Fla., where many young American hopefuls train. But then he altered his approach \xe2\x80\x94 and flashed the kind of game that he will have to employ if he is to get past Andreas Seppi of Italy, a tour veteran ranked No. 35, in the third round.'
b'He had decided to \xe2\x80\x9ckind of just mix it up,\xe2\x80\x9d he explained. \xe2\x80\x9cPlay smarter. Don\xe2\x80\x99t try to go for cannons. Be unpredictable.\xe2\x80\x9d Once he settled on a game plan, Tiafoe was particularly effective mixing a slew of low-bouncing slices into his powerful repertoire, forcing Anderson out of his comfort zone, making Anderson bend and contort his 6-foot-8 frame.'
b'How far can Tiafoe go at this tournament? When I posed that question to him, he was succinct. \xe2\x80\x9cTo the third round, man,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, before laughing slyly.'
b'Should Tiafoe beat Seppi on Friday, he would find himself deeper in a Grand Slam tournament than he has ever been. Maybe because he\xe2\x80\x99s keenly aware of that fact, he leaned on a tried-and-true sports clich\xc3\xa9 \xe2\x80\x94 but one that might show he has enough locked-in maturity to do real damage right now. He said he couldn\xe2\x80\x99t afford to consider anything more than the next match.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLook at today, I mean, he is five in the world,\xe2\x80\x9d Tiafoe said, referring to Anderson, who is actually ranked No. 6. \xe2\x80\x9cI was able to beat him. It\xe2\x80\x99s so tight now. Anybody plays a good match, you can beat anybody on a given day.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Fritz, 21, a Californian ranked 50th, can only hope those last words ring true. Shortly after Tiafoe\xe2\x80\x99s win, Fritz upset 30th-seeded Ga\xc3\xabl Monfils of France, 6-3, 6-7 (8), 7-6 (6), 7-6 (5). The match featured some of the most exquisite shotmaking of the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s opening days.'
b'Like Tiafoe, Fritz has never advanced past the third round of a major. But Fritz\xe2\x80\x99s next opponent is Federer, the two-time defending champion and No. 3 seed. The two have played only once: Federer won a tight three-setter on grass in 2016, as Fritz was just starting out on the tour.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI learned my lesson last time we played,\xe2\x80\x9d Fritz said. \xe2\x80\x9cI won the second set, and it was one of the most amazing feelings I have ever had playing tennis, winning a set off Roger Federer! And then we were deep in the third and I had a chance to break his serve, and I started thinking: Oh my God, I am about to beat Federer. I might beat Federer.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAnd then that thinking definitely lost me the match pretty quick. I didn\xe2\x80\x99t win another game after that. I have definitely learned I just have to treat it like any other match.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Playing Federer in Melbourne will not be any other match, of course. Same for Tiafoe, when he battles Seppi. But both matches present a real opportunity.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBetween Frances and Taylor today, we saw something different, something better, an intensity and composure I have never seen before,\xe2\x80\x9d said Martin Blackman, the U.S.T.A.\xe2\x80\x99s general manager for player development. \xe2\x80\x9cAll of our players can learn from this.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 Simona Halep of Romania is ranked No. 1 in the world in women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis. Last season, she won her first Grand Slam title, on the red clay of Roland Garros.'
b'On Monday night at Melbourne Park, she faced an opponent who, if judged by the numerical listing spit out by the pro tour\xe2\x80\x99s computer, should have been handled by Halep with relative ease. Except that player, currently ranked 16th in the world, is no slouch. That player, in fact, is Serena Williams, pure greatness in fishnet tights.'
b'Halep versus Williams in the round of 16 was a rare moment in tennis. It was a match in which the top-ranked player was also the decided underdog. Not only was Halep facing a formidable opponent with 23 major titles, seven of them in Melbourne alone, but she was also confronting someone who had dominated their career head-to-head matchups, winning eight times and losing just once.'
b'So it was hardly a shock that Williams ended up improving that record on Monday, rolling past the 27-year-old Halep by a 6-1, 4-6, 6-4 score.'
b'In the quarterfinals, Williams will now face seventh-seeded Karolina Pliskova of the Czech Republic, who easily defeated Garbi\xc3\xb1e Muguruza of Spain, 6-3, 6-1, to advance. Williams has beaten Pliskova twice in three matches, but the one loss came in the United States Open semifinals in 2016. Pliskova, meanwhile, has won all nine matches she has played this season. Williams will be the lower-ranked player when they meet but is again the actual favorite.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI have to return better, but I will be ready,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams vowed as she looked ahead to Pliskova. \xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s ready, I\xe2\x80\x99m ready, let\xe2\x80\x99s do it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It was vintage Serena confidence. And it also stood in contrast to her demeanor at the very beginning of her match against Halep. In those opening moments, Williams actually seemed shaky. She lost her first service game, the product of uncharacteristically poor shot-making and a clunky double fault.'
b'But in a flash, Williams got going. Playing with great precision, she continuously sent balls deep and into corners, often for winners.'
b'Game after game flew by, six straight in all decided in Williams\xe2\x80\x99s favor. At the age of 37, she simply did not allow her younger opponent to find her rhythm. Total time for the opening set: 20 minutes.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI felt like I\xe2\x80\x99d been hit by a train,\xe2\x80\x9d Halep would say later.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI played really good,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams said when asked about that first set. She spoke in a plain, matter-of-fact tone.'
b'A question came: \xe2\x80\x9cWere those six straight games the best you had played since coming back last year after the baby was born?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t know,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, \xe2\x80\x9cbut probably.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Still, Halep is among the most tenacious fighters in tennis, and as the match progressed, she began extending the rallies, which is more to her liking and style. She began serving better, fending off Williams\xe2\x80\x99s attacks.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI felt that my level is growing,\xe2\x80\x9d Halep said afterward. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd I had more confidence.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'And after capturing the second set, there was a brief period in the third when Halep appeared to have Williams on the ropes. Williams looked fatigued, her movements slower and less sure. But midway through that final set, Williams fended off three crucial break points. In the last, she pinned Halep into a corner and blasted a backhand winner down the line.'
b'As happens so often in tennis, Halep had trouble bouncing back from missing such an important opening. And as happens so often when Williams seems to be in trouble, she broke serve in the next game, seizing control with a string of strong baseline replies.'
b'When the last game of the match arrived, Halep offered meager resistance. Williams had prevailed again. Total time: 1 hour 47 minutes.'
b'Afterward, Halep was asked about the dynamics of taking on Williams, and whose confidence should have been higher when the match began.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou are ranked No. 1, and she is Serena Williams,\xe2\x80\x9d the questioner began before Halep politely cut him off.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cExactly,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'That one word response said it all, for Halep and for all of the women not named Serena who end up at the top of the computer rankings so long as she is playing.'
b'Williams now seems to be closing in on her old form after taking time off following the 2017 birth of her daughter. Even with that layoff, Williams still made the finals at Wimbledon and the U.S. Open last year. At the U.S. Open, she lost the final to Naomi Osaka in a swirl of controversy and accusations of sexism.'
b'Williams is on a collision course with Osaka again. Seeded fourth in Melbourne, Osaka advanced to the quarterfinals with a 4-6, 6-3, 6-4 victory over Anastasija Sevastova on Monday. Osaka next plays sixth-seeded Elina Svitolina and could face Williams in the semifinals.'
b'Williams\xe2\x80\x99s goal is clear and right there for the taking. If she wins her next three matches, she wins her 24th Grand Slam title, at last equaling the Australian great Margaret Court\xe2\x80\x99s total of major singles championships.'
b'Will she?'
b'Her coach, Patrick Mouratoglou, offered the strongest assessment.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI believe she will,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cShe is ready physically, I think emotionally, too.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By Ben Rothenberg'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 For Simona Halep, it was better to think that the United States Open wasn\xe2\x80\x99t held last year.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNever happened,\xe2\x80\x9d Halep said, grinning. \xe2\x80\x9cThat tournament didn\xe2\x80\x99t exist.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Top-seeded Halep was ousted from that tournament within its opening hours, blasted off the court by Kaia Kanepi in a 6-2, 6-4 demolition that sent shock waves through the newly built Louis Armstrong Stadium.'
b'Five months and 10,000 miles removed from that scene on Tuesday evening at the Australian Open, Halep was able to build back her sturdy defenses, digging into a gritty first-round rematch and defeating Kanepi, 6-7 (2), 6-2, 6-4, in 2 hours 11 minutes.'
b'Halep, who has had a tendency to give into negativity when being outplayed, did not relent this time. She expressed frustration, exasperation and disbelief after Kanepi struck many of her 40 winners, but remained dialed in throughout.'
b'Halep said all she could control was her effort.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think it\xe2\x80\x99s the best match I played in the last period, not giving up for one ball,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think I improved in that direction.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Halep\xe2\x80\x99s consistent, rugged defense eventually outlasted Kanepi\xe2\x80\x99s attacking; Halep hit only eight unforced errors in the final two sets, compared with 36 by Kanepi.'
b'Though a first-round win against a player ranked 71st would not normally be a milestone for a top seed, it was a steep test for Halep. Not only had she been clobbered by Kanepi in their previous meeting, Halep had not won a match since, losing three times and pulling out of the year-end championships with a back injury.'
b'Halep, who has maintained her No. 1 ranking despite not winning a match since August in Cincinnati, projected no precariousness. \xe2\x80\x9cIf I\xe2\x80\x99m thinking of all these things,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9cI cannot play tennis anymore.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A No. 1 ranked player whose ranking merits a Wheaties box but whose dominance belongs on the side of a milk carton is hardly a rare phenomenon in women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis. Dinara Safina, Ana Ivanovic and Angelique Kerber are among those went through crises of confidence when they reached the top of the ladder. Halep preached contentment, particularly after winning a long-awaited first Grand Slam title at last year\xe2\x80\x99s French Open.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not putting pressure on myself anymore with the results, but I\xe2\x80\x99m still motivated,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat comes now, it\xe2\x80\x99s a bonus.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Halep split with her longtime coach Darren Cahill at the end of last season, but she projected much of the clarity he instilled in her game \xe2\x80\x94 perhaps because the two are still in close contact. Cahill, also an analyst for ESPN, the American rights holder for the tournament, was on her court during pretournament practices.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s great to have him around,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cAlso it\xe2\x80\x99s tough that he\xe2\x80\x99s not in my team anymore. I don\xe2\x80\x99t know what I\xe2\x80\x99m going to do. For sure, I need a coach, because at this level you cannot do it alone. I\xe2\x80\x99m just chilling for the moment, and we will see after this tournament.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Because of Halep\xe2\x80\x99s slide, and the even distribution of titles around the top tier of the tour, nine women can leave Melbourne with the No. 1 ranking at the tournament\xe2\x80\x99s end. Halep, who finished the last two seasons at the top, said retaining the spot was not in the front of her mind.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe ranking doesn\xe2\x80\x99t matter anymore,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cI play tennis because I like it. Now my challenge is to win every match I play. b'Several current and former coaches, some with national titles and many with ties to U.S.C., were named in a federal indictment Tuesday.'
b'By Andrew Das, Marc Tracy and Naila-Jean Meyers'
b'The coaches led soccer teams and sailing teams, guided water polo champions and budding volleyball stars. At least two had won N.C.A.A. championships. A third gave Michelle Obama and her daughters tennis lessons from his post at Georgetown. '
b'The coaches charged Tuesday in a massive federal college admissions fraud scandal were some of the most prominent in their fields. But it was their apparent willingness to exploit their access to the admissions process at several exclusive universities that has them facing federal charges. '
b'Who are they? Several had deep associations with the University of Southern California, where Donna Heinel, a senior athletic department administrator, is accused of playing a central role in the scandal. For nearly a decade, Heinel had overseen the admissions of athletes into U.S.C., working closely with several of the current and former Trojans coaches who have been indicted. She was fired Tuesday.'
b'Here is a brief look at the current and former coaches identified by a federal complaint.'
b'U.S.C. water polo coach'
b'Vavic won 16 national titles at U.S.C., more than any coach in university history (10 in men\xe2\x80\x99s water polo, the most recent coming in December, and six in women\xe2\x80\x99s water polo). He was fired Tuesday after he was arrested in connection with the admissions scheme. He had coached the women\xe2\x80\x99s team, currently ranked No. 1 and the defending national champion, since 1995 and had been the sole head coach of the men\xe2\x80\x99s team since 1999. A 15-time national coach of the year, Vavic was named the Pac-12 Conference\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9ccoach of the century\xe2\x80\x9d for water polo in 2015. '
b'According to the indictment, the co-conspirators in the admissions fraud paid $250,000 to an account that financed the U.S.C. water polo program, and in return Vavic recommended two students as recruits to the water polo team. The ringleader of the scheme, William Singer, known as Rick, is said to have paid the private school tuition for Vavic\xe2\x80\x99s children through one of his company\xe2\x80\x99s charitable accounts \xe2\x80\x9cunder the guise of a fabricated scholarship.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Former Georgetown tennis coach'
b'According to the indictment, Ernst, known as Gordie, earned more than $2.7 million between 2012 and 2018 in payments that were falsely labeled \xe2\x80\x9cconsulting\xe2\x80\x9d fees. He \xe2\x80\x9cdesignated at least 12 applicants as recruits\xe2\x80\x9d for Georgetown\xe2\x80\x99s tennis teams, court papers said, \xe2\x80\x9cincluding some who did not play competitively.\xe2\x80\x9d One such player, listed in the complaint, was encouraged to make playing tennis part of her application essay and claimed to be a top-50-ranking player in the U.S.T.A. for junior girls, which was not true. She was accepted at Georgetown in 2016. '
b'A spokeswoman for Georgetown said Tuesday that the university had fired Ernst in December 2017 after an internal investigation found he had violated university rules concerning admissions. Ernst, a native of Rhode Island who is in the New England Sports Hall of Fame, was named the women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis coach at the University of Rhode Island last August. The university placed him on administrative leave on Tuesday. '
b'Wake Forest volleyball coach'
b'Ferguson has been the women\xe2\x80\x99s volleyball coach at Wake Forest since 2016. Before that, he coached the men\xe2\x80\x99s team at U.S.C., winning 150 matches and leading the Trojans to three N.C.A.A. Final Fours. He was the American Volleyball Coaches Association coach of the year in 2009 and 2012. His success has not continued at Wake Forest, where he was 22-41 in his first two seasons. After Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s charges were unsealed, Wake Forest announced that he has been placed on administrative leave. Ferguson is accused of accepting $100,000 from Singer in 2017 to help Singer\xe2\x80\x99s client\xe2\x80\x99s daughter, who had been wait-listed by the school, gain admittance to Wake Forest as a volleyball recruit.'
b' U.C.L.A. men\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach'
b'Salcedo has been U.C.L.A.\xe2\x80\x99s men\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach since 2004. The Bruins are one of the nation\xe2\x80\x99s top programs annually, and Salcedo has produced dozens of players who have gone on to play professional soccer. A former All-American at U.C.L.A. who had a brief career in Major League Soccer and other leagues, he has been a member of the Bruins\xe2\x80\x99 soccer program as either a player, assistant coach or head coach for two decades. He is accused of helping two students gain admission to U.C.L.A. as student-athletes in exchange for $200,000. The Los Angeles Times and others reported that he had been placed on leave Tuesday.'
b'Former U.S.C. women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coaches'
b'Khosroshahin won a national championship in his first season with the Trojans in 2007, when he was named national coach of the year, but he was fired in 2013 after missing the N.C.A.A. tournament three years in a row. U.S.C. went 8-10-2 in his final season; he was 82-53-15 over all. '
b'Janke joined Khosroshahin\xe2\x80\x99s U.S.C. coaching staff as an assistant after playing for him in his previous job at Cal State-Fullerton. A biography of her at the Geffen Academy, a private school in Los Angeles for students in grades 6 through 12, lists her as the physical education department chair. A previous announcement hailed her hiring as the head of the school\xe2\x80\x99s girls soccer program. '
b'In the indictment, Singer is said to have contributed $350,000 a private soccer club run by Khosroshahin and Janke in exchange for their suggesting four children of Singer\xe2\x80\x99s clients as recruits. '
b'Khosroshahin and Janke were also asked to create misleading recruiting profiles and to serve as references for students who were not competitive soccer players in order to help them gain admission to other colleges. '
b'Former Yale women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach'
b'A third cooperating witness in court papers was an unnamed person whose description closely matches Meredith, who served as Yale\xe2\x80\x99s women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer coach from 1995 through late last year. Meredith was also a participant in the scheme, according to court filings. Meredith resigned as Yale\xe2\x80\x99s coach in November after a disappointing season, but also after, the authorities said Tuesday, he had accepted hundreds of thousands of dollars of payments to facilitate the admission of a non-soccer-playing soccer recruit to Yale. When he stepped down after last season, Meredith told the university that \xe2\x80\x9cit is time to explore new possibilities and begin a different chapter in my life.\xe2\x80\x9d A month later, he was elected to the Connecticut Soccer Hall of Fame. '
b'Stanford sailing coach'
b'Vandemoer is accused of taking financial contributions to his championship-winning sailing program from an intermediary in exchange for agreeing to recommend two prospective students for admission. \xe2\x80\x9cNeither student came to Stanford,\xe2\x80\x9d Stanford said in a statement Tuesday. \xe2\x80\x9cHowever, the alleged behavior runs completely counter to Stanford\xe2\x80\x99s values.\xe2\x80\x9d Stanford said Vandemoer had been fired.'
b'Texas men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis coach'
b'The Longhorns have one of the top programs in the country, having reached the N.C.A.A. tournament every season since Center took over in 2000. He was placed on administrative leave Tuesday after being accused of accepting $100,000 from Singer in 2015 in exchange for recruiting a student who was not a competitive tennis player. According to court papers, the student\xe2\x80\x99s application to Texas said he played one year of tennis as a freshman, but his other activities included being manager of his high school basketball and football teams. The student withdrew from the tennis team shortly after beginning classes at Texas. '

b'By Christopher Clarey'
b'MIAMI GARDENS, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 No matter how smooth and imperious Roger Federer looked in the Miami Open final, whipping winners seemingly on demand and breaking big John Isner\xe2\x80\x99s serve on four occasions, Federer knows all too well how fragile this all is as the shadows lengthen.'
b'There can be no doubt that Federer is back near top gear at 37. He is moving like a man 10 years younger and has a sparkling 18-2 record this season. After his 6-1, 6-4 victory on Sunday, he is the first man or woman to win more than one singles title in 2019.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cKind of fitting,\xe2\x80\x9d Isner said of Federer ending that unprecedented streak of 33 different singles champions. \xe2\x80\x9cOne of our game\xe2\x80\x99s greats.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Perhaps the greatest, though it remains so tough to compare apples to apples and Federers to Lavers. Comparing eras is seemingly as foolish an errand as writing definitive lists until Rafael Nadal and Novak Djokovic are all done winning, too.'
b'But Federer\xe2\x80\x99s enduring excellence is an evermore elegant and persuasive argument, even if the reminders of how challenging it is for tennis champions to endure and prosper were right there in front of him again on Sunday.'
b'There was his opponent, the defending champion Isner, 33, suddenly hobbling between points in the second set with a left foot injury that Isner fears could be a stress fracture.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI have never had anything like this before,\xe2\x80\x9d said Isner, who began feeling the pain late in the first set.'
b'And when it very soon came time for Federer to accept his fourth Miami Open singles trophy, one of the officials whose hands he shook was the tournament director James Blake, one of his former tour rivals who is now 39 and long retired.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cRoger, I don\xe2\x80\x99t know what else to say,\xe2\x80\x9d Blake said after Federer\xe2\x80\x99s 101st tour singles title. \xe2\x80\x9cIt just makes me feel like such an underachiever.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Nearly all the stars of Federer\xe2\x80\x99s tennis generation have moved on to other roles: Tommy Haas, one of Federer\xe2\x80\x99s closer friends, is now the tournament director at Indian Wells.'
b'Federer made his debut in Miami in 1999 and is the only man who participated that year who is still playing singles.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s been a superlong journey for me here,\xe2\x80\x9d Federer said. \xe2\x80\x9cI got a wild card here in \xe2\x80\x9999 and made my first final here in 2002 against Andre Agassi.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He went on to win the title in 2005, 2006 and again in 2017, the year when he roared back to the top after recovering from knee surgery.'
b'That could have been his last hurrah, but the hurrahs keep coming with titles at Dubai and Miami in 2019 and a very close call at Indian Wells, where he was beaten in three tight sets by Dominic Thiem in the final.'
b'But Federer bounced back convincingly in a familiar tournament in an unfamiliar place: Hard Rock Stadium, the Open\xe2\x80\x99s new, much more capacious home after 31 years in the more intimate, boutique setting of Key Biscayne.'
b'In 2018, when the event was still on an island instead of in an N.F.L. stadium, Federer lost in his opening round to Thanasi Kokkinakis. Though Federer had another scare in the same round this year against the qualifier Radu Albot, he rallied to win in three sets and then gathered nothing but momentum, winning five straight matches in straight sets.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s easy just to say, \xe2\x80\x98Well last year didn\xe2\x80\x99t work out, so I won\xe2\x80\x99t come back this year, and as I\xe2\x80\x99m playing the clay, maybe add rather another clay-court event,\xe2\x80\x99 \xe2\x80\x9d Federer said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I felt like let\xe2\x80\x99s extend the hardcourt season. Let\xe2\x80\x99s see the new venue. To be honest, I think that was something also I was excited to see. I did feel like the game was there last year, and I thought also the game was definitely here this year even after the Australian Open. So I\xe2\x80\x99m happy with the team, we took the right decision.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The team has also agreed that Federer will play on clay for the first time since brief, unfulfilling visits to Monte Carlo and Rome in 2016. His next tournament: Madrid in early May, which will give him time to reboot and reacquaint himself with the game\xe2\x80\x99s grittiest surface.'
b'How confident is he?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNot very confident,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t even remember how to slide anymore. You know, I\xe2\x80\x99m taking baby steps at this point.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It is smart, as ever, to try to underpromise and overdeliver, particularly when you are entering the kingdom of Nadal, the 11-time French Open champion and most successful men\xe2\x80\x99s clay-court player in history.'
b'But Federer, despite his fourth-round loss to Stefanos Tsitsipas at the Australian Open, has certainly had another hardcourt run to savor in 2019.'
b'He looked thoroughly in his element on Sunday, just as Isner feared and expected he would.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI knew he was going to play well today; I knew he was seeing the ball very big,\xe2\x80\x9d Isner said. \xe2\x80\x9cCertainly that was the case. I wasn\xe2\x80\x99t up to the task in the first set, that\xe2\x80\x99s for sure.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Before the final, Federer compared the experience of facing Isner\xe2\x80\x99s serve to that of a soccer goalkeeper facing a penalty kick.'
b'If you embrace that metaphor, he made a very quick save, breaking Isner in the opening game, blunting the power with sliced returns on the stretch and then hooking passing shots that even the 6-foot-10 Isner struggled to reach.'
b'Federer rolled through his own service games in a hurry. He won all 20 of his first-serve points in the match and dropped only three points on his second serve.'
b'Isner, who had not faced Federer in an official match since 2015, would have needed to be very near the top of his game to stop this train or even get into one of his beloved tiebreakers.'
b'But he was far from his peak and eventually in great discomfort, limping down the stretch after an injury timeout late in the second set and later wincing and limping off the dais in the interview room.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou hope it\xe2\x80\x99s nothing serious, and I hope he\xe2\x80\x99s fine,\xe2\x80\x9d said Federer, who said experience helped him remain focused as Isner struggled. \xe2\x80\x9cBut it\xe2\x80\x99s tricky, no doubt.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Tricky indeed to remain hale and hearty year after year in a Darwinian individual sport; even trickier to keep holding up trophies year after year with younger men swinging full force across the net.'

b'By Kurt Streeter'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 It started as a curiosity, believed to be the tallest match in tennis\xe2\x80\x99s Grand Slam history.'
b'And yet by the end of a nearly three-hour slugfest on the Australian Open\xe2\x80\x99s opening day on Monday, fans left less impressed by all of the long-limbed height than by the guts of the surprising victor: the virtually unknown Reilly Opelka \xe2\x80\x94 21, American, 7 feet tall in socks \xe2\x80\x94 who doled out an eye-popping upset by defeating his ninth-seeded compatriot John Isner, 33, who stands a looming 6 feet 10 inches.'
b'Tennis players in the modern era trend taller than the players of yesteryear, even compared to those of 15 and 20 years ago. But not this much taller. In a sport where the best male players still typically hover around 6 feet (top-ranked Novak Djokovic is listed at 6-2), not only do Isner and Opelka seem like human skyscrapers, they come to the court for each match with the simplest game plan possible: Crush serves, slam forehands and hide their considerable deficiencies in movement by keeping every point whiplash short.'
b'Staring across the net at Isner, Opelka said after the match, was like looking in the mirror, and not just because of his opponent\xe2\x80\x99s height.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s just a lot of things that are out of your control,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, speaking of the distress that comes from playing one of the few who can hit just as hard as he can, and from such high, imposing angles. \xe2\x80\x9cI was expecting that today I probably wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t touch too many balls. I was hoping the same for him.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Official match statistics back Opelka up. He did not touch many balls. The average rally lasted two shots. On only four points were at least nine balls struck. Isner slammed 47 aces. Opelka slammed 40, the last a 141-mile-per-hour fastball that Isner barely moved for.'
b'The final score underscored how little separated the pair. Opelka, ranked No. 97, won, 7-6 (4), 7-6 (6), 6-7 (4), 7-6 (5).'
b'When it was over, Isner could barely hide the disappointment. He rarely made eye contact during the postmatch news conference. At times, his hands shook with tension.'
b'He has long been ranked in the top 20 on the ATP Tour. Last season was his best. He won his first World Tour Masters 1000 at the Miami Open, made the semifinals at Wimbledon and, as one of the top players of the year, appeared in the elite tour finals in London.'
b'But last season also started poorly, punctuated with a loss that was in some ways similar to the one against Opelka: a first-round defeat at the Australian Open at the hands of a little known, albeit much smaller opponent, Matthew Ebden, an Australian who stands a tour-typical 6-2.'
b'Isner vowed to lean on the fact that he had begun last season in such bad shape \xe2\x80\x94 not only being upset in Melbourne but posting an early record of two wins and six losses \xe2\x80\x94 before breaking through and winning Miami.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was off and running from there,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cJust got to get one under my belt and see what happens.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Though hardly one for long answers, Opelka appeared relaxed and casual as he spoke in the wake of the most significant victory of his young career. He spoke of the main difference between him and Isner. In the early stages of his career, Opelka, who is listed as 6-11 but has acknowledged that he is even taller, does not have a deeply successful professional past to hark back to.'
b'Hence, even after Monday, his primary motive remains clear: Keep playing well enough that he never again has to compete in tennis\xe2\x80\x99s often brutal minor leagues, where he won two titles at the end of last season to break into the top 100.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cis the immediate goal.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'More than making a long run in Melbourne?'
b'Yes, he replied, saying he could only allow himself to think of his next match, against Thomas Fabbiano, an Italian who is ranked No. 102 and, compared to Isner, is a relative munchkin.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOne guy is 5-10,\xe2\x80\x9d Opelka said, referring to Fabbiano. \xe2\x80\x9cThe other guy,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, referring to Isner not by name but with a pregnant pause, \xe2\x80\x9cis not.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'On Tennis'
b'By Karen Crouse'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 Time did not freeze, like a televised sporting event placed on pause, during the 13 months Serena Williams spent away from tennis. The absence of Williams, who has averaged one title in every three majors played, allowed younger players to wade deeper into the draws and grow their games and their confidence.'
b'Karolina Pliskova, 26, was already on the rise when a pregnant Williams took her leave from tennis after winning the 2017 Australian Open. The previous year, Pliskova had graced the final of the United States Open, beating Williams on the way. But it was the only Grand Slam event where she advanced past the third round in 2016.'
b'With Williams out of the picture from February 2017 to March 2018, the ascent of Pliskova continued apace. Advancing to the quarterfinals or better in 15 of 20 tournaments in 2017, Pliskova assumed the women\xe2\x80\x99s world No. 1 ranking that July, two months after Williams\xe2\x80\x99s last stay there.'
b'In the eight majors contested since Williams\xe2\x80\x99s last Grand Slam title, at the 2017 Australian Open, Pliskova has made it to the quarterfinals or better in five. With her 6-4, 4-6, 7-5 defeat of Williams on Wednesday in the quarterfinals of the Australian Open on Wednesday, Pliskova avenged a two-set quarterfinal loss to Williams at last year\xe2\x80\x99s U.S. Open.'
b'The way Pliskova pulled out the victory was telling; she played the big points as fearlessly as Williams, 37, once did. Down by 1-5 in the third set, Pliskova won six consecutive games and staved off four match points by swinging for the lines and serving to dime-sized spots. She did to Williams what Williams did to Kim Clijsters in the 2003 semifinals here. In that match, Williams staved off two match points while climbing back from a 1-5 deficit, then beat her sister, Venus, in the final to hold all four major titles concurrently.'
b'That Williams had an aura that sometimes all but overshadowed her. The Williams standing across the net from Pliskova hasn\xe2\x80\x99t appreciably changed. In spotting the rest of the women\xe2\x80\x99s game a full year, she simply gave everybody else a chance to catch up to her level of intensity and fight.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis time I just feel somehow different and more confident,\xe2\x80\x9d Pliskova said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not doubting myself.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Williams held her first match point while serving at 5-1 in the third. She was called a foot fault on her first serve. Then at the end of the point she turned her left ankle after Pliskova wrong-footed her. Williams never called for a trainer to treat her ankle.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAt that point I didn\xe2\x80\x99t feel like I needed it or I didn\xe2\x80\x99t feel like it would be a big deal,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams explained.'
b'There was a good reason she felt that way. Many times over the years, less than Williams\xe2\x80\x99s best was good enough.'
b'But that no longer is the case.'
b'Williams\xe2\x80\x99s serve has always been the weapon she can lean on when all else fails. On Wednesday, Williams didn\xe2\x80\x99t win another point on her serve after turning her ankle.'
b'Williams said of Pliskova: \xe2\x80\x9cI think she just kind of started playing really, really good. I don\xe2\x80\x99t think it had anything to do with my ankle per se.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Williams was right. Did her level of play drop in the last six games? Yes. But to focus on that is to miss the bigger picture. Williams lost because during the year that she spent growing a child instead of a game, Pliskova and the other top players got better.'
b'If Williams is to resume her winning ways, she will have to play better than she did in 2017, when she vanquished Venus here for her 23rd major title.'
b'It is not impossible. Williams\xe2\x80\x99s mission, if she chooses to accept it, is to forget the past and resolutely move forward, one honest day\xe2\x80\x99s work at a time. The good news for tennis is that she seems committed to the chase of Margaret Court and her record 24 major singles titles.'
b'This was Williams\xe2\x80\x99s eighth official tournament since her return from a difficult pregnancy. The golfer Tiger Woods, with whom Williams is friendly, won the Tour Championship in his 18th official start after his return from back surgery. As long as Williams is patient, she can once again prosper.'
b'Speaking earlier in the week, Williams\xe2\x80\x99s coach, Patrick Mouratoglou, said it was unrealistic to expect Williams to hit the tour winning after the birth of her daughter, Alexis Olympia Ohanian Jr. She won no titles last year, but reached the final at Wimbledon and the United States Open, losing to opponents whose masterly performances kept her off balance.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou cannot buy time,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThings take time. To get back to shape, back in shape after a baby, a few months are not enough. I mean, still she could have won because she\xe2\x80\x99s doing things other people don\xe2\x80\x99t, but it was \xe2\x80\x94 I mean, the story said it was too early. That\xe2\x80\x99s it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Williams didn\xe2\x80\x99t win six majors before her 22nd birthday because she was a patient person. But motherhood is a daily practice in living in the moment, and Williams is nothing if not a diligent student. Earlier in the tournament, she said her year off \xe2\x80\x9cgave me a new fire, a new purpose, a new meaning.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It did the same for her opponents, which is why the women\xe2\x80\x99s game is infinitely more interesting now that Williams is back.'

b'On Tennis'
b'By Karen Crouse'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 The first tennis player to capture Novak Djokovic\xe2\x80\x99s imagination was a big-serving American with a beautiful one-handed backhand. A grade-school-aged Djokovic, living in the Serbian mountain resort town of Kopaonik, watched on television as Pete Sampras won one of his seven Wimbledon titles, and he fell madly in love with tennis.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI did not have a tennis tradition in my family,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said, adding, \xe2\x80\x9cTo me it was definitely a sign of destiny to start playing tennis, to aspire to be as good as Pete.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Djokovic tried to emulate Sampras\xe2\x80\x99s game, right down to the one-handed backhand, before his first coach, Jelena Gencic, encouraged him to switch to both hands because that was his natural stroke. But on other things, Djokovic refused to budge.'
b'Most significantly, Djokovic never abandoned the belief that he would grow up to be the best men\xe2\x80\x99s player in the world, like Sampras, who held the year-end No. 1 ranking for a men\xe2\x80\x99s record six years beginning in 1993, when a 6-year-old Djokovic began playing tennis in earnest.'
b'On Sunday at the Australian Open, Djokovic finally and decisively slipped the surly bonds of Sampras. With his 6-3, 6-2, 6-3 defeat of Rafael Nadal, Djokovic secured his 15th Grand Slam singles title, breaking his tie with Sampras. Djokovic took sole possession of third on the list, behind his contemporaries Roger Federer (20) and Nadal (17).'
b'When Sampras retired in 2002, he held the record for men\xe2\x80\x99s Grand Slam titles. Unlike Djokovic, who has peers to push him, Sampras spent his career in a mostly lonely pursuit of a long-retired player, Roy Emerson, who collected 12 major championships, including a men\xe2\x80\x99s record six Australian Open titles.'
b'Emerson, 82, attended Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s final at Rod Laver Arena, and, like the 47-year-old Sampras, he had a target on his back. Djokovic\xe2\x80\x99s title was his seventh at Melbourne Park. When he met up with Emerson after the trophy presentation, Djokovic said, smiling, that \xe2\x80\x9cMr. Emerson\xe2\x80\x9d was mad at him for breaking his record.'
b'The careers of Djokovic and Sampras never intersected \xe2\x80\x94 Djokovic turned pro the year after Sampras retired \xe2\x80\x94 but their paths crossed in Los Angeles in 2013 when they played together (and lost) in an exhibition doubles match at U.C.L.A. against Bob and Mike Bryan.'
b'At the time, Djokovic described it as \xe2\x80\x9ca blast\xe2\x80\x9d to share the court with Sampras and said he had always hoped to play a match with or against him. Two months before the exhibition, Djokovic had collected his sixth Grand Slam title with his fourth Australian Open crown. But it wasn\xe2\x80\x99t considered a given that he would one day share a piece of Grand Slam history with Sampras, much less move past him.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo surpass him with Grand Slam titles, I\xe2\x80\x99m speechless,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said Sunday. \xe2\x80\x9cI haven\xe2\x80\x99t had too much time to contemplate on everything that has happened, but I\xe2\x80\x99m planning to do that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In 2014, Sampras returned to the Australian Open as a spectator, and while there, he sat for a news conference in which he fielded a question about the aging process for champion athletes.'
b'Sampras was 31, the same age that Djokovic is now, when he retired. The grind of the tour, especially the extensive travel, eroded his motivation, Sampras said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAs you get older, it just gets tougher,\xe2\x80\x9d Sampras said then. \xe2\x80\x9cIt gets tougher to play. It gets tougher to travel. Sometimes it gets a little stale.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He added: \xe2\x80\x9cI just know from my perspective, I was fatigued the last couple years. I was enjoying my tennis, but it was a tough job.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Djokovic understands what Sampras meant. He traveled here without his wife and two small children. During the trophy presentation, Djokovic thanked his loved ones in absentia for their forbearance. He expressed gratitude for all the sacrifices they made so that he could maintain what he described as a selfish existence. He said that it was hard to be apart from his family for weeks on end.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHunger is always there,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut nowadays it\xe2\x80\x99s just more relevant for me to organize myself in life better, to manage to be very concise and concrete with what I do and what I plan to do, because I am a father and a husband. Right now it\xe2\x80\x99s not only about tennis.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After his fourth-round exit here last year, Djokovic had surgery on his elbow, and that was tough, too, he said. He acknowledged having doubts about whether he could regain his championship form.'
b'That sounds ludicrous now, with Djokovic in current possession of three of the four major trophies and needing only a French Open victory to complete a Novak Slam.'
b'After passing Sampras, Djokovic has no plans to slow down. Many players, Djokovic was told, believe that he can surpass Federer on the major victory list.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHow do you live with that?\xe2\x80\x9d a reporter asked.'
b'Djokovic laughed. \xe2\x80\x9cHow do I live with that?\xe2\x80\x9d he replied. \xe2\x80\x9cJust fine.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'\xe2\x80\x9cShe basically knows where he\xe2\x80\x99s going to hit in advance, because she hits with him every day, so there is no surprise,\xe2\x80\x9d Mouratoglou said. \xe2\x80\x9cShe doesn\xe2\x80\x99t feel that she\xe2\x80\x99s challenged because she knows him too well. b'\xe2\x80\x9cSo it\xe2\x80\x99s completely different relationship with a professional player, because she has to give him good rhythm, to give a good ball to him, too, so she can\xe2\x80\x99t lose focus.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Other top men and women have shared practice courts in the first month of the tennis season. Andy Murray and Naomi Osaka, for example, hit together for 30 minutes at a tournament in Brisbane, Australia.'
b'Mouratoglou said that he emphasized to the men that they should not treat Williams differently from any other practice partner.'
b'He said he told Eubanks, \xe2\x80\x9cPlay for yourself \xe2\x80\x94 it\xe2\x80\x99s your practice.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'\xe2\x80\x9cSerena hits, in my opinion, one of the cleanest balls in the history of tennis,\xe2\x80\x9d Eubanks said. \xe2\x80\x9cI was working on absorbing pace, because she puts enough pace on it that you\xe2\x80\x99re really working the legs. b'\xe2\x80\x9cI practiced again in the evening, and I told my coach I felt like I did a lift today, because my quads are so sore from just hitting with her for an hour,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'After Williams\xe2\x80\x99s victory over Bouchard, the on-court interviewer Jim Courier joked that she should charge the men she hits with for lessons. b'For the tens of thousands of Australians of Serbian descent, Djokovic is the secular saint of sport, worshiped by Serbs who still feel an acute sense of persecution nearly two decades after the worst of the Balkans\xe2\x80\x99 fractious ethnic violence. '
b'Even during the 50 weeks of the year when the Melbourne Park courts go quiet, Djokovic\xe2\x80\x99s presence looms. '
b'For Serbia, a nation of seven million people, it is \xe2\x80\x9ca big deal\xe2\x80\x9d to be able to claim the top-ranked player in men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis \xe2\x80\x94 and one of the best ever \xe2\x80\x94 said Zeljko Prodanovic, the newspaper\xe2\x80\x99s editor.'

b'The newspaper\xe2\x80\x99s owner, Zivana Jovanovic, has welcomed several Serbian luminaries to her office in her two decades at the helm, including the actor Dragan Nikolic and the retired N.B.A. player Vlade Divac. b'\xe2\x80\x9cI like that about him,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe hasn\xe2\x80\x99t let all his success go to his head.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Djokovic\xe2\x80\x99s celebrity status has made it hard for him to move freely in public in Melbourne, but in his younger days he had regular haunts: a church where he would ring in the Orthodox New Year, or the restaurants on Lygon Street, known for its outdoor cafes and European eateries. The night before, Pokrajac said, he had imagined getting to hit again with Djokovic, borrowing a technique that has served him well in his matches.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf I visualize something before,\xe2\x80\x9d Pokrajac said, \xe2\x80\x9cthen it will happen.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After Djokovic finished practicing, Pokrajac shouted, \xe2\x80\x9cRemember me, Novak? I\xe2\x80\x99m here from Perth.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Djokovic remembered. He came over, hoisted Pokrajac over the fence again, handed him a racket, and they began to hit. They played four \xe2\x80\x9cpoints.\xe2\x80\x9d The second rally was 34 shots; the fourth ended on the 16th, when Pokrajac hit a half-volley for a winner.'
b'His prize was a hug and a signed T-shirt from Djokovic, who also offered a tip on how to return a slice.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe told me to get lower,\xe2\x80\x9d Pokrajac said.'
b'Two days later, Pokrajac staked out his same spot. He unfurled a Serbian flag that he had signed and which he intended to present to Djokovic as a parting gift. After his session, Djokovic came over and accepted the flag. He read what Pokrajac had written: \xe2\x80\x9cTo Novak from Novak from Perth.\xe2\x80\x9d Under his signature Pokrajac had written, \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s going to be worth gold money\xe2\x80\x9d and added a smiley face.'
b'Djokovic hugged him. As Pokrajac turned to rejoin his mother, his smile was incandescent.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI feel like I know him,\xe2\x80\x9d Pokrajac said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think we\xe2\x80\x99re going to be friends now.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ben Rothenberg contributed reporting. '

b'MIAMI GARDENS, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 In what is usually one of his most successful stretches of the season, top-ranked Novak Djokovic fell short of expectations for the second time this month, losing, 1-6, 7-5, 6-3, to No. 22 Roberto Bautista Agut in the fourth round of the Miami Open on Tuesday afternoon.'
b'After gaining a foothold in the match early in the second set, Bautista Agut endured a 40-minute rain delay before drawing level. After breaking for a 3-1 advantage, Bautista Agut dropped his serve but then broke Djokovic again immediately, extending his lead to 5-2 before the two traded holds to finish the match.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe key of the match was at the beginning of the second set, no?\xe2\x80\x9d Bautista Agut said. \xe2\x80\x9cIf I wanted to win the match, I had to be very close at the score. Otherwise Novak, when he gets an advantage, he plays really aggressive.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Indeed, Djokovic had never previously lost a match at the Miami Open after winning the first set, a string of 41 matches.'
b'His advantage looked even more secure when he broke Bautista Agut in the first game of the second set, but Djokovic could not hold in the next game.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI lost the momentum,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cI lost the rhythm in the second set. I gave him a little room to step in, and he did. b'Djokovic, a six-time champion in Miami, came into the tournament with little momentum, having lost to Philipp Kohlschreiber in the third round at Indian Wells, a tournament where he is a five-time champion.'

b'\xe2\x80\x9cI just had way too many things off the court,\xe2\x80\x9d Djokovic said. \xe2\x80\x9cI guess that affected me a little bit on the court.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By Ben Rothenberg'
b'Naomi Osaka, the No. 1-ranked player in the world, announced on Monday that she was splitting with her coach, Sascha Bajin, abruptly ending one of the most successful recent partnerships in women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis at what seemed to be a high point.'
b'Hey everyone, I will no longer be working together with Sascha. I thank him for his work and wish him all the best in the future.'
b'The surprising announcement came just 16 days after Osaka won the Australian Open, her second major title under Bajin\xe2\x80\x99s watch. The win vaulted her to the No. 1 ranking, a first for an Asian player on the men\xe2\x80\x99s or women\xe2\x80\x99s singles tours.'
b'Bajin, who became a coach after serving as the longtime hitting partner of Serena Williams, was named the WTA\xe2\x80\x99s Coach of the Year in 2018. He responded on Twitter to Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s announcement.'
b'Osaka, 21, was ranked 68th when she hired Bajin in the lead-up to the 2018 season, giving him his first head coaching role. She quickly surged under his guidance, reaching the second week of a Grand Slam for the first time at the 2018 Australian Open, and then winning her first professional singles title at Indian Wells, Calif., in March.'
b'Osaka beat Williams, her idol, for the first time in her next match in the first round of the Miami Open, and then memorably beat her again six months later in the final of the U.S. Open, a victory which took her into the top-10 for the first time.'
b'The reasons for the split were unclear. Bajin did not respond to messages seeking comment, and Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s agent, Stuart Duguid, declined to comment.'
b'Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s split from Bajin is the latest on a coaches\xe2\x80\x99 carousel in which success has not guaranteed longevity in player-coach partnerships. Last year\xe2\x80\x99s French Open champion, Simona Halep, and the Wimbledon champion, Angelique Kerber, parted with their coaches at the end of last season, meaning that the reigning champions of the past four Grand Slam events are no longer with the coaches who helped them to those titles.'
b'Halep, ranked third, is now working with Thierry Van Cleemput, who split with his longtime charge David Goffin at the Australian Open.'
b'Osaka, who has not yet named a successor to Bajin, will play her first match as WTA No. 1 next week in Dubai. It will be her first time as the No. 1 seed at any WTA event.'
b'Asked after the Australian Open final what advice Bajin had given her before the match, Osaka smiled and said she hadn\xe2\x80\x99t talked to him.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYeah, no, like we haven\xe2\x80\x99t really been talking, to be honest, like before any of my matches here,\xe2\x80\x9d Osaka said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe would tell me, like, one thing, then I would be, like, \xe2\x80\x98O.K.\xe2\x80\x99 That was it.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'The U.S. women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer team has filed a gender discrimination lawsuit. The players are the latest athletes to demand equal treatment. '
b'By Maya Salam'
b'You\xe2\x80\x99re reading In Her Words, where women rule the headlines. Sign up here to get it delivered to your inbox. Let me know what you think at dearmaya@nytimes.com.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEveryone thinks women should be thrilled when we get crumbs, and I want women to have the cake, the icing and the cherry on top, too.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x94 Billie Jean King, a tennis legend who led the charge for pay equality in her sport'
b'Last week, all 28 players on the U.S. women\xe2\x80\x99s national soccer team \xe2\x80\x94 the greatest women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer team in the world \xe2\x80\x94 filed a gender discrimination lawsuit against the United States Soccer Federation, another move in its long-running battle for equality.'
b'The athletes \xe2\x80\x94 including the stars Alex Morgan, Megan Rapinoe and Carli Lloyd \xe2\x80\x94 are not just taking issue with their paychecks but also with where they play, how they travel to matches, and the medical treatment and coaching they receive, in what they called \xe2\x80\x9cinstitutionalized gender discrimination,\xe2\x80\x9d as my colleague Andy Das reported.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve always, dating back to forever, been a team that stood up for itself and fought hard for what it felt it deserved and tried to leave the game in a better place,\xe2\x80\x9d Rapinoe told The New York Times on Friday.'
b'The women\xe2\x80\x99s team holds a record three World Cup championships and four Olympic gold medals.'
b'[READ MORE: U.S. Women\xe2\x80\x99s Soccer Team Sues U.S. Soccer for Gender Discrimination]'
b'The issue of pay inequality in sports is of course not just soccer\xe2\x80\x99s problem. Women across all sports are paid less, and many have fought for equity in salary and in prize money. '
b'Here are other cases where pay inequality has been stark, compelling female athletes to speak out.'
b'The U.S. Open. After long-fought battles by champions like Billie Jean King, Chris Evert, Martina Navratilova, and Venus and Serena Williams, tennis has seen the most progress when it comes to pay equity.  The first real appeal was made in 1970 by King, after a tournament in Italy for which she was paid just $600 for taking the women\xe2\x80\x99s title. The men\xe2\x80\x99s winner was awarded $3,500. King would later make this statement: \xe2\x80\x9cEveryone thinks women should be thrilled when we get crumbs, and I want women to have the cake, the icing and the cherry on top, too.\xe2\x80\x9dIn 1973, King threatened to sit out the U.S. Open unless the prize money was made equal. It worked. That year, the men\xe2\x80\x99s and women\xe2\x80\x99s champions were paid equally, and the U.S. Open has paid its winners equally since. Other Grand Slams, though, were slow to follow suit.'
b'[READ MORE: Eight Times Women in Sports Fought for Equality]'
b"The Australian Open, and other Grand Slams. Prize money for the Australian Open had fluctuated for decades: In 1978, the men\xe2\x80\x99s winner was paid about 585 percent more than the women\xe2\x80\x99s, ESPN reported last year. And in the mid-1980s, the women\xe2\x80\x99s winner was paid slightly more. By the mid-1990s, men were again paid more, prompting officials in the Women's Tennis Association to push hard for equal pay. In 2001, the Australian Open agreed, and winners have been compensated equally since. The French Open came around in 2006, and then Wimbledon in 2007, a change led by Venus Williams. Williams made a failed plea to Wimbledon\xe2\x80\x99s governing body the night before she took the title in 2005. And in 2006, she wrote an op-ed in The Times of London titled \xe2\x80\x9cWimbledon Has Sent Me a Message: I\xe2\x80\x99m Only a Second Class Champion.\xe2\x80\x9d In 2007, she was awarded $1.4 million for her victory, the same as the men\xe2\x80\x99s champion, Roger Federer. More recently, Novak Djokovic, currently the No. 1 men\xe2\x80\x99s player in the world, suggested men deserve more money. \xe2\x80\x9cThe stats are showing that we have much more spectators on the men\xe2\x80\x99s tennis matches,\xe2\x80\x9d he said in 2016. \xe2\x80\x9cI think that\xe2\x80\x99s one of the reasons why maybe we should get awarded more.\xe2\x80\x9d"
b'The W.N.B.A. When compared with the N.B.A., athletes in the W.N.B.A. face extreme pay disparities \xe2\x80\x94 though, as is often pointed out, the N.B.A. is a multibillion dollar industry, while the W.N.B.A. is not. Nonetheless, in 2018, the W.N.B.A. set an individual salary cap of $117,500, and rookies earned a minimum of about $50,000. The minimum starting salary for N.B.A. players is about $580,000.'
b'Last summer, A\xe2\x80\x99ja Wilson, a star rookie who was the No. 1 overall W.N.B.A. draft pick in 2018, commented on LeBron James\xe2\x80\x99s $154 million contract with the Los Angeles Lakers. \xe2\x80\x9cMust be nice. We over here looking for an M but Lord, let me get back in my lane,\xe2\x80\x9d she tweeted. Wilson earned about $53,000 that season. The top N.B.A. draft pick last year, Deandre Ayton, is expected to earn $6.8 million in his first year.'
b'U.S.A. Hockey. In March 2017, the women\xe2\x80\x99s national hockey team announced that it would boycott the coming world championship if U.S.A. Hockey did not increase the women\xe2\x80\x99s wages. The risk paid off. Within days, the team and U.S.A. Hockey reached a four-year deal that gave the female players a $2,000 training stipend each month from the United States Olympic Committee and larger bonuses for winning medals. \xe2\x80\x9cWe want to do the fair thing, and the right thing \xe2\x80\x94 not just for hockey but for all women,\xe2\x80\x9d Meghan Duggan, the team\xe2\x80\x99s captain, said at the time.'

b'MIAMI GARDENS, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 In a short stretch of Saturday afternoon, the Miami Open lost two of its biggest attractions \xe2\x80\x94 and just held on to a third. Top-ranked Naomi Osaka lost her third-round match, 4-6, 7-6(4), 6-3 to 27th-seeded Hsieh Su-wei. Midway through Osaka\xe2\x80\x99s match, Serena Williams, an eight-time tournament champion, unexpectedly withdrew, citing a left knee injury.'
b'Osaka, who had emerged as the sport\xe2\x80\x99s best front-runner, had won 63 straight matches when winning the first set, dating to 2016. Hsieh, a crafty 33-year-old veteran, closed out the victory on her first match point, hitting an overhead smash that Osaka blocked back, and then finishing off the point with an unreturnable slice volley.'
b'Osaka had beaten Hsieh earlier this year in the third round of the Australian Open, 5-7, 6-4, 6-1. Hsieh has used her unorthodox game of jabs and feints to establish a reputation as a giant killer; she knocked then-No. 1 Simona Halep out of the third round of Wimbledon last year.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9dIt\xe2\x80\x99s always great to pick up a better level during the match,\xe2\x80\x9d Hsieh said in her on-court interview. \xe2\x80\x9cEvery time you\xe2\x80\x99ve made it and you beat a good player, you feel, \xe2\x80\x98Wow, this is everything. In the Australian Open quarterfinals in January, Williams was leading Karolina Pliskova, 5-1, in the third set when she twisted her ankle on match point. Though she had more match point opportunities, the injury particularly encumbered Williams\xe2\x80\x99s serve, causing her to lose all 10 subsequent points in her service games.'
b'After receiving a bye in the first round of the Miami Open, Williams survived an up-and-down second-round match against 63rd-ranked Rebecca Peterson on Friday afternoon.
