b'By Kurt Streeter'
b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 Early in his quarterfinal match at the Australian Open on Tuesday, Frances Tiafoe, part of a new generation of male stars who have emerged for the first time at a Grand Slam tournament, faced a break point against his battle-tested opponent.'
b'But Rafael Nadal, of course, is not just any opponent. He is the No. 2 seed, a champion in Melbourne in 2009, the owner of 17 Grand Slam titles and as punishing a player as ever at age 32.'
b'Nadal\xe2\x80\x99s return of serve came back powerfully, pushing the 21-year-old Tiafoe far to his backhand side for a meager reply. And with that, Nadal, as he did during the entire span of a vintage and coldly efficient victory, had put his opponent on an energy-sapping, confidence-draining string.'
b'The exchange ended, mercifully, with a booming Nadal down-the-line forehand, which the powerfully built Tiafoe sent meekly into the net.'
b'Two games into a much-anticipated fight, Tiafoe\xe2\x80\x99s serve had been broken, his fighting spirit dealt a severe blow.'
b'After winning that first break point, Nadal never looked back. Roughly 90 minutes later, the scoreboard flashed the result: 6-3, 6-4, 6-2.'
b'Earlier, another rising star had done what Tiafoe could not, beating his elder to reach the semifinals. Stefanos Tsitsipas, a 20-year-old from Greece, defeated the 30-year-old Spaniard, Roberto Bautista Agut, 7-5, 4-6, 6-4, 7-6 (2), several hours before Nadal and Tiafoe took the court.'
b'But with Nadal\xe2\x80\x99s win at Rod Laver Arena, a measure of order was restored by a member of the old guard.'
b'Buoyant on court after the match, Nadal told the crowd that he had recently joked that the tour\xe2\x80\x99s young challengers could wait awhile before challenging for tennis supremacy.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBut looks that they don\xe2\x80\x99t want to wait,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey are there, no?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In this tournament, Nadal has also beaten Alex de Minaur, the 19-year-old new hope of Australia. In the semifinals on Thursday, he will play Tsitsipas.'
b'Tsitsipas, seeded 14th and the first Greek player to make a serious dent in the pro game, is among the clutch of college-age players heralded by the ATP Tour as eventual successors to the four aging kings of the sport: Nadal, Novak Djokovic, Roger Federer and Andy Murray, who have won virtually every Grand Slam singles title since 2003.'
b'They will not be able to defy time forever. Case in point: Murray, the three-time major champion, a former No. 1 and a two-time Olympic gold medalist, announced at the start of this tournament that his days as a player may end at this year\xe2\x80\x99s Wimbledon, if not sooner.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt feels like a fairytale,\xe2\x80\x9d Tsitsipas said in a post-match interview.'
b'As he spoke, inside the stadium and out, rowdy fans, many from Melbourne\xe2\x80\x99s large Greek population, chanted songs and danced \xe2\x80\x94 as they have all tournament long.'
b'With his flowing locks and scythe-like, one-handed backhand, Tsitsipas had proved himself a legitimate threat to win here when he blunted Federer on center stage Sunday night.'
b'The upset \xe2\x80\x9cgot people\xe2\x80\x99s attention,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cMy biggest challenge was to stay concentrated, stay focused\xe2\x80\x9d in order to prove the win over Federer was no fluke.'
b'Tiafoe \xe2\x80\x94 known as \xe2\x80\x9cBig Foe,\xe2\x80\x9d and one of the few black players on tour \xe2\x80\x94 could not come close to duplicating Tsitsipas\xe2\x80\x99s effort. Before playing Nadal, the young American seemed to be playing with the form and confidence that would give him a chance for a monumental upset of his own. He had scored three straight surprising wins against higher-ranked players, including one over the No. 5 seed, Kevin Anderson. He had also gained an avid following with his vivacious on-court persona and post-match celebrations \xe2\x80\x94 taking off his shirt and pounding his chest, mimicking his favorite N.B.A. players.'
b'His hope against Nadal was that his young legs would push him past a champion who has won 80 tour titles in a career of nearly two decades.'
b'Add to that: Maybe, just maybe, Nadal would break down on the unforgiving hard court, a surface that has taken a toll on his body.'
b'After all, Nadal completed just one hard court event last year. At the Australian Open, he retired during the fifth set of his quarterfinal against Marin Cilic, because of an upper leg injury. At the United States Open in September, he retired again, this time because of a knee injury during a semifinal against Juan Mart\xc3\xadn del Potro.'
b'Nadal took the rest of the year off and had ankle surgery. Then, after he arrived in Australia, he withdrew from a warm-up event in Brisbane because of a left thigh injury.'
b'But at Melbourne Park this year, he looks refreshed. His movement is fluid. His ball striking has looked as crisp and powerful as ever.'
b'Tiafoe spoke to this, offering a view of what it\xe2\x80\x99s like from the distressed other side of the court.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI knew he was going to bring crazy intensity,\xe2\x80\x9d Tiafoe said. \xe2\x80\x9cI knew the ball was going to be jumping.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI knew if he got hold of a forehand, it was going to be barbecue chicken,\xe2\x80\x9d he continued, resorting to a culinary metaphor to describe how he felt after just a few points: cooked.'
b'Keenly aware of how small the margins between winning and losing are at this level, Nadal slightly altered his service motion during the off-season. He cut down on his backswing to gain more efficient power. He said after Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s match that he had also worked on finishing points earlier than usual, to reduce the wear on his body.'
b'There is still much tennis to be played in this tournament. Novak Djokovic, the firmly entrenched No. 1 player, remains on the other side of the draw. He and Nadal could meet in the final here for the second time, a rematch of 2012, when Djokovic won in a nearly six-hour marathon.'
b'But first things first, and for Nadal that means facing Tsitsipas, another chance for the old guard to keep a youthful challenger at bay.'

b'MELBOURNE, Australia \xe2\x80\x94 This is a story about Roger Federer\xe2\x80\x99s third-round match. Only it is not about Roger Federer.'

b'At Rod Laver Arena this Friday afternoon, the education of Taylor Fritz took a significant, though bruising, step forward. This was a graduate level course held in front of 15,000 fans, taught with calculating precision by a 37-year-old Swiss who has won 20 Grand Slam titles.'

b'After that match, though he was playing as confidently as he ever had, Fritz was cleareyed about his slim chances against an all-time great like Federer. b'This time, though aware of the long odds against him, Fritz vowed to play loose and relaxed. \xe2\x80\x9cHave fun,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cPlay my game, hit big.\xe2\x80\x9d He wanted to soak up the moment, and learn.'
b'At 1 p.m. on a muggy afternoon, Fritz finally took the court at Rod Laver Arena. He had never played there. He smiled tightly. He fidgeted with his brown hair and white headband. His mind raced.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere were a lot of thoughts going on in my head,\xe2\x80\x9d he would explain, noting that he had simultaneously tried to pump himself up and find calm by listening to rap on his headphones as he strode before the fans.'

When Federer\xe2\x80\x99s followed, crackling over the public address system, it was a condensed version of the Swiss star\xe2\x80\x99s achievements. Even shortened, it took a full minute.'
b'Now the match was on, and it was clear from the beginning that Federer considered Fritz dangerous. He had reason to. In that one and only meeting, in Stuttgart, Germany, in the summer of 2016, Federer had emerged victorious, 6-4, 5-7, 6-4. Hardly smooth sailing. b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s been a long time since I have gotten a beat-down like that,\xe2\x80\x9d Fritz told me, unspooling the entire experience once it was done. \xe2\x80\x9cIt didn\xe2\x80\x99t feel great, not at all.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The first set took 20 minutes. Federer: 6-1.'
b'In the second set, Fritz fared better. He began using the leverage from his 6-foot-4-inch frame. With Federer serving, Fritz nudged ahead in a key game. Federer responded with a pair of scorching forehand winners and a curveball ace.'

b'But the tighter shoes did not keep her in the match. Pliskova won the next two games, pulling to 4-5, suddenly back on serve. Williams earned three more match points in the 10th game, but Pliskova saved them all.'

b'Pliskova, a former No. 1, had knocked Williams out of a Grand Slam event before, beating her in straight sets in the 2016 United States Open semifinals. She had looked on track for a similarly efficient victory when she broke Williams for a 3-2 lead in the second set.'

b'Schnur stands at the baseline, waits for his opponent to get into the ready position, and then simply tosses the ball into the air and slams away. b'The circadian rhythm can be reset by changing sleep or eating patterns. But how can players adjust their internal clocks for optimal performance when they\xe2\x80\x99re playing at 2 a.m. one day and at 2 p.m. another?'

b'By Sarah Mervosh and Christina Caron'
b'On Friday, all 28 players on the United States women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer team filed a gender discrimination lawsuit against the United States Soccer Federation, an escalation in their increasingly public battle for equality.'
b'The players have said that they play more games than the men\xe2\x80\x99s team \xe2\x80\x94 and win more of them \xe2\x80\x94 yet still receive less pay. They said \xe2\x80\x9cinstitutionalized gender discrimination\xe2\x80\x9d affected not only their paychecks, but also where they played and how often, how they trained, the medical care and coaching they received, and even how they traveled to matches.'
b'They are not alone in their fight for fairer pay and better treatment. Here are eight times in recent memory when women fought for equality in sports.'
b'Experts claimed for years that distance running was damaging to women\xe2\x80\x99s health and femininity.'
b'In 1967, women weren\xe2\x80\x99t allowed to officially enter the Boston Marathon, so Kathrine Switzer entered that year as \xe2\x80\x9cK.V. Switzer\xe2\x80\x9d to hide her gender.'
b'Two miles in, an official tried to eject her from the course, a moment captured in dramatic photographs. She finished anyway, becoming the first woman to complete the race as an official entrant.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe learned that women are not deficient in endurance and stamina, and that running requires no fancy facilities or equipment,\xe2\x80\x9d Switzer wrote in The New York Times in 2007.'
b'Women were officially allowed to enter the race in 1972. Women\xe2\x80\x99s marathoning joined the Olympics in 1984.'
b'The year 1973 was a big one for Billie Jean King, the trailblazing tennis star.'
b'She founded the Women\xe2\x80\x99s Tennis Association. She led a movement for female players to earn equal prize money in tournaments that featured players of both sexes.'
b'And, on a September night at the Astrodome in Houston, she epitomized her crusade for gender equality when she handily beat Bobby Riggs, a self-described male chauvinist pig, in the Battle of the Sexes.'
b'King went on to receive the Presidential Medal of Freedom in 2009 for her work championing the rights of women and gay people. She is considered to be one of the most important athletes of the 20th century.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEveryone thinks women should be thrilled when we get crumbs,\xe2\x80\x9d King once said. \xe2\x80\x9cI want women to have the cake, the icing and the cherry on top, too.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Chris Ernst is a two-time Olympic rower. But in the spring of 1976, she was the captain of Yale University\xe2\x80\x99s women\xe2\x80\x99s crew team \xe2\x80\x94 and sick of not having proper showers to use after practice.'
b'She led 18 teammates in an eye-catching protest at Yale\xe2\x80\x99s athletic office. The athletes stripped to their waists, revealing the words \xe2\x80\x9cTitle IX,\xe2\x80\x9d which had been drawn in blue marker on each woman\xe2\x80\x99s back and breasts.'
b'The Times ran an article in the next day\xe2\x80\x99s paper, and a photograph of the history-making event also ran in The Yale Daily News.'
b'Within two weeks, the female rowers had new locker rooms. And, across the country, educators began viewing Title IX \xe2\x80\x94 which had been in effect for just four years \xe2\x80\x94 as a law that required compliance.'
b'In 2007, after pressure from the tennis great Venus Williams and others, Wimbledon announced that women\xe2\x80\x99s tennis players would receive prize money equal to the men\xe2\x80\x99s.'
b'Williams had made a failed plea to Wimbledon\xe2\x80\x99s governing body the night before she won the title in 2005. And in 2006, she wrote an op-ed essay in The Times of London titled \xe2\x80\x9cWimbledon Has Sent Me a Message: I\xe2\x80\x99m Only a Second Class Champion.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHave you ever been let down by someone that you had long admired, respected and looked up to?\xe2\x80\x9d she wrote. \xe2\x80\x9cLittle in life is more disappointing, particularly when that person does something that goes against the very heart of what you believe is right and fair.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After the policies changed in 2007, she was awarded $1.4 million for her fourth Wimbledon victory, the same amount as the men\xe2\x80\x99s champion, Roger Federer.'
b'In March 2017, the women\xe2\x80\x99s national hockey team announced that it would boycott the coming world championship if U.S.A. Hockey, the sport\xe2\x80\x99s national governing body, did not increase the women\xe2\x80\x99s wages.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s hard to believe that in 2017, we have to fight so hard just to get equitable support,\xe2\x80\x9d Meghan Duggan, the team\xe2\x80\x99s captain, said at the time. \xe2\x80\x9cWe want to do the fair thing, and the right thing \xe2\x80\x94 not just for hockey but for all women.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'They put their careers on the line, but the risk paid off.'
b'Less than two weeks later, the team reached a four-year deal with U.S.A. Hockey. It provided the female players a $2,000 training stipend each month from the United States Olympic Committee and larger bonuses for winning medals. The team also received the same travel and insurance provisions that the men\xe2\x80\x99s national team did, and a pool of prize money to be split each year.'
b'Four prominent female big-wave surfers, Bianca Valenti, Andrea Moller, Keala Kennelly and Paige Alms, spent years fighting for equal pay in the largely male sport where they regularly risk their lives.'
b'Last July, the Committee for Equity in Women\xe2\x80\x99s Surfing, an organization formed by six women, sent letters to the California Coastal Commission arguing that by treating women unequally, the World Surf League was in violation of state civil rights law.'
b'Months later, in September, Valenti and other female surfers earned a victory when the World Surf League announced it would offer equal prize money to men and women.'
b'Valenti, along with Sabrina Brennan, the president of the San Mateo County Harbor Commission, and Karen Tynan, a labor lawyer, also successfully pushed for women to be included in the Maverick\xe2\x80\x99s Challenge, a big-wave surfing competition that had traditionally invited only men.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSome people would tell me that by trying to get the (prize) pie redistributed I was ruining it for everyone,\xe2\x80\x9d Moller said in December. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I would just say: \xe2\x80\x98That\xe2\x80\x99s wrong. We\xe2\x80\x99re fighting for the industry. People love watching women surf big waves, so the whole sport will grow.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the world of professional basketball, pay disparities are well-documented: In the N.B.A., a multibillion-dollar industry where players often make millions, the minimum starting salary is about eight times what the average W.N.B.A. player makes.'
b'And female players are speaking up, on social media and on TV.'
b'Skylar Diggins-Smith, the W.N.B.A. All-Star who plays guard for the Dallas Wings, recently appeared in a commercial to raise awareness about pay inequity.'
b'The commercial, by the investment adviser Wealthsimple, contrasts the paths of two young players, a boy and a girl. Each lists their basketball dreams and accomplishments, but only one will grow up to receive a multimillion-dollar rookie contract.'
b'A\xe2\x80\x99ja Wilson, a star rookie who was the first overall W.N.B.A. draft pick in 2018, has also weighed in: \xe2\x80\x9cmust. be. nice,\xe2\x80\x9d she wrote about LeBron James\xe2\x80\x99s $154 million contract with the Los Angeles Lakers. \xe2\x80\x9cWe over here looking for a M but Lord, let me get back in my lane.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Wilson earned about $53,000 that season. The top N.B.A. draft pick last year, Deandre Ayton, was expected to earn about $6.8 million in his first year playing for the Phoenix Suns.'
b"Ada Hegerberg, a 23-year-old Norwegian, was recognized as the best female soccer player in the world last year when she became the first person to win the women\xe2\x80\x99s Ballon d'Or, a prestigious individual honor in soccer that had previously been reserved for men."
b'Despite the big award, she has decided not to play on the biggest stage of all, the Women\xe2\x80\x99s World Cup, in France this summer.'
b'Hegerberg quit the Norwegian national team in 2017 in protest of what she said was a lack of support for women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer in her home country.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was quite clear with them about what I thought needed to be better,\xe2\x80\x9d she said in an interview after winning the Ballon d\xe2\x80\x99Or. \xe2\x80\x9cI gave them the reasons. I wish my national team all the best. I love my country. I wish I could play for them. In this case, I had to move on.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Maya Salam and Mihir Zaveri contributed reporting.'

b'By Victor Mather'
b'Tiger Woods hadn\xe2\x80\x99t won a major in 11 years. He had struggled through injury and personal crises. He was dismissed as finished, his years of dominance fading into memory.'
b'Then on Sunday he won the Masters again, at age 43.'
b'When athletes begin to fade, it\xe2\x80\x99s usually all over. But a select few have returned in triumph, defying setbacks or Father Time.'
b'The comeback most people thought of when Woods won Sunday was the Masters victory by Jack Nicklaus at age 46 in 1986. Nicklaus had not won a major in six years and became the oldest player to win the Masters.'
b'Even more incredible was the return of Ben Hogan at the 1950 U.S. Open. His car had collided head-on with a Greyhound bus in Texas in 1949, and Hogan was nearly killed. After two months in the hospital, and a year recovering, he returned to golf and won the Open. He added five more major championships over the next three years.'
b'After three straight championships with the Chicago Bulls from 1991 to \xe2\x80\x9993, Michael Jordan decided to give baseball a try. A .200 batting average in the minor leagues made him a figure of ridicule for many fans and commentators, and the N.B.A. moved on.'
b'Then as abruptly as he retired, Jordan came back in 1995. In his first three full seasons, the Bulls won three more titles. Jordan retired again in 1999, generally considered the best player in basketball history. (A second comeback, with the Washington Wizards, was less successful.)'
b'After Muhammad Ali declined to serve in the military during the Vietnam War, he was stripped of his heavyweight title and was unable to box for three years.'
b'When he was able to get relicensed in 1970, he resumed a career that is regularly cited as the greatest. He regained his title in 1974 and battled through three immortal fights against Joe Frazier.'
b'George Foreman, from whom Ali recaptured the heavyweight title in 1974, hung up the gloves in 1977. But 10 years later, at 38, he decided to return to the ring. After a series of wins, he got a shot at the title at age 42, but lost to Evander Holyfield. He kept boxing, though, and got another improbable title shot in 1994 at 45 years old. Incredibly, he beat the champion, Michael Moorer, and won three more fights before losing in his final bout in 1997 at age 48.'
b'Roger Federer\xe2\x80\x99s win at the Australian Open in 2017, at age 35, was his first major title in five years and capped a comeback from back injuries and knee surgery. Beating Rafael Nadal in that final showed Federer could defeat the younger rivals who had flummoxed him during his drought. In 2018, he won the Australian Open again, for his 20th major title, and returned to No. 1.'
b'Jennifer Capriati was written off after her career as a teen star was derailed by personal problems. She quit the tour for two years and dropped out of the rankings. But she returned in 1996 a more mature player and won the Australian Open in 2001 at 24. She became world No. 1 and added two more Grand Slam titles.'
b'But the most inspiring tennis comeback undoubtedly belonged to Monica Seles, who was stabbed by a deranged fan on the court in 1993. She was 19, No. 1 and an eight-time major singles champion at the time. Seles struggled with her injuries and with understandable anxiety after the attack. Still, she returned to win the 1996 Australian Open and make three other Grand Slam finals.'
b'Quarterback Doug Williams helped lead the Tampa Bay Buccaneers to the 1979 N.F.C. championship game. But after a salary dispute in 1982, he left to join the fledgling U.S.F.L.'
b'When that league folded, Williams caught on as a backup to Jay Schroeder for the Washington Redskins in 1987. But Williams earned the starting job just before the playoffs and led the team to a Super Bowl title, the first black quarterback ever to do so.'
b'Aldiniti was a solid steeplechaser in Britain in the late 1970s before sustaining a bad leg injury. At about the same time, the jockey Bob Champion learned he had testicular cancer. Once both had recovered, they were paired for the 1981 Grand National and won it. Their triumph was turned into a 1984 movie, \xe2\x80\x9cChampions,\xe2\x80\x9d starring John Hurt.'
b'Honorable mention goes to Da Hoss. He won the 1996 Breeders\xe2\x80\x99 Cup Mile, then raced only once in two years. Yet in his return to the Mile in 1998, he won it again, causing the race announcer Tom Durkin to proclaim it \xe2\x80\x9cthe greatest comeback since Lazarus.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Greg LeMond became the first American to win the Tour de France in 1986 and seemed poised to reel off several more. But the next year he was accidentally shot while turkey hunting, hit by several dozen pellets, including some in his heart lining.'
b'He returned to the Tour in 1989 in poor form and was considering retirement. But he strengthened as the race went along and won it in one of the most famous finishes ever, beating his rival Laurent Fignon in a time trial on the Champs-\xc3\x89lys\xc3\xa9es. The final margin was the closest in history: eight seconds. LeMond went on to win another Tour the next year.'
b'Tommy John had a strong 12-year career as a pitcher for the Indians, White Sox and Dodgers. But in 1974 he sustained an injury to the ulnar collateral ligament of the elbow, which usually meant the end of pitchers\xe2\x80\x99 careers.'
b'John decided to try an untested, speculative surgery, now known as Tommy John surgery. In the procedure, now routine, a tendon from elsewhere in the patient is removed and replaces the damaged one in the elbow.'
b'John missed the 1975 season, but returned the next season at 33. He had three more All-Star appearances and three 20-game win seasons before finally retiring in 1989 at 46.'
b'An earlier version of this article referred incorrectly to Jack Nicklaus\xe2\x80\x99s win at the 1986 Masters at age 46. It made him the oldest man to win the Masters, not the oldest man to win a golf major. (Julius Boros was 48 when he won the 1968 P.G.A. Championship.)'
